Dai and Ma originally planned to go to [Shanghai] and go south by boat, but because the Sixth Plenary Session has been in session for several days and the date of the Fifth National Congress is also approaching, they specially changed to fly to Guangdong by a giant aircraft on the morning of the 4th. The hotel in Beijing has been prepared for Chen and Li. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 4th)

Current Commentary

Revision of Curriculum Standards for Primary and Secondary Schools 4

— Bing

Recently, the Ministry of Education convened experts for a discussion meeting on curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools. It has been three years since the promulgation of the curriculum standards for primary and secondary schools. Practitioners, based on their experience, and observers, based on their knowledge, have all felt the necessity to carefully consider revisions to achieve perfection. The Ministry of Education convened this meeting with the same motivation, integrating various opinions and following the best strategies. Their utmost concern for education is truly admirable. The outcome of this meeting should naturally not be overlooked.

It is noted that the agenda of this meeting included a proposal for detailed teaching outlines for each subject in primary and secondary schools. This is indeed crucial and fills a previous gap. In the past, the standards only contained broad outlines. Editors of textbooks relied on their own interpretations, which inevitably led to inconsistencies. Examining textbooks from various publishers, they all claim to be edited based on the curriculum standards, yet books on the same subject vary greatly in detail, emphasis, and selection of content. Practitioners either did not adopt textbooks or determined their own teaching outlines, similar to textbook editors, injecting their own discretion, which inevitably deviated somewhat from the broad outlines. As a result, the education received by primary and secondary school students varied in quality and quantity depending on the textbooks used and the teachers encountered. This led to disparities in levels of attainment, and significant differences in knowledge and skills. With the establishment of detailed teaching outlines for each subject in the future, editors and practitioners will have common guidelines to follow. This will ensure that the education received by primary and secondary school students, regardless of location or school, will be of uniform quality, and the problem of uneven levels of attainment and significant differences in knowledge and skills can be largely avoided. Although the appropriateness of the teaching outlines remains to be seen, the resolution to formulate detailed teaching outlines for each subject is undoubtedly a further step forward and deserves our praise.

Regarding high school mathematics, this meeting resolved to divide students into groups in the second year. Those inclined towards science will study more mathematics, while those inclined towards humanities will reduce mathematics hours and increase studies in subjects such as Chinese and foreign languages. The burden of high school mathematics on students has long been a common complaint, and the lack of outstanding achievements in mathematics has also been a widely observed fact. Since Ms. Chen Hengzhe published the article "Save the Middle School Students" in the Ta Kung Pao, the examples cited mostly concerned the heavy workload of mathematics affecting students' physical health. As a result, those concerned with education paid particular attention to the issue of the quality and quantity of mathematics courses. In our opinion, students' physical health depends on the entire educational system and cannot be solely attributed to the heavy workload of one or two subjects. Even considering that mathematics courses cause headaches and mental fatigue for students, imperfect teaching methods should be regarded as the most significant factor. It is not appropriate to hastily discuss the quality and quantity of the mathematics course itself. The current resolution does not disregard the importance of mathematics to the entire education system but merely increases or decreases the hours allocated to it, allowing students to develop according to their inclinations and within their capabilities. It also avoids the previous tendency to excessively separate the humanities and sciences into separate extremes. It can be confidently asserted that this will be endorsed by insightful individuals. However, after the division into groups, the improvement of teaching methods remains urgently needed. Otherwise, the effects of the division will be difficult to see, and criticism will continue to arise.

Another important resolution is to merge hygiene, nature, and society into a General Knowledge subject in lower and middle grades of primary school. The intention is to create a systematic approach, and we particularly appreciate that it deeply understands the principles of integrated teaching. When children first enter school, based on their inherent experiences, they only know individual things and events, and have no concept of separate subjects. They are presented with a timetable from the teacher and textbooks, with numerous subjects that are difficult to remember quickly. When they study each subject, individual things and events are divided into several parts. One part is encountered in subject A, and another part is encountered in subject B. It does not suit children’s established habits. This is known by education experts. Now, hygiene, nature, and society are merged into a General Knowledge subject. What was previously possible is now uniformly implemented. Only in the higher grades will subjects be separated to focus children’s learning concepts. Starting with integration adapts to children’s habits, followed by analysis to guide research. The intention is extremely good. However, we still have something to say. The goal of General Knowledge is to obtain practical experience. It is best to abandon textbooks and replace them with personal experience and on-site observation. In primary schools, hygiene has a book, nature has a book, and society also has a book. In teaching, it does not go beyond explaining sentences and writing notes. Although the subject names are different, the actual content is an appendage to the Chinese language. Even if there is practical benefit, the amount is limited. Publishing houses benefit from having textbooks, and teachers who are lazy and inexperienced also benefit from having textbooks. Are textbooks really necessary tools in teaching? This is something worth considering when revising curriculum standards.

For female primary and secondary school students, there is also a resolution to increase home economics education. If this is regarded as a work project, there is naturally no objection. Other resolutions seem to be secondary, and will not be discussed for now. Overall, the results of this meeting provide better revisions and supplements to the previous curriculum standards, which is gratifying.

Both Britain and the United States Express Sympathy for China's Currency Reform, Considering it a Good and Timely Plan for Self-Rescue 5

(Washington) Government officials today, while unwilling to offer any formal criticism of China's new currency policy to stabilize currency prices, expressed that they believe this plan is a timely measure that can strengthen the central government's financial position and stabilize China's currency, thus alleviating the exchange rate fluctuations that have recently plagued the banking and business communities. Currency experts here vaguely stated that this plan is an expanded form of currency control recently implemented by China, a good plan for self-rescue, and one that has long been recognized as necessary for China. Because international financial powers have been unable to decide on a method to alleviate China's currency difficulties, China has no choice but to strive for its own solutions. Government officials stated that the U.S. Treasury Department is not involved in this move, and that other governments are also not involved. However, well-informed sources in the private sector generally believe that Sir Otto Niemeyer, the chief economic advisor to the British government, may have been consulted by China in advance. It is believed here that the nationalization of silver is a very important undertaking, the success of which depends entirely on whether the Chinese government can manage it effectively. The detailed implementation rules have not yet been disclosed, so observers are unwilling to judge its effectiveness. However, it is generally felt that the unification of banknote issuance will greatly consolidate the power of the central government, and that the concentrated efforts of various banks to issue banknotes will strengthen their credit. It is believed here that the recent successful issuance of banknotes by the central government in the interior has encouraged China's new currency policy. As for the centralization of foreign exchange powers, it can stabilize the value of China's legal tender, which is desired by the government and the general business community. Experts here believe that the biggest problem with this plan lies in maintaining sufficient reserves. Currently, these reserves are higher than those of any other country in the world, and the Chinese government should be able to exercise its powers prudently to maintain the existing exchange rate. (National Telegram, 3rd)

(London) The Times commented on China's currency reform, stating that this plan is welcomed by the general public, and if faithfully implemented, it can serve as the basis for reorganizing China's finances and placing them on a permanently sound footing. The Daily Mail stated that the Chinese government's announcement was welcomed by people in London. This plan was formulated along the lines of the most constructive new laws, and there is little doubt that it will meet the needs of those remitting funds to China. This move should bring inestimable benefits to the Chinese people and facilitate commerce, thereby enhancing the prosperity of the Chinese people. The Financial News stated that well-informed sources in London generally believe that China's announcement to stabilize currency values ​​almost means that the authorities intend to stabilize China's currency at a price aligned with the British pound. Whether the Chinese government can force its people to hand over privately held silver is still uncertain. Its ability to collect silver from the public will largely determine whether it can maintain exchange rates at the current price. This reform has a good chance of success, and U.S. silver policy may be revised. The Manchester Guardian reported that the Chinese government's abolition of silver is viewed in London as an emergency measure. Many believe that this move will ultimately be beneficial, and the first impression of currency and banking reform is extremely satisfactory. (Reuters, 4th)

(London) British newspapers today published the Chinese government's currency reform measures in large print. The Financial Times stated that the Chinese government's move is in line with the best Western systems in all respects and is a good decision. It also stated that the success of this plan depends on the integrity and consistency of those who implement it, but there is no doubt that China can find people to manage this plan to gain trust and usher in a new era of financial stability for China. The newspaper concluded by saying that Britain and other countries will definitely provide the most sincere support and cooperation. The Daily Telegraph stated that this resolute and far-reaching plan for financial reform will definitely be endorsed by the business communities of all countries trading with China, and will open up great prospects for Chinese commerce. The Morning Post stated that the Chinese government has effectively announced China's departure from silver. This decision is swift and decisive, and should be done when the situation is critical. Its intention is probably to keep the Chinese currency from breaking away from its existing relationship with the British pound, but what kind of reserves and funds will the paper money be based on, and what kind of reaction will the Chinese people have? These are difficult questions to fathom. Britain will watch this great experiment with sympathy and hope for its success. (Reuters, 4th)

The Sixth Plenary Session Held a Memorial Week Yesterday 6

Cai Yuanpei Reports on Chinese Scientific Research

(Nanjing) The Sixth Plenary Session held Premier Sun Yat-sen’s memorial week in the auditorium at 8 a.m. on the 4th. Over a hundred Central Committee members attended, standing in order of age. Chairman Yu Youren was at the front, with committee members Lin Jiangbai and Ju Zheng in the first row, divided into five rows. All staff members were behind, also standing in two groups, in an orderly fashion. Under the leadership of Chairman Yu, tributes were paid. Cai Yuanpei reported on the Central Research Institute and the general situation of scientific research in China. The main points were as follows: Major research institutions in the country are divided into two categories. 1. Government-funded institutions: A. The Central Research Institute, divided into administrative, research, and evaluation departments. B. The Peiping Research Institute, also with administrative and research departments. C. The Geological Survey. D. The Central Agricultural Experiment Station. E. The Economic Commission, with livestock, tea, cotton production, silk improvement centers, and cotton textile dyeing halls and hygiene experiment stations. 2. Private organizations and groups: the Science Society of China, the Ching Sheng Biological Research Institute, the Yellow River Chemical Industry Institute, the Chinese Xilang Academy of Sciences, and the Lester Institute for Medical Research. 3. University research institutes: Tsinghua, Peking, Zhongshan, Central, Wuhan, Nankai, and Yenching Universities, and Beiyang Engineering College, covering seven disciplines: literature, science, law, agriculture, commerce, education. The general outline of cooperation between this institute and other institutions is as follows: The duties of this institute are roughly divided into three categories: 1. Regular or permanent research; 2. Using scientific methods to study domestic raw materials and production; 3. Pure scientific research and cultural-related history, language, anthropology, and archaeology. Based on these duties, the institute has completed a cooperation and mutual assistance program to promote scientific research, in order to fulfill our mission of actively contacting other institutions while passively avoiding academic leadership. Concrete facts about liaison and cooperation include: 1. Establishing a council as the hub of academic cooperation in China; 2. Establishing the Chinese branch of the Pacific Science Association to complete cooperation in oceanographic research; 3. Completing cooperation in meteorological research; 4. Establishing biological cooperation; 5. Numerous other cooperation matters. However, upon careful observation, the scientific research undertaking, from its initial advocacy to the present, has only been around for a few decades. There have already been such achievements, and it has begun to be recognized by others in the international academic community. The Central Research Institute is the highest academic research institution in the country and dares not fail to inherit Premier Sun Yat-sen's legacy to catch up, learning from the strengths of Europe and the United States. 1. To enrich itself, 2. To welcome cooperation from others, both of which will hopefully achieve the initial intentions of Premier Sun Yat-sen in planning to establish the Central Academy of Sciences. The meeting adjourned after Cai's speech. (Central News Agency, 4th)

Premier Wang's Temperature Normal 14

Nuer Arrives in Nanjing to Treat Wang, Cheekbone Stitches Removed Yesterday, Various Senior Officials Enter Ward for Discussions

(Nanjing) Premier Wang fell asleep at 10 PM on the 3rd and woke up at 6 AM on the 4th. He consumed liquid foods such as chicken broth. Around 7 AM, Chairman Chiang, Wu Jingheng, Zhang Renjie, Li Yuying, and others visited. Wang personally received them and then browsed the newspapers. His spirits seemed good. According to those around Wang, based on the current situation, Wang's injuries are expected to fully recover in a short period. (4th Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Central Hospital officially released a report on Premier Wang's condition at 9 AM on the 4th, stating that Premier Wang's condition and overall state are showing good progress. The stitches on his cheekbone were removed in the morning of the 4th. His temperature on the 4th was 37 degrees Celsius, pulse 82, and respiration 18. (4th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Dr. Nuer Arrives in Nanjing for Examination

(Nanjing) Dr. Nuer arrived in Nanjing at 5:18 PM on the 4th via a Eurasia plane from Baotou. Chu Minyi greeted him at the airport and accompanied him to the Central Hospital to examine Wang's injuries. Wang's condition has been progressing well. The cheek stitches were removed on the 4th. (4th Dispatch)

Senior Officials Enter the Ward for Discussions

(Nanjing) Premier Wang's condition is improving daily on the 4th. According to Chu Minyi, he is expected to fully recover in a few weeks. Around 7 AM on the 4th, Chairman Chiang arrived at the hospital first to visit. He was very pleased to see Wang's condition improving. He spoke briefly with Wang and then departed. At 7:30 AM, Wu Zhihui, Li Shizeng, and Zhang Jingjiang, three elder statesmen, arrived at the hospital to offer their condolences and spoke with Wang for half an hour. Wang was in good spirits and did not appear tired. Afterwards, Chairman Lin, Sun Ke, Ye Chucang, and heads of various ministries and commissions who had not personally entered the ward in the past three or four days all entered the room for discussions. Wang also requested to read newspapers, browsing important domestic and international news, and frequently asked those around him about the details of the plenary session, indicating his generally good spirits. Two renowned doctors, Miller and Niu Huilin, arrived in Nanjing on the 2nd. Their examination confirmed that Wang's injuries would not be an impediment and they fully agreed with the diagnosis methods and opinions of Liu Ruiheng, Shen Kefei, and Bai Liangzhi. Therefore, they returned to Shanghai on the night of the 3rd. Currently, the cheekbone stitches have been removed, and the swelling is gradually subsiding, expected to be resolved in two or three days. Whether the bullet in the back ribs is removed or not is irrelevant. Today, in addition to regularly consuming chicken broth, orange juice, and milk, Wang also consumed spinach and sago porridge, and his appetite has increased. Dr. Nuer, who came specifically to examine Wang, arrived in Nanjing at 5:20 PM on the 4th from Baotou on a special plane. The Executive Yuan sent personnel to greet him at the hospital. Around 6 PM, he conducted a detailed examination. It is understood that Wang's pre-existing diabetes did not recur as a result of the attack. The hospital announced that Wang's temperature on the 4th morning and afternoon was 37 degrees Celsius, pulse 80, and respiration 18. (4th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(4th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Madame Wang's Remarks at the Time of the Assassination

(Nanjing) This reporter recently met with Zeng Zhongwu, who showed a Reuters report on the Central Party Headquarters attack on the 1st, stating that Madame Wang said at the time that Mr. Wang would not die. If he were destined to die, he would have died 27 years ago when he assassinated Prince Regent. Zeng shook his head and smiled upon seeing this, saying that the report was quite different from the facts. The reporter then asked Zeng about the true situation, as he was present at the scene at the time. Zeng said that after Mr. Wang was shot, Madame Wang heard the alarm from upstairs at the Central Party Headquarters and rushed down. At that time, Mr. Wang was lying on the ground covered in blood, but his expression was very calm, and his voice was clear. Seeing Madame Wang leaning over him, he used his hand to support his wounded head and said to Madame Wang, "I have been shot five times and will probably die. This is the result for a revolutionary. I have no regrets." He also said, "I have been a comrade and shared hardships with you for more than 30 years, and I have no regrets. I have no will." Madame Wang replied, "Yes, yes, everyone must die. We are revolutionaries, so even if we are unfortunate, I will continue to work hard. I will take full responsibility for raising our children. You can rest assured. But you are seriously injured now and should not talk too much. You should be rushed to the hospital for treatment. If you don't die, we can still work hard. Even if we die, that's all it is for us revolutionaries." At that time, Chairman Chiang was also supporting Wang's head with one hand, facing Madame Wang. Zhang Xueliang, Chu Minyi, Chen Gongbo, and others were also taking care of him. Madame Wang also said to Chen Gongbo, "This is not the time to cry. You should immediately call the doctor and notify our sons-in-law, but don't tell my mother yet." Then, Chairman Chiang, Madame Wang, and us sent Mr. Wang to the Central Hospital. Madame Wang had no other remarks except to constantly tell people not to panic and to call the doctor quickly. The above is what happened that day. The Reuters report of Madame Wang's remarks is not only inconsistent with the facts, but also quite ridiculous. (4th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Chen Liang should be relieved of his current post. This is the order. It also ordered the appointment of Xiong Zhongtao as Deputy Director of the Quartermaster Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs. This is the order.

A Glimpse of U.S. Army Chief Dunn's Visit to Guangzhou 31

Paying Visits to Military and Political Authorities to Foster Sino-U.S. Friendship, Departing Guangzhou to Attend the Philippine Independence Day Celebration

Guangzhou Communication: The Republic of the Philippines is officially established on November 15. The United States has a special relationship and hopes for the establishment of a nation by its fostered territory. Therefore, hundreds of people from the United States, both from the government and the public, will cross the ocean to the Philippines to attend the celebration. Important figures in the political world, such as the Vice President of the United States and the U.S. Army Chief Dunn, also took ships to the Philippines one after another. The U.S. Navy ship Dunn was on, arrived in Hong Kong on the morning of October 29. The American warships stationed in Hong Kong fired a 19-gun salute to pay tribute. Dunn landed and formally paid a visit to the Governor of Hong Kong. After entertaining in Hong Kong for a day, he also responded to the invitation of the Guangdong Provincial authorities to visit Guangzhou. The US Navy sent a shallow draft warship for Dunn to ride in, arriving in Zhujiang Baimaotan on the morning of the 30th, landed on the Shamian Concession, first went to the US Consulate in Guangzhou for a brief rest, and then took a car with霍琪士 to visit the Guangdong military and political authorities. Chen Jitang, Lin Yunkai, Li Zongren, Zou Lu, Xiao Focheng, Liu Jiwen, and others from the Guangdong military and political circles welcomed them at the Yingbin Pavilion on Zhonghua North Road, and arranged a large team of guards in full gear in front of the pavilion to await inspection. Upon Dunn's arrival, they raised their guns to pay tribute. Amidst the melodious military music, Secretary Dunn inspected the warriors for a week before entering the flower hall of the Yingbin Pavilion, shaking hands with Chen, Li, Lin, Liu, Xiao, Zou, and others. A brief conversation was had. Around 11 o'clock, Secretary Dunn resigned and departed, attending a luncheon at the American Consulate in Shamian. After the meal, he visited the famous attractions of Guangzhou, including Hualin Temple, Liurong Temple, Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, Sun Yat-sen Memorial Monument, Huanghuagang Seventy-Two Martyrs' Cemetery, and the new campus of Sun Yat-sen University in Shipai. At 4 pm, he went to the Dongshan Aviation Society to attend a tea party of the various committees of the Southwest Political Council. All political commissars and military and political officials were present. After the meeting, he returned to Shamian to attend a welcome party for American expatriates. At 8 pm, Chen Jitang and Lin Yunkai hosted a banquet for Dunn at the joint office of the municipal government, accompanied by military and political officials from the province. After Chen's speech, Lin Yunkai gave a welcome speech as follows: "Secretary Dunn, ladies and gentlemen, we are deeply honored to have the presence of the US Army Secretary and his wife in Guangzhou today. The provincial government has specially joined forces with Commander-in-Chief Chen to host a banquet to express our welcome. China's foreign policy has always been based on friendship. We inherit the teachings of our ancestors and have always advocated being kind and good neighbors. This policy remains unchanged to this day and is in line with President Roosevelt's so-called Good Neighbor Policy of respecting oneself and respecting others. Premier Sun also instructed us with the principles of faith, justice, and peace. However, the realization of peace must be based on the establishment of true international friendship. Therefore, we are deeply impressed by President Roosevelt's words in his official speeches that "international friendship is no different from private friendship and must do its best to unite the power of mankind to create an atmosphere of mutual understanding and cooperation. " China and the United States started trading in Guangzhou the earliest, and most of the Chinese residing in the United States are from Guangdong. This time, the Secretary's willingness to come has greatly increased the friendship between the people of the two countries, which is truly a valuable record in history, etc." At about 8 o'clock, they dispersed in joy. Dunn took the original ship to Hong Kong that night and rushed to the Philippines from Hong Kong on the 31st. (October 31)

Jiujiang's Commercial Decline, More Than Thirty Businesses Closed 32

Nanchang Communication: Jiujiang is an important commercial port on the Yangtze River and the gateway to Jiangxi Province. The prosperity or decline of its commerce reflects the import and export trade of Jiangxi Province. The province has been plagued by bandits for eight years, and the production of major specialties such as rice, tea, bamboo, wood, porcelain, ramie cloth, sesame, peanut oil, and paper has plummeted. At the same time, due to the domestic and international recession and the Yangtze River flood, all industries are in decline, showing a downward trend. The following briefly describes the situation of various industries:

(1) Finance: The financial hub of various industries. In 1931, there were still 25 Jiujiang pawnshops. Later, due to sluggish business, many closed down. Currently, only Youcheng, Sanhe, Yuanxing, Shengchanghe, and Deyu remain. Among them, two are for exchanging small amounts of cash, and only three are lending. (2) Cotton Fabric Industry: The only textile factory in the province, Jiuxing Yarn Factory, has been heavily indebted in recent years due to the dumping of foreign yarn and the impact of the domestic recession, almost to the point of stagnation. The cotton fabric industry, which relies on rural areas, is in a precarious state due to rural bankruptcy. Only five operators can barely survive. (3) Porcelain: Export-oriented, with a large domestic and international market. When Chairman Chiang was stationed in Nanchang, the number of porcelain shops increased by one-third due to the military training held in Lushan. Before April and May of this year, each firm competed to purchase raw materials and produce fine art porcelain. Later, due to the transfer of troops and the cessation of training, no one was interested, and all capital was stagnant, causing great distress. (4) Ramie Cloth: This year's floods were devastating, affecting both the north and the south, and business is far from last year's. (5) Kerosene: The dumping of kerosene from the UK, the US, and Russia in China has a history of several years. Recently, due to the decline in purchasing power, bandit areas, and controlled sales, business is far from what it used to be. (6) Transshipment: Jiujiang is the gateway to the entire province, and the customs declaration and transshipment industry was extremely developed in the past. Now, with no exports of the five major specialties and declining imports due to low purchasing power, the number of businesses closed has reached more than 30 from 1931 to this year. This is just for the major ones, and all other businesses are also declining. (October 31)

Shen Honglie Discusses His Inspection of the Northwest 33

--The Northwest Has Vast Land and Resources Worth Developing--

Qingdao Communication: Qingdao Mayor Shen Honglie went to the northwestern provinces to inspect agriculture, industry, commerce, and ancient culture. Shen gave a speech at the Qingdao Rotary Club yesterday on his inspection and the current situation in the Northwest, and expressed his views on developing the resources of the Northwest. The following is a record of the speech for the reference of those who are concerned about the people's conditions in the Northwest. Shen said: "This time I went to the Northwest to inspect agriculture, industry, commerce, and new and old cultures. I departed by Jiaoji train on the evening of September 14, stayed briefly in Jinan, Tianjin, Beiping, and other places, and then took the Pinghan Railway to Shijiazhuang. I transferred to the Zhengtai Railway to Taiyuan. Then, I took the Jinbei highway from Taiyuan and reached Datong in one day. From Datong, I took the Pingsui Railway to Suiyuan, passing through Yin County to Baotou, the end of the Pingsui Railway. From there, continuing westward, although there are highways and camel teams or various Yellow River routes available, they are all exceptionally slow. Fortunately, Eurasia Airlines has regular flights between Ningxia, Lanzhou, and Xi'an, so I took a plane from Baotou to Ningxia, then from Ningxia to Lanzhou to Xi'an. The route I took was more than 4,000 li, and the total time spent flying was only seven hours, showing the progress of transportation."

Italian Army Advances on the Northern Front, Major Battle Imminent 34

Outpost 35 Miles from Magal, Only Minor Contact Along the Way

Italian Army Front Line on the Northern Front: The Italian army has occupied all of its offensive objectives tonight. It occupied the important caravan transit town of Haoxing at noon without encountering any resistance from the Ethiopian army. The town is 50 kilometers from Magal, which is the target for the first day of the offensive. (3rd National News Agency Dispatch)

Asmara: The Italian army occupied the town of Haoxing early this morning. The Ascari scouts under General Biroli have occupied the highlands southwest of Magal, and the Blackshirts under General Santini are also advancing on Magal from the southeast. (4th Reuters Dispatch)

Asmara: Yesterday at dawn, the Italian army began its offensive along the northern front, with Magal as its main objective. A major battle is expected in the coming days. Italian planes flew out for reconnaissance today and discovered a small group of Ethiopian soldiers advancing from Haoxing towards Magal, and another group of about 10,000 people advancing from the south. The division of indigenous troops led by General Biroli is attacking on the right and has reached Haoxing, 35 miles northwest of Magal, a few miles outside the town. Its scouts have entered the town today. At the same time, the main force of General Santini's First Corps is attacking on the left and has reached Taibai Laixing. Italian engineers are working hard to repair the roads, so that trucks can transport food directly to the front line. The Italian soldiers at the outposts are strictly disciplined and take various precautions to prevent attacks. (4th Reuters Dispatch)

Asmara: At dawn today, the Italian army launched a major offensive along the entire northern front, with Magal, 65 miles southeast of Aduwa, as its main objective. A total of 100,000 troops are participating in the battle, led by General Santini's troops, who will engage with the forces commanded by Ethiopian generals Gasa and Seyum. The two generals have so far not prevented the Italian army from building roads outside General Santini's front line. The Italian army is using Ascari scouts as the vanguard, followed by small tanks and infantry. Prior to the offensive, the Italian army had transported 10,000 tons of ammunition, loaded on 3,500 trucks. (3rd Reuters Dispatch)

Italian Army Front Line on the Northern Front: Today, it was learned from the headquarters here that the attacking force consists of 125,000 soldiers and tens of thousands of indigenous troops. Apart from minor skirmishes, there was no resistance from armed Ethiopian troops. The Italian army only encountered natural obstacles in the terrain. All troops are passing through deep forests and steep rocks. The Blackshirt troops of the central column led by General Loli have reached Haoxin tonight, marching 14 miles without firing a shot. General Santini's right wing encountered only scattered resistance from Ethiopian soldiers. General Malavigne's left wing, leading camel and mule teams, opened into the Danakil Desert with the help of the surrendered chieftain Geksa and his 1,500 guards as guides. All Italian aircraft are soaring in the air to find the Ethiopian army's concentration. Prime Minister Mussolini's son-in-law, Count Ciano, and Mussolini's two sons are personally flying planes to participate in the war. Countless tanks are covering the infantry and going straight into enemy territory, followed by 5-inch caliber cannons. Magal can be occupied on Thursday, so that the Italian army on the front line can celebrate the recapture of a major town on Italy's war memorial day. Pilots reported that there were only a few Ethiopian machine gun and artillery teams on the flanks of the Italian army along the way to Magal. The Associated Press war correspondent said today that this offensive will probably take four or five days, after which it will stop to consolidate the front line, just as it did after the fall of Aduwa. (3rd National News Agency Dispatch)

Italian Troops Advance on Four Fronts 35

Northern Front: Italian troops advanced today in four columns. The extreme left flank was composed of Ascari troops, advancing south along the edge of the plateau. The second column, led by General Bitru's Malavina troops, covered the right flank of the two main columns. The main force, led by General Biroli, was also composed of Ascari troops. General Santini led the extreme right flank, advancing 30 kilometers. (November 4th National Telegram)

(Rome) Italy has sent a total of 280,000 troops to East Africa. Among them, 110,000 are deployed on the Tigray front in Abyssinia. On the southern Somaliland front, there are only two and a half Italian divisions. It is said that reinforcements will be sent soon. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Northern Front: After several hours of advancement, the Italian troops on the northern front have achieved their initial objectives. Italian and Eritrean troops have reached Embercon and Emba Mashel. At 10:30 AM, Blackshirt troops reached Ho-shan. According to Italian air reconnaissance, large Abyssinian forces are concentrated in Taishi, with 3,000 men detached to form a column and sent to Magale to resist the Italian advance. The column in the Tang Kaili area has not yet moved. When the "October 28th Division" of Blackshirts departed for the front from Mulih, they first lined up and saluted the statue of Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, singing revolutionary songs. Some speculate that the Italian and Eritrean troops departing from An-di-si-ao did not follow the road from Ho-shan to Agu-la to join General Santini's forces in attacking Magale, but instead followed the Feijia River road from Ho-shan to Ma-san-bo-er to attack Magale. Although this road is not on the map, it is passable. Furthermore, two columns of Italian troops from the An-di-si-ao front are advancing on Magale from different directions, one starting from Fa-la-si and the other from Sa-sai-er-la-jia-mi. These two columns are composed of local soldiers and Blackshirts. (November 3rd Havas News Agency Dispatch)

Asmara: Shortly after the Italian offensive began, the main force of Ascari troops under General Biroli occupied the controlled area of Anda Abamas, surrounded by fertile and watery valleys. Many women came out to welcome them, bringing out their hidden cattle and sheep, which the Italian soldiers bought in large numbers. Meanwhile, the Blackshirt troops under General Santini will enter Ho-shan tomorrow. The current Italian front extends from the Taibela Hing Temple on "English Street" to the Amba Hing Temple on the A-di-ge-la Ho-shan road. As the Italian troops advanced, the temple rang its stone bell to welcome them. Monks from the temple sent a delegation with fresh meat, chicken, and eggs to offer to the Italian troops, expressing their submission. (November 3rd Reuters Dispatch)

League of Nations Sanctions Progress 36

(Geneva) The Economic Committee of the League of Nations sanctions committee today passed in principle a ban on the supply of oil, coal, and steel to Italy. If the Committee of Eighteen also passes this resolution on Wednesday, the League of Nations will invite the United States and Germany to unanimously support it. (November 4th National Telegram)

(Geneva) The Economic Sanctions Committee, appointed by the Committee of Eighteen, met this morning. After an address by the chairman, Portuguese representative Vasconcelos, they immediately began discussing the issue of compensation agreements and the consequences for various countries resulting from the implementation of sanctions. They also passed a proposal by the Canadian representative to ban the export of petroleum, petroleum products, coal, iron, and steel to Italy. Regarding purchase contracts between various countries and Italy where a portion of the payment has already been made, the committee decided to appoint a subcommittee to discuss the conditions under which the import of Italian goods would be permitted under these contracts. Countries with such contracts should notify the League of Nations with the details of the contracts for study. The Economic Sanctions Committee then decided to continue its meeting tomorrow to discuss the issue of exports to countries not participating in sanctions. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Britain and Italy Closer Than Before 37

(London) It is believed in British circles that the Italian government may stop its anti-British propaganda in Italian newspapers by the end of this week and further reduce its troops stationed in Libya by at least one division. These are the conditions for Britain to reduce its naval strength in the Mediterranean. If Italy implements the above two measures, Britain will also reduce its warships in the Mediterranean. This is the result of recent talks in Geneva between British Foreign Secretary Hoare and Italian Chief Delegate Aloisi. Furthermore, as the atmosphere between Britain and Italy is now clearly more relaxed than before, Aloisi expressed a strong desire to improve British-Italian relations during the talks and made certain suggestions in his personal capacity, but implementation will require Mussolini's permission. (November 4th Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Foreign Secretary Hoare and cabinet member Eden arrived in London today from Geneva. Hoare traveled by plane, while Eden traveled by train. The Foreign Secretary told Reuters reporters that his talks in Geneva were very effective and he was very satisfied with the results of the trip. (November 3rd Reuters Dispatch)

(London) Two Italian naval experts will arrive here tomorrow evening to conduct preliminary talks with the British side before the London Naval Conference. According to information obtained by our correspondent, the Italian government has not yet decided whether to participate in the London Naval Conference. The arrival of the Italian naval experts is to study whether Italy can participate in this conference. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

(London) It is rumored that the British government intends to reform the League of Nations. According to official sources, the current government does not intend to reform the League of Nations to maintain its power after the general election, nor will it change British foreign policy. Furthermore, after the talks between British Foreign Secretary Hoare and Italian representative Aloisi in Geneva, the diplomatic situation has not changed. Hoare and Aloisi did not propose a ceasefire between Italy and Abyssinia to facilitate peace negotiations. It is also said that the results of the British-Italian talks have not encouraged the British government to withdraw any warships stationed in the Mediterranean. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

(Rome) Official sources stated today that the next three weeks may be the most important period after the intensification of the Abyssinian problem. Whether the war will spread to Europe will be decided at this time. Italy is prepared for any eventuality. Prime Minister Mussolini is now implementing his three-step plan: (1) Invade Abyssinia, (2) Attempt to avoid a European war, (3) Encourage the people to endure the various sacrifices of economic sanctions and seek alternative goods to those previously supplied by League of Nations member states. Diplomatic circles here believe today that if Britain can avoid further angering the Italians, there will be no possibility of war in Europe. However, any naval or military action to prevent Italy from conquering Abyssinia is likely to ignite the European powder keg. Mussolini met twice with Undersecretary of State Suvich today, while another 10,000 troops boarded ships for Africa. (November 3rd National Telegram)

Djibouti: Britain is preparing for war at the eastern entrance of the Red Sea. A sudden emergency alerted this normally quiet military port, which is now concentrated with 17 British warships, including three large cruisers from India and China. The Associated Press correspondent learned that there are currently 120 military aircraft at the Djibouti airfield, as well as a fleet of airships parked on the sea. The British Navy's fuel reserves are also being greatly expanded, and more anti-aircraft guns have been added. (November 3rd National Telegram)

Lyon: Édouard Herriot, leader of the Radical Socialist Party and minister without portfolio, gave a speech at the "Friends of the Soviet Union Association," saying, "War is now lurking beside us, and a little carelessness will lead to irreversible consequences. Fortunately, the League of Nations can guide us on the path to peace, and within the League of Nations, there is a great nation cooperating for peace, which is a fortunate thing in this unfortunate situation. I hope that France and Russia will continue to support each other, as they have for a long time. The Soviet people and their leaders are all friends of mine. What we want, in a nutshell, is to unite all the nations of the world to maintain peace. We may have reservations about certain people in certain countries and their political methods, but we should not blame their people for this. We will not allow anyone to use the power of the French Republic to oppress peace." (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Greek Plebiscite: Monarchists Triumph 38

Yes Votes Account for 90 Percent. The King Will Return and Be Restored This Month

Athens: General Kondylis, upon hearing the initial reports of the national vote indicating a major victory for the monarchists, declared that George II would be King of Greece from Sunday. The Interior Ministry also announced that according to reports from various regions, supporters of constitutional monarchy accounted for nearly 90 percent, with approximately 80 percent of the electorate voting. (November 3rd National Telegram)

(London) Former King George II of Greece told his friends today that he is scheduled to return to the country and ascend the throne on November 16th. (November 3rd National Telegram)

Athens: The Greek plebiscite was completed yesterday. The final results are as follows: 1,527,712 people participated in the vote, of which 1,491,992 voted in favor of the monarchy, 32,454 voted in favor of the republic, and 3,268 ballots were invalid. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Athens: Greece held a plebiscite today. According to the initial results, a majority of voters support the restoration of the monarchy. Approximately four million people voted today. All those over 20 years of age received two colored papers, one green (for the monarchy) and one red (for the democracy). Those who did not vote would be punished. (November 3rd Reuters Dispatch)

Athens: Yesterday, a national plebiscite was held to resolve the issue of the form of government. According to the Greek news agency, 95 percent of the electorate voted in favor of restoration, but the final results have not yet been announced. The people are delighted with the outcome of the vote, and celebrations are being held throughout the country. According to news from London, the deposed King George plans to return to the country and be restored to the throne in two weeks, and his associates expressed their pleasure at the national vote supporting the monarchy. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Athens: According to the Athens news agency, in the provinces of Darras, Macedonia, Epirus, and the islands of Western Cyclades, the majority voted in favor of restoration. In the initial results from Crete, 7,553 voted in favor of restoration, while fewer than 100 voted in favor of the republic. Regent General Kondylis has telegraphed King George to report the victory of the vote and the jubilation of the people. (November 4th Havas News Agency Dispatch)

Regent's Address to the People

Athens: According to the Athens news agency, Regent General Kondylis issued an address to the people, stating: "We do not yet know how the political situation will be resolved after the King's return, but we can be certain that His Majesty George II will return and be restored as the monarch of all of Greece. His Majesty has no fixed political views, nor does he have any room for political parties. He has only the Greek people in his heart, and what he never forgets is to give them absolute equality and fair treatment. From now on, political parties will no longer exist. The people will unite as one, so that Greece can open a new era. We are extremely pleased about this." (November 4th Havas News Agency Dispatch)

Italy Also Demands Quantitative Equality. The Future of the Conference is Uncertain

(London) Regarding Japan's demand for quantitative equality at the upcoming naval conference, it is said that Italy has agreed. Naval circles believe that regarding the issue of total tonnage, the opinions of Britain and the United States are already at odds with Japan's. Red Army Has Ample Strength: British Officer Describes Impressions of Traveling in Russia 41

(London) A military magazine published a lengthy article by General Waters, who was an aide-de-camp in Berlin and Petrograd before the Great War. He recently described his impressions of traveling in Russia as follows: "In terms of combat power, I feel that the Red Army is on par with the strongest armies in Europe." Waters went on to describe the situation in the Far East, saying, "The Soviet Union is also invincible in this region. The existence of first-class troops and large bombers, and the relative independence of the Far Eastern Army from the European part of the Soviet Union, forces the Japanese warlords to be cautious. If the Soviet Union does not pay attention to strengthening its defenses, there may be more than one country in Europe willing to attack the Soviet Union." (November 4th TASS Dispatch)

New French Political Party Appears 43

Named Republican Socialist Union. Former Prime Minister Paul-Boncour Elected President

(Paris) The New Socialist Party, the French Socialist Party, and the Socialist Republican Party have cooperated to form a new party called the "Republican Socialist Union," with incumbent Senator and former Prime Minister Paul-Boncour as its president. The main platform of the new party is as follows: (1) To protect the republican system and oppose fascism; (2) To eliminate economic panic; (3) To safeguard peace. On the economic front, the party's declaration advocates controlling lending, increasing production and international trade, and developing business institutions, while breaking away from the control of trusts and speculation. On the international front, it advocates implementing a collective security system within the framework of the League of Nations. (November 3rd Havas Dispatch)

League of Nations Transport Division Chief, Haas, Dies. Visited China Three Times to Investigate 44

(Geneva) Haas, chief of the Transport Division of the League of Nations, died suddenly of a heart attack yesterday afternoon at the age of 44. Haas was French and graduated from the École Normale Supérieure in Paris. After joining the League of Nations, he visited China three times. The first time was in 1930, as chief of the Transport Division of the League of Nations, to investigate transportation in China. The second time was in 1932, when he served as the secretary-general of the Lytton Commission investigating the Sino-Japanese incident, assisting the work of the investigation team. A large part of the investigation team's report was written by Haas. His third visit to China was last year, when he succeeded Rajchman as the liaison officer for technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China. In the spring of this year, he traveled by car to various provinces in northern, southern, and central China to inspect road construction, and also traveled to Guangdong and Guangxi. He returned to France in May and gave a speech at the Institute of Intellectual Cooperation, detailing his experiences in China. Recently, the League of Nations published Haas's report, praising China's economic construction and road-building achievements. (November 4th Havas Dispatch)

Minister Liu to Take Up New Post in Austria. German University President Hosts Farewell Banquet 45

Frankfurt, Germany: Former Chinese Minister to Germany Liu Chongjie has been transferred to be Minister to Austria and will soon take office in Vienna. Today, he was hosted by the president of the University of Frankfurt. On behalf of the Chinese government, Minister Liu presented two famous paintings to the city of Frankfurt, which were accepted by the mayor's representative. In the evening, the Chinese Academy of the University of Frankfurt hosted a farewell banquet for Minister Liu. Many people gave speeches at the banquet, expressing their resentment over the assassination of Chinese Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei and hoping for his speedy recovery, asking Liu to convey their wishes. (November 3rd Havas Dispatch)

No Changes in Hong Kong Dollar Currently 46

(Hong Kong) It is not yet possible to find out any news about what changes will occur in the Hong Kong dollar. However, well-informed circles believe that the Hong Kong government may take swift action to move towards managed currency measures. Today, HSBC offered an exchange rate of one shilling and six and a half pence to genuine trading merchants, with a monthly reduction of one French centime (i.e., one-quarter of a penny) for forward contracts, but still refused to offer interbank rates. Chinese banks are currently quoting one shilling and six pence. As of noon today, the Hong Kong government has not shown any signs of action. (November 4th Reuters Dispatch)

Each Boasting of Their Achievements in China, They Will Adopt a Policy of Great Unity in the Future

(Tokyo) The Great Asia Alliance, hosted by General Iwane Matsui, held a symposium at the Aviation Hall the other day. —Reuter's Special Commercial Report, October 4th—

Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold price today is 141 shillings 5 pence, down by half a pence.

British Silver: London silver market is stable, spot price rose 1.875 to 29 and a half pence, futures rose 3.125 to 29 and 1/875 pence. China sold, market is stable.

Exchange Rates

British-American: London foreign exchange market, today there was a slight demand for pounds from the European continent. At 2 PM, it rose by half a cent to four dollars, nine dimes, two cents, four three seven five.

British-French: Opened at 74 francs 63, higher by one pound音 than the closing price on Saturday. At 2 PM, it rose twelve磅音 to 74 francs 75.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: New York cotton market opened slightly higher due to favorable Alexandria telegrams, but soon fell by one to three pounds音. British Cotton: Liverpool cotton market turned slightly looser. At 1 PM, the January futures fell by three pounds音 to 6.09.

, economy of time, the ancient art of shrinking the land, is seen today. From Xi'an, take the Longhai Railway, then the Jinpu and Jiaoji Railways, and return to Qingdao on October 13th. In each place passed, stay for three or four days in most, one or two days in few. The total travel time is exactly one month. I have spent half my life at sea, and have set foot in most places in the world with waterways, but this is my first time in the northwest of our country, and I feel endless interest. The places inspected on this trip include the five provinces of Shanxi, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Gansu, and Shaanxi. During the visit, I received warm hospitality from the local military and political leaders, providing me with various conveniences. Factories, handicrafts, and schools in all the cities were almost completely visited. Their kindness is deeply appreciated. Unfortunately, due to time constraints, many desired places could not be visited. Day after day on the road, what was seen was not in depth. I will discuss my personal observations and feelings in the following points. First, the greatness of ancient culture is admirable. The Northwest is the birthplace of the Chinese nation. The traces of the evolution of various ethnic cultures recorded in history can be found in the Northwest provinces. For example, in Xi'an City, there are still the old sites of Feng and Hao, the two capitals of the Zhou Dynasty. The Epang Palace of Qin can still be vaguely examined. The capitals of the Han and Tang Dynasties also left relics. Just by relying on broken tiles and bricks, one can imagine the magnificence of the ancient capitals. The beautiful origin of Chinese Buddhism, this is just in terms of all spiritual civilization. As for material civilization, there are also things that have been passed down for thousands of years, and are still sufficient to be used for the people's livelihood today. For example, in Ningxia's water conservancy projects, there are the Qin Canal, the Han Canal, and the Tang Canal, all of which were built by the Qin, Han, and Tang Dynasties. Their scale is grand, the length of the canals is hundreds of miles, and the short ones are also more than a hundred miles. Countless branch canals are opened on the sides, drawing water from the Yellow River to irrigate the fields. Farmers still benefit from it to this day. The design conforms to the terrain and follows the water's nature, which is very consistent with scientific methods, so the Yellow River water does not cause harm, but is turned into a benefit. The Yungang Grottoes in Datong have long been famous in the world. Their structure is carved from a single stone, carving Buddha statues in the rock between the rocks. The greatness of the project and the exquisiteness of the art, modern sculpture cannot surpass. Looking at the traces of history, it really gives people endless emotions. Second, the Northwest is vast and rich in resources, sufficient for development. The Northwest provinces are mostly vast and sparsely populated. For example, Suiyuan has an area of 1.17 million square miles and a population of only 2.1 million. Ningxia has an area of 800,000 square miles and a population of only 1.4 million. Gansu has an area of 1.1 million square miles and a population of only 6 million. Therefore, the population density of the three provinces is only two people per square mile, which is more than twenty times different compared to the southeastern provinces, which have forty or fifty people per square mile. Therefore, the Northwest only has geographical advantages, but lacks people to develop it. Along the way, wherever the rivers pass and the plains are located, the land is mostly fertile and the agricultural products are abundant. The mountain areas are mostly bare, but the forests cultivated in the Yin of Helan Mountain in ancient times still have towering trees, with ancient trees that can be embraced, which shows that the soil is suitable for afforestation. If artificial　planting is applied, then the timber will be inexhaustible. Currently, on the upper reaches of the Yellow River, once the bare mountains on both sides are washed by rain, the streams carry sediment into the river, causing the riverbed to silt up and flooding every year. If　trees are planted, then the roots will be intertwined, the soil will not be eroded, and the river can be dredged. Therefore, afforestation not only has the benefit of people's livelihood, but also can prevent the disasters of the Yellow River. The areas with water and grass in the Northwest are suitable for animal husbandry. Herds of cattle, sheep, horses, and camels, the resources needed for the leather and wool weaving industry, and the benefits relied on by the transportation industry, are the most important resources in the Northwest. This time, I visited the Xinong Company in Saxian, Suiyuan, which uses modern agricultural tools to develop vast lands, and also engages in animal husbandry, forestry, and textile industries. Its service providers are mostly specialized talents, adapting to local conditions, and the results are very good. Other places are no different. In short, the Northwest is rich in geographical advantages. Whether it is running agriculture and forestry, or organizing animal husbandry, or opening a wool weaving industry, as long as people can do their best, there will be good harvests. Currently, local officials can all pay attention to this. Even in an economically difficult environment, they still strive for development. In addition to the industry and commerce of Shanxi, which have been built for many years and are quite large in scale, Sui, Ning, Gan, and Shaanxi are also actively underway. However, based on my observations, I believe that there are three prerequisites for developing the resources of the Northwest. First, transportation. Currently, the PingSui Railway only reaches Baotou, and the Longhai Railway only reaches Xi'an. Efforts should be made to extend them separately, connecting Ningxia, Lanzhou, Xi'an and other places, so that the transportation in the Northwest provinces is like the meridians of the body, connected to each other. All local products, as well as imported raw materials and machinery, will be exported and imported, and the exchange will be smooth. Then, the industry will be easier to develop. Second, manpower. The Northwest has natural treasures, but lacks manpower to manage them. Therefore, it is necessary to first immigrate people from the interior to supplement the manpower, and to recruit technical personnel to organize and plan with scientific methods, and work together to manage them, so that development can be planned. Third, financial resources. The Northwest's geographical advantages have not been developed, the economy is difficult, transportation is inconvenient, and production is not easy. The government must advocate for fundraising from above, and the financial sector must assist from below. Officials and people of each province work together to make it have basic construction first, then the resources can be gradually developed. If these three, transportation, manpower, and financial resources, can be combined into one, then there is no need to worry that the land cannot be used to its full potential and the goods cannot flow smoothly. Third, regarding the climate and customs of the Northwest, before we went to the Northwest, we imagined that the place must be filled with cold wind and sand. But who knew that it was not so? Most of the places I passed through were too warm, just like the interior. The winter clothes I brought were all useless. The dialects of Fujian and Guangdong cannot be understood, and there are no major differences in customs and habits. This is the case for the Han people, as well as the Mongolians and Hui people. In recent years, local officials have actively paid attention to education, and there are many schools in the provincial capitals. If transportation develops further, the contribution to culture will also be very great. As for the problem of the Red Bandits scurrying and attacking, apart from a part in northern Shaanxi, the rest once fled to the northwest through the southern border of Gansu. The area of Gansu and Shaanxi is vast and the mountain roads are rugged, and although it is a little difficult to encircle and suppress them, Chiang Kai-shek has established a bandit suppression headquarters in Xi'an, and has established command posts in Chongqing and Yichang, combining the large armies of Shaanxi, Gansu, Ning, Sichuan, and Hubei to jointly suppress them. It is believed that the fleeing Red Bandits will have nowhere to escape. Currently, the Northwest is sparsely populated, it is not easy to obtain food, and the people hate the cruelty of the communists extremely. No matter what threats or inducements are used, they cannot use their tricks. It is thought that they will be completely eliminated in the shortest time.

Current Status of the Yuehan Railway Project 49

The entire line is scheduled to be completed by the end of next year. Currently, 201 kilometers are open to traffic.

Changsha Correspondent: The Yuehan Railway is a major line connecting the north and south. Construction began in the 24th year of Guangxu in the late Qing Dynasty. The entire line is 1,096 kilometers long. The section from Guangzhou to Shaozhou is 222 kilometers, and it was opened to traffic in the 4th year of the Republic of China. The section from Wuchang Xujiapeng to Zhuzhou in Hunan Province is 417 kilometers, and it was also opened to traffic in the 7th year of the Republic of China. The middle section from Zhuzhou to Shaozhou is 456 kilometers long. Due to the difficulty of the work and the large amount of funds required, it was suspended for many years. In the 18th year of the Republic of China, the central government decided to use Boxer Indemnity funds for the construction of the road, so the Zhushao Section Engineering Bureau was established in Guangzhou, and Ling Hongxun was appointed as the director. The first section to be built was from Shaozhou to Lechang, which is 50 kilometers long. Construction started in the 19th year and was completed and opened to traffic in June of the 22nd year. In September of that year, the Engineering Bureau moved from Guangdong to Hengyang in Hunan Province, and actively planned the construction work. It was divided into three sections, north, south, and middle, and carried out simultaneously. It was originally limited to four years to complete, and then Tai Ling reduced the knowledge by half a year, limited to the end of the 25th year of the Republic of China to complete and open to traffic.

Sectional Construction

For the convenience of construction, the Engineering Bureau divided it into seven general sections. The first general section is from Shaozhou to Lechang, 50 kilometers (completed and open to traffic). The second general section is from Lechang to Luojiadu, a little over 46 kilometers (completed). The third general section is from Luojiadu to Shuitoudong, a little over 66 kilometers. The fourth general section is from Shuitoudong to Gaotingsi, a little over 59 kilometers (currently under construction). The fifth general section is from Gaotingsi to Guanyinqiao, 75 kilometers (two-thirds completed). The sixth general section is from Guanyinqiao to Fengtang, a little over 67 kilometers (one-third completed). The seventh general section is from Fengtang to Zhuzhou, 90 kilometers (eighty-nine tenths completed). In total, about 76 percent of the entire project has been completed.

Track Laying Situation

The southern section is being laid northwards from Lechang, the middle section is being laid southwards from the south bank of the Lei River in Chongzhou territory, and the northern section is being laid southwards from Zhuzhou. Because the Lu River Bridge has not yet been completed, the southern section is being laid southward across the Lu River. It is estimated that by the end of August next year, it will be laid to the border between Hunan and Guangdong provinces, and will connect with the middle section. The middle section reached Leiyang from the south of the Lei River in mid-August this year. It is estimated that it will reach Chenzhou in February next year, and will connect with the southern section in August. The northern section has reached Lukou this year from the south of Zhuzhou, and will continue to advance south from Lukou. By the end of this month, it can reach Shishan Hengshan, and it is estimated that it will reach the north bank of the Lei River in June next year, and will connect with the middle section.

Bridges and Tunnels The entire line passes through the three tributaries of the Lu, Mi, and Lei rivers. There are three steel bridges built, each with a length of more than three or four meters. There are also five large arch bridges, including the Xin Yan Xia Bridge with six arches, 190 meters long, the Duiwei Chong Bridge with two arches, 105 meters long, the Provincial Border Bridge with three arches, 105 meters long, the Fengchui Kou Bridge with three arches, 88 meters long, and the Yantang Bridge with two arches, 75 meters long. All projects have been completed by six or seven tenths. There are also 17 tunnels in the southern section, the longest being more than 400 meters long and the shortest being 46 meters long, all of which have now been completed.

Traffic Situation

The completed sections of the Yuehan Road have been opened to traffic in sections by engineering trains, and passenger and freight business is being handled. The northern section from Zhuzhou to Lukou, Lukou to Zhaoling, was opened to traffic in March and May of this year, with a total length of 66 kilometers. The middle section from the south bank of the Lei River to Leiyang, was opened to traffic in mid-August, with a length of 79 kilometers. The southern section from Shaozhou to Lechang, 50 kilometers, has long been open to traffic. From Lechang to Pingshi, 56 kilometers, was opened to traffic in September of this year. At the same time, in order to facilitate traffic, the Hunan-Guangdong Road Administration Bureau and the Hunan and Guangdong Provincial Highway Bureaus jointly organized the Yuehan entire line railway and highway intermodal transport, and preparations are complete and will be implemented immediately.

Guangdong Provincial Construction Bonds Postponed 50

The face value of the bonds has also been finally decided. The operating profits of the cement plant will be used as a fund.

Guangzhou Correspondent: Since the bankruptcy of the Guangdong National and Two Banks in Guangdong Province, the social finance has been greatly affected, and the capital of various places is short. However, the credit of the provincial bank notes is consolidated, and it is also planning to expand the currency, and decided to expand the scope of circulation of the provincial bank haoquan to regulate the rural economy of various counties and cities. On the one hand, it welcomes the investment of Shanghai's silver industry in rural industries. At the same time, in order to actively handle the construction of the entire province, the government issued construction bonds of 5 million yuan, originally scheduled to be issued on August 1, but due to the rush to print, it has been postponed to December 1. Previously, the face value of the bonds was planned to be divided into four types: 5 yuan, 10 yuan, 50 yuan, and 100 yuan. Recently, it has been decided to change the small denominations into larger ones, and the face value has been changed to three types: 100 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 10,000 yuan, to facilitate sales. It is now found that the bonds with a face value of 100 yuan are printed in 20,000 sheets, totaling 2 million yuan; the bonds with a face value of 1,000 yuan are printed in 1,000 sheets, totaling 2 million yuan; the bonds with a face value of 10,000 yuan are printed in 100 sheets, totaling 1 million yuan. This bond is printed by the Shanghai Commercial Press, and will be transported to Guangdong within days. In the future, half of the bonds will be sold by Shanghai banks. The total amount of the bonds is 5 million yuan, with a fixed interest rate of 7 percent per year. The operating profits of the Guangdong Xicun Shimin 10th factory will be used as a fund to form a fund management committee. The remaining profits of the factory will be allocated to the committee every month for special reserves. The Guangdong Provincial Bank will be responsible for the repayment of principal and interest. The repayment period is from May 25th of the Republic of China to November 29th, repaying in five years. As for the use of the bond funds, they will be used to expand Guangdong's sugar factories, textile factories, fertilizer factories, and to establish paper mills and soda factories. May of next year will be the first time for drawing lots to repay the principal and pay interest. After that, lotteries will be held every five months to repay the principal and pay interest. It is estimated that the principal and interest can be repaid by November 29th. This case was presented to the Nanjing Executive Yuan by the Guangdong Provincial Government in May of this year, requesting that it be allowed to issue in accordance with the precedent of the construction bonds issued by Zhejiang and Hunan provinces. The Executive Yuan replied by telegram, stating that the case had been approved by the 38th Yuan affairs meeting and sent to the Central Political Conference for approval. On July 13, a telegram was received from the Legislative Yuan, stating that the case had been jointly presented to the Executive Yuan by the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and had been passed by the Central Political Conference and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. The Guangdong Provincial Government recently reported to the Executive Yuan again for the record the reasons for postponing the issuance to December 1 due to the time required for printing the bonds. Yesterday, it received a reply from the Yuan, approving the implementation. (October 26th)

Escaped Prisoner Captured and Sent to Songjiang

Zhong Shaoyun, the bandit involved in the Huang Guoxiang case in Shanjiaqiao, a county under the jurisdiction of the former, was sentenced to 15 years in prison by the court and sent to prison. Unexpectedly, he escaped from prison on March 18. He had been wanted for a long time without success. Until recently, he was spotted in the Jiaofu teahouse in Shanyang. Because the prisoner had a record of escaping from prison, he was arrested. He has now been sent to Songjiang and returned to the local court for retrial.

Suzhou

Silver and Money Industry Calls Emergency Meeting

The silver and money industries in Suzhou received a telegram from the Shanghai Banking Association on the evening of the 4th, stating that the Ministry of Finance was implementing the legal tender system. Special emergency meetings were convened by the banking and money industries respectively at 9:00 am on the 5th to discuss everything. Since there is no branch of the Central Bank in Suzhou, the exchange of legal tender will be handled by the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. According to people in the money industry, the silver reserves of the silver and money industries in Suzhou are about 300,000 yuan. The exchange rate of various cigarette stores inside and outside the city on the evening of the 4th was 3,400 copper coins per yuan. Small foreign coins could be exchanged for 12 jiao and 250. From 8:00 am on the 5th, there was a sudden chaos, and the exchange rates varied. Some even removed the foreign exchange price signs. By noon, it had calmed down a little. The exchange rate was 3,000 copper coins per yuan, and small foreign coins were 12 jiao. In order to stabilize the market, the county government decided to hold a meeting with representatives from the county chamber of commerce and the silver and money industries to discuss solutions.

Wuxi: Copper Coins Suddenly Plunge on the Market

After the news that the Ministry of Finance stipulated that banknotes from the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications were legal tender reached Wuxi, people on the market told each other. It was expected that the market for copper coins would take a sharp turn for the worse. Before the opening of the copper coin market in the morning, those with good information bought up copper coins, making huge profits. At noon, the Money Industry Association discussed the market. The purchase price of copper coins was 3,000 wen, and the selling price was 2,990 wen, which was 260 wen more than yesterday, which was a dramatic change that broke the record. The market for small foreign coins, yesterday's purchase price was 759, and the selling price was 763. Yesterday's purchase price was 77 percent, and the selling price was 77.4 percent, with each jiao worth 203 wen.

Silk Cocoon Prices Soar

Since the autumn of this year, the European and American markets have suddenly seen active Chinese silk. Foreign firms stationed in Shanghai are also purchasing Chinese silk, leading to soaring silk prices. The current price per dan for silk of the highest grade has risen to 850 yuan in national currency, which is more than double the previous silk price. This has not happened since 1930. Silk factories and silk merchants in various places have made huge profits, especially Yongtai in our county and Baotai in Shanghai. The price of dried cocoons has risen to 270 yuan per dan. At the same time, silk cocoon by-products have also risen. There are currently about 12,000 silk reeling machines in our county. Assuming that each machine uses 4 jin of cocoons per day, 412 dan of dried cocoons are needed every day. It is found that the cocoons stored in warehouses and stockers throughout the county are only enough for the factories for one month, and the dried cocoons in the hands of the stockers are waiting for a good price. Therefore, by the end of this month, various factories will reduce the number of machines they operate to maintain business.
