The Jiangsu Provincial Public Security Bureau's political police training class, the first class of political police, graduated last year and have now been dispatched to serve in various places. The second class began training in May of this year, with a total of 50 male and female police officers. They were sent to various sub-bureaus for two weeks of practical training at the beginning of last month, and the term has now expired. A graduation ceremony was held a few days ago and certificates were issued. The General Bureau, headed by Director Chuan, will transfer a part of the female police officers in this class to the General Bureau for service. It is reported that the class was ordered to transfer all the female police officers to the General Bureau for service on the 4th.

Changshu

County Magistrate Personally Destroys Red Pill Factory

Lu Bingzhong, a resident of Yangjian Town, which is located at the junction of Xichang, secretly set up a large-scale red pill manufacturing factory, selling and transporting it to Xichang, Suzhou, Cheng, and other areas. The business was very prosperous. In the summer of this year, Lu was arrested and sent to the province. On September 18, he was executed by shooting in the town. His son, Lu Fenglin, who had been on the run, is still hiding in the countryside and manufacturing privately. The authorities have been investigating repeatedly for more than two months. A few days ago, Sun Daxing, Zhang Xiqing, and other investigators secretly dispatched by the county disguised themselves as sailors and arrived in the countryside to Lu's place.

Yangzhou

Jiangsu Gentry Please Block the Yellow River Breach

Korean Jun, Ma Shijie, Leng Yu, and Zhang Yipeng, gentry from Jiangsu, submitted a joint request to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Relief Committee, and the Economic Committee regarding the Dongzhuang Yellow River breach, stating that on July 10 of this year, the Huangnan Zhulin Dyke between Heze and Juancheng in western Shandong had not yet been completed, and the Min Nian Guandi under Dongzhuang suddenly breached one, two, three, four, and five mouths, diverting seventy-eight tenths of the Yellow River water and pouring down. The breach reached dozens or hundreds of feet. Tracing back to the Lisheng Tun breach in 1925, it still returned to the main river at Taojiabu, and the disaster area did not expand. This time the situation is different. The water divides into two branches, flowing northeast and southeast, entering the Dongping and Weishan Lakes, and advancing from western Shandong to northern Jiangsu. Recently, because the Yishui and Wenshui rivers in southern Shandong were flooded by the Yellow River water, the disaster area in northern Jiangsu is twice as large as that in western Shandong. The autumn harvest is reduced, and spring farming is hopeless. Therefore, Jun and others only hope to block the breach. It is expected that the authorities will never procrastinate or underestimate the breach. Now, there are less than three months before the ice melts. If the surveying, planning, funding, personnel, materials, and all matters that should be handled can be completed by the time of the Frost's Descent solar term, waiting for the water level to drop, working day and night, there may be hope of closing the gap before the ice melts. It is also said that the Yellow River migrated north to Jiangsu only eighty years ago, and a part of the riverbank is in danger. The guards have prior responsibility and contingency plans. If there is danger, the river should be diverted. Then, in the four thousand years of the Yellow River, there have been no less than six changes, and the north-south division has been a precedent since the Song Dynasty to the Ming Dynasty. Based on the history of the Yellow River breach in 1933, it is requested that the supervision and control of breach blocking and diversion be implemented separately, which is a virtue and convenience.

Contact was made to purchase a large number of red pills. Lu believed it to be true, and agreed to deliver the goods at Yanjiaqiao on the third night at 11:00 pm. The investigators found out the truth and immediately reported it to the county government by telephone. At 9:00 pm, County Magistrate Zhai personally led Geng Boyang, the head of the Anti-Smoking Section, and 40 security team members, including all the bailiffs, to the village in three large trucks overnight, surrounded Lu's factory, arrested the principal offender Lu Fenglin, his wife Zhou, and two accomplices, and returned to the city that night. From 2:00 am to 9:00 am on the 4th, County Magistrate asked Lu personally. Lu admitted to manufacturing red pills without denial, and said that the raw materials were purchased through Chen Junying's introduction. The county government will now transfer the case to the provincial garrison headquarters for review.

The National Situation of Abyssinia 51

— Ang Ro

——Race, Politics, Military——

One

Abyssinia is an ancient feudal country. Almost all the people in the country are illiterate, there are virtually no roads, and the annual foreign trade is less than 25 million U.S. dollars. The Abyssinian natives rule many dependent tribes, and those belonging to the ancient Abyssinian race probably account for no more than one-third of the total population. The rest do not believe in any Christian religion, nor do they speak Amharic. The Abyssinian natives live in the central plateau, while the dependent tribes live in the surrounding lowlands. It is difficult to determine the total population, and estimates generally range from 5 million to 20 million. Scholars familiar with the Abyssinian national situation estimate it to be between 7 and 8 million. However, any statistics on Abyssinia are scarce and completely unreliable.

The racially complex people of the Abyssinian Empire can be distinguished in several ways. Physical characteristics are the most difficult to rely on. The Abyssinian natives consider themselves to belong to the white race and are descendants of the North African Hamitic people. This is correct, but thousands of years of contact with black people in Central and East Africa have dyed their skin coffee-colored, or even a dark chocolate color.

Language is a more reliable standard for distinguishing ethnic groups. The people of the central plateau speak a Semitic language. The Galla people, who live in the south of the central region, are black and have their own language. They migrated from the south in the early modern period. They also account for one-third of the total population. The remaining one-third is divided into several small tribes, scattered in the border provinces of Danakil, Somalia, and Sidamo. Based on this linguistic distinction, we can say that the one-third of the population in the highlands (Semitic) rules the two-thirds of the population in the lowlands (non-Semitic).

Religion is also a way to distinguish ethnic groups. The Abyssinian natives are Christians, but at least nominally some of the Galla people have also converted to Christianity. The total number of Christians accounts for about half of the total population. Muslims account for three-eighths and live in the east and southeast. In addition, there are the Falasha people—Abyssinian Jews—about 100,000 to 200,000 people, whose Jewish teachings are very corrupt and who do not understand Hebrew. The rest of the people are non-religious.

The Christians in Abyssinia belong to the ancient Egyptian Church. The archbishop is appointed by the patriarch of Alexandria and is often an Egyptian. The Abyssinian emperor wants to replace him with a local, but it is not easy to break the customs in Abyssinia, so he has to set up several local bishops to assist him. There are many pastors, some say they account for one-third of the adult population. This is of course an exaggeration, but in a static society (such as Tibet), the number of people who hold world-weary ideas must exceed the needs of the church. The pastors in Abyssinia are rich in land. They are uneducated and quite superstitious. They have thus created a great conservative force. For 1,500 years, religion has been a great force in maintaining Abyssinia's independence.

Two

The Abyssinian Empire is the best example of a feudal state today. The society within its borders is based on strict layers of classes, each class having its traditional economic and political functions. The foundation of the social organization is military. Those who can lead troops against the enemy in wartime are the national elite and receive the supreme honor of the country. In peacetime, these soldiers are the officials who govern the country. This system has been passed down for centuries without much change. Before the end of the 19th century, Abyssinia was isolated from the outside world. However, in the 16th century, it was briefly invaded by the Portuguese, but only for a short time. By the reign of Menelik (Emperor Menelik died in 1913), Western civilization had invaded Abyssinia again. However, to this day, this force has only reached the king's side. Although the king has tried his best to reform, he is still inflexible.

The current Emperor Haile Selassie is implementing a system of centralized monarchy. In the past, unless the monarch was as powerful as Menelik, the feudal lords of the four directions often wanted to become arrogant and not be restrained by their nominal monarch. Because the territory was vast and mountainous, local ideas developed, and mutual suspicion often made it difficult for weak leaders to rule. The current emperor's centralization movement has achieved great success. Several hereditary feudal lords have already submitted, and those who are not supervised by the capital have been replaced by the king.

After Menelik's death, the disintegrating monarchy is now gradually recovering. This movement took a sharp turn in 1926 due to the death of Grand Marshal Fivives. Fivives commanded the national army for 30 years. Once he died, Crown Prince Tafari Makonnen (now the Emperor) seized the opportunity to seize his fiefdom, take over his military power, and merge it with his hereditary Harar province army, leaping to become the most powerful prince in Abyssinia. He made a thunderous announcement to the feudal lords who had the same right to inherit the throne, expressing his determination to take power alone. In 1928, Empress Zewditu (Menelik's daughter) made him king. In 1930, the empress died and he ascended the throne, with the national title Haile Selassie. In 1932, General Hailu of the once independent Gojjam province rebelled, and the king sent troops to put him down. Thus, the most important and fertile area located in the loop of the Blue Nile also came under the jurisdiction of the central government. However, on the whole, the hereditary feudal lords have not abolished their fiefdoms, and the centralization movement is limited to the eastern and southern border provinces, where the people are mostly Muslims or non-religious, and the land was only conquered during Menelik's reign, so there has not been time for assimilation.

Abyssinia also has a constitution, which was promulgated by the emperor in 1931. The constitution also stipulates that the "Parliament" must meet regularly. It is needless to say that this "Parliament" cannot be compared with the legislative bodies of European and American democratic countries. The so-called "representatives" have no power to supervise legislation and administration. Their terms of office are completely controlled by the king. This "Parliament" can only be regarded as a registry. If the king has an edict to make known at home and abroad, he will personally announce it at this "Parliament." These members of parliament cannot be regarded as representing the ignorant masses of Abyssinia. At best, they can only be regarded as representing the feudal lords.

Three

Because Abyssinia is a feudal state, even a powerful king must rely on the cooperation of the feudal lords to resist foreign aggression. In theory, every soldier in Abyssinia must be loyal to the king, but this is not always the case. The king is high above, and the power of the government has not been completely centralized. The soldiers are only controlled by the feudal lords. Although the feudal lords cannot rebel, they can still sabotage the central government's plans through passive resistance.

Recently, there have been frequent reports that many border chiefs have surrendered to the Italian army, but this cannot be without considerable conditions. This kind of thing of buying over the Abyssinian dependent tribes has always failed in the past. At the end of the 19th century, the Italians secretly helped King Menelik of Shoa to resist King Yohannes. In 1889, Yohannes died, and Menelik succeeded to the throne and implemented an anti-Italian policy. After that, Italian Prime Minister Crispi wanted to instigate a rebellion by the northern dependent tribes, but in the Battle of Adwa, the northern feudal lords all worked for Menelik and defeated the Italian army. This is a prominent historical example.

The Abyssinian army is an outdated force. If there were no dangerous terrain as a natural barrier, it would be difficult to maintain national independence.

The Abyssinian Imperial Guard is the only modern force, with a strength of about 2,500 to 30,000 men. Since 1929, this army has been trained by Belgian and Swedish officers. They wear uniforms, are barefoot, carry modern weapons, and drill according to military science. This army can be said to be a strong force. The emperor is unwilling to send them to the front unless it is a critical moment.

In addition to the Imperial Guard, the emperor also has his own Imperial Army, which is composed of armed subjects within his jurisdiction. The current emperor's jurisdiction includes the three provinces of Harar, Wollo, and Shoa. These Imperial Armies are stationed in various places, serving as guards and enforcing edicts. There are no accurate statistics on the number of Imperial Armies, probably between 50,000 and 100,000. This kind of army can only be regarded as a mixed army in other countries. Their military equipment and organization are very outdated.

The feudal lords' conscription is also the same outdated. All able-bodied men must join the army. Only monks, priests, merchants, shepherds, and guards of noble women can be exempted from military service. If the population decreases in the future, these people will inevitably have their exemption qualifications revoked.

There are different opinions on the actual number of troops that the emperor can mobilize. Some say that one million people have already been mobilized. This is probably an exaggeration. There may be this number of people in service, but the overall mobilization, supplies, and weapons are insufficient, which is detrimental to the military. Therefore, mobilizing 500,000 people is probably closer to the truth. Eritrean former governor 石禮 estimated that Abyssinia could mobilize at most 250,000 troops to the front line. In Tigray Province, supplies are difficult, and it would be unwise for Abyssinia to concentrate a large army. ;

It is also difficult to count Abyssinia's military equipment. There are probably 500,000 to 600,000 rifles of various types, hundreds of machine guns, and dozens of cannons. The so-called cannons are probably just exhibits in museums. Although there are a few airplanes, they cannot be used for combat. There are certainly no gas equipment, tank fleets, and other modern tactical weapons.

In terms of military equipment, although Abyssinia is far inferior to the Italian army, it has several advantages. First, they have the advantage of terrain. Second, they are familiar with the terrain for combat. Third, their actions are more convenient than the enemy's. They do not need auxiliary teams that European military departments consider indispensable, such as baggage trains and ambulance teams. The Abyssinian army does not need to bring much food and pay for its progress, and they can eat on the spot. This is very convenient for a quick battle. The Italian army, which is accustomed to European life, cannot eat African food, so it must bring enough bulky military supplies. The Abyssinian army does not have front-line hospitals or rear-line hospitals. Women servants who go out with the army to bandage wounds must help themselves.

In a protracted war, this advantage in mobility loses its value. The food requisitioned on the spot will soon run out, and the courage of the armies collected from various places will also decline. Moreover, Abyssinians are unwilling to leave their homes for several months. They are especially unhappy about joining the army during the rainy season. What they hope for is a victory in one battle. Once the enemy army is defeated, they will disperse and return home, no longer eager to take advantage of the victory. The defeats of the Egyptian army in Gonder and Gura in 1875, and the defeat of the Italian army in Adwa in 1896, all came to an abrupt end in this way. If the Abyssinians still have this old temper in this war, then when the rainy season arrives, we will see hundreds of thousands of Italian troops stationed in the Abyssinian mountains, but no Abyssinian army fighting against them. However, Mussolini has various concerns, and his military operations cannot last for a long time. (Excerpt from RcbertGajcWoolbert's thesis)

Nantong

Jiangbei Remote Ports Blockaded

The small and remote ports along the river and sea in the six counties under the jurisdiction of Nantong District are being blockaded by the public security teams of the District Security Command, both on water and land, to prevent bandits from intruding. The blockade will remain in effect until the end of the winter defense period, and will then be lifted. Haimen

Yongxing Town Pillaged by Bandits

Yongxing Town in Qidong was suddenly attacked by more than 20 bandits armed with box guns at around 7:00 PM on the first day of the month. They broke into various shops and looted them at will. The Huang Yuantai Yuchunxiang, Ding Taiyuan, and Zhu Julang families suffered the heaviest losses. ...... They marched north in formation. Many villagers beat gongs to pursue and arrest them. ...... They shot and wounded four people: Zhang Zhiren, Lu Baohua, Lu Hongfu, and Lu Shun. Zhang Zhiren died soon after due to excessive blood loss. On the morning of the second day, the merchants of the town reported the incident to the Qidong County Government. County Magistrate Li personally inspected the scene and instructed the merchants to continue their business as usual. The family members of the deceased were instructed to prepare coffins and bury the body. At the same time, the police were ordered to strictly arrest the bandits and bring them to justice for interrogation.

Gangster Group Arrested and Paraded

Sixteen people, including orderlies from government offices and corrupt police officers, swore blood oaths and formed a secret society called the "We Ethnic Group Affectionate Society." Even female gangsters like Mao Wenying joined the group. It was reported that their subordinates and henchmen numbered in the hundreds, and that they had elected a certain Lu as their leader. Two photos of the group were also submitted for verification. Director Yu was furious upon receiving the report. He pointed out that with the winter defense period about to begin, these gangsters dared to form secret societies, which would inevitably lead to trouble. He personally issued an order to all sub-bureaus and teams to strictly investigate and arrest them by name and send them for investigation. Subsequently, the sub-bureaus and teams successively arrested six male and female gangsters and sent them to the bureau. After interrogation, they were ordered to denounce their accomplices. In the afternoon, the six men and women were bound and paraded through the streets as a warning. Meanwhile, the remaining criminals and their ringleaders were still being strictly apprehended to maintain social security.

Incoming Mail: A Humble Opinion on Salt Administration Reform 53

— Li Youyi

(Continued from Part Three)

(4) Appropriately reduce the salt tax and rectify smuggling suppression so that no grain of illegally produced salt escapes and tax revenue can still maintain its original state. Salt tax is a major source of national income. Besides customs duties, salt tax is the most important. Recent average figures are about 13 to 14 million yuan. The reason for such a huge amount is because the tax is fixed. Unlike other goods, which are taxed a few percent of their assessed value, let us try to compare the price sold by salt farmers with the tax. In areas with heavy taxes, it is almost ten times the price, and in lighter areas, it is several times. Even in terms of the selling price, the tax accounts for most of it. This is truly a deformed method of taxation. Some may think that although salt is necessary for people, the amount consumed is very small and the impact on livelihoods is light. It doesn't hurt to increase the tax and make the people bear it universally. However, I do not know that this burden falls particularly heavily on the poor. It is appropriate to reduce it to alleviate their plight. In this autumn of national events and urgent need for money, even if it cannot be taxed a few percent of the assessed value like other goods, it is appropriate to carefully consider possible methods to reduce it. The new salt law stipulates a tax of five yuan per 100 kilograms, and all surcharges are waived. A kilogram is larger than a market catty, and each dan is about two market catties. The tax rate is thus reduced a lot, which can be said to benefit the poor a lot (but the price paid to salt farmers should be raised even higher). Some may argue that with the treasury strapped for cash, reducing the salt tax will only make the Ministry of Agriculture look up at the roof and struggle to cope. I would say that the only way to remedy this is to earnestly rectify smuggling suppression and eliminate all private sales in the country, so that the tax lost to illegal sales can be used to offset the reduction. Let us elaborate on this point. China's population is over 470 million (according to statistics from the Ministry of Interior), and based on the amount of salt consumed per person, each person consumes about five coins of salt per day, which amounts to one catty per month and twelve catties per year. Multiplying this by the population of 470 million, the total annual sales of salt can reach 56.4 million dan (and that doesn't include salt used in agriculture and industry, fishing salt, pickling, vegetable sales, and sauce sales). Based on the new salt law's tax rate of five yuan per dan, the annual revenue can be 182 million yuan. As mentioned earlier, the average salt tax revenue in recent years is about that amount. According to the statistics of the auditing office, the total amount of salt sold by the government in recent years is weak at an average of 37 million dan (including salt used in agriculture and industry, fishing salt, pickling, vegetable sales, and sauce sales). Compared with the sales based on the amount of salt consumed per person, there is a shortage of about 19 million dan. That is to say, the amount of salt sold privately throughout the country is about that number. Every year, about 95 million yuan in salt tax is lost. Even if the tax rate per kilogram stipulated in the [Salt] Law were halved, it would not break the average number of current income. Strict smuggling suppression is indeed the key to remedy. Please further discuss the disadvantages of illegal salt as follows: The value of table salt includes the majority of central and local surcharges, followed by transportation costs, and then by all expenses. The purchase price of salt is very low. The profit from private sales is that they are avoiding significant taxes, and even if they are caught by the smuggling suppression team after ten trips, they can still make a profit. The implementation of smuggling suppression in various provinces has always been corrupt, and the firearms are not complete. The large gangs of salt smugglers are all powerful figures with sophisticated firearms. It is easy to arrest fixed bandits. Moreover, after the smugglers are arrested and interrogated, they are sent to the county courts for trial. Although there are laws against smuggling to base on, county courts are not aware of salt matters and often consider it as a case of trying to make a living by evading taxes, so the sentences are reduced or even pardoned out of pity. Smugglers have high profits to gain and no strict laws to fear, so they are unscrupulous and the number of smugglers is increasing day by day (in 1933, when salt affairs administration was transferred to the auditing office and the offices for hearing salt cases were cut off, I once sent a letter to the Salt Affairs Office to discuss the advantages and disadvantages. At that time, the director of the Salt Affairs Office, Zhu Tingqi, seemed to adopt the idea and asked the deputy of Songjiang to review it, but it was rejected due to lack of funds). In this transition period of reform, I believe that we should revise the laws for the punishment of smugglers through the Legislative Yuan, pay attention to the judicial organs, and also heavily revise the regulations for smuggling suppression, practice reorganizing the national smuggling suppression team, and purchase sophisticated firearms to enrich its strength (although the Ministry of Finance previously formed a tax police regiment in the Song District, it is only limited to one corner, and I heard that it has not been used to replace the old smuggling suppression team for smuggling suppression). The production areas are garrisoned near the location, and the sales areas are stationed on the borders of each district, so that smugglers cannot escape the net. Arrest and severely punish the offenders to serve as a warning. Then, reduce the tax and reduce the price to combat private sales. Again, raise the price of salt to maintain the livelihood of salt farmers so that they are not happy to sell privately. Treat the root and the branches, and proceed on both sides. If we can earnestly reorganize and implement it for several years, I do not believe that smugglers will not be eliminated. The government will not only gain the reputation of benefiting the poor, but also will not lose the revenue from salt tax. I sincerely hope that it will be implemented as soon as possible, and the blessings will spread to the common people, which will bring infinite benefits to the country and society. (5) Formulate methods for merchants to pay taxes and contract transportation in order to facilitate tax collection. Article 1 of the general principles of the New Salt Law (Salt is taxed at the location, allowing the people to buy freely, and no one should monopolize it.) According to the meaning of taxing at the location, when salt farmers produce table salt, they should pay taxes before they are allowed to sell it. Since salt farmers have no untaxed salt, private salt will naturally be eliminated. It is indeed a good strategy to prevent private sales. However, it is difficult to do this in reality because salt farmers are all poor and have no ability to pay taxes. It is still necessary for merchants to pay taxes. That is to say, salt merchants who contract transportation must first pay taxes and prepay packaging and transportation costs, and all expenses must be pre-paid by those who are wealthy. The government can fix the sales amount in each district and recruit merchants to contract transportation, and pay the tax first according to the number, and not allow them to change transportation without authorization. This will not only continuously provide people with food, but also obtain the entire tax revenue. Some may argue that contracting transportation may still follow the same path of exclusive merchants, but it is not known that exclusive merchants rely on the Qing Dynasty's paper permit as a hereditary occupation. If they do not willingly sell the permit to others, even the wealthy cannot engage in salt trade. They rely on it and monopolize it very much. They manipulate it and think that no one else can do it. Even if the government knows it, it cannot cancel its business and find a replacement. If it is changed to contracting transportation and strictly supervised, there will be no way to monopolize it. Even if there is fraud, the punishment will be light and another merchant will be recruited to continue the contract. Merchants have considerable benefits, and there is nothing more stable than the salt business. Those who seek profits with money will undoubtedly rush to it. The disease of the old system lies in giving special exclusive privileges and setting low salt prices. Natural wealth comes to people, and for a long time, those with long sleeves are good at dancing. Since the Qing Dynasty, all salt merchants have amassed wealth. Those who are good at planning gain even more profits and take the world's benefits as their own. This is what is criticized by the world. However, salt tax revenue cannot be scattered and difficult to manage. The disease is recognized by the government to be where exclusive merchants are located and the old system is to be abolished. Then, the detailed methods for paying taxes and contracting transportation will be set in order to facilitate tax collection. As for the government's occasional emergency needs, it used to collect and borrow from salt merchants in advance. This was originally an expedient measure for temporary relief and should not be regarded as a normal practice. Moreover, this kind of action is not only a foolish policy of financial overdraft, but it is also enough to inspire merchants to hope for non-profits, which is not appropriate.

In summary, it can not only remove all the difficulties in implementing the new salt law, but also not be stubborn and difficult to implement. I believe that it is the best method for the initial reform in the transition period from the old to the new. As for the salt administration policy after the national treasury is abundant in the future, it is better to adopt Liu Yan's method of salt administration: people produce, officials collect, and merchants transport. Although it cannot be tax-free like in ancient times, it should be set at the lightest tax rate so that most of the salt profits belong to the people and are popularized. This is the final ending of thoroughly governing salt. Because the salt problem has a profound impact on everyone's interests, and looking around at people in the community, many still regard it indifferently. Since I know something, I cannot remain silent, so I do not hesitate to speak in detail. The people of the country should pay attention to it.

Education and Broadcasting Special Issue Wang

Citizen and the Law (Part 2) 54

— Lin Bin, Member of the Legislative Yuan

(Lectures given to the national public on October 30th and October 1st)

(4) The Rights People Should Legally Enjoy

What is called a right? A right is the power granted by law to a specific person to enrich their recognized interests. To break it down into two aspects: The content of a right is the interest recognized by law. The form of a right is the power granted by law. With this legal power, one can thoroughly assert their claims and obtain legal benefits. The rights enjoyed by the people are diverse, with the most important ones stipulated in the constitution. The constitutions of various countries are generally similar. The constitutional provisions regarding the rights of the people are sometimes designed solely to restrict the executive and judicial powers to prevent them from infringing upon the people. Others are designed solely to restrict the legislative power to prevent it from infringing upon the people. In most countries, the constitutional articles include phrases such as "the freedom of the people shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law," and "the people shall have a certain freedom within the scope of the law." These wordings are designed to restrict the executive and judicial powers because the enactment of laws is the prerogative of the legislative body. If the legislative body has not enacted a specific law to restrict the rights of the people, the executive or judicial bodies have no basis to arbitrarily restrict the rights of the people through orders or judgments. The U.S. Constitution, in its amendments added in 1791, states that "Congress shall make no law abridging the freedom of speech, or of the press; or the right of the people peaceably to assemble, and to petition the Government for a redress of grievances." Article 25 of the Draft Constitution of the Republic of China states that "laws restricting the rights and freedoms of the people shall be limited to those necessary to safeguard national security, avert imminent danger, maintain social order, or promote public interest." These wordings are designed to restrict the legislative power because, although the legislative body has the power to enact laws, it shall not arbitrarily enact laws to restrict any freedom or right of the people if such restriction is not necessary. If the executive, judicial, or legislative bodies violate these provisions, the laws they enact shall be invalid, and the dispositions or judgments they make shall be revoked. The people, for the harm they suffer as a result, may also request compensation in accordance with the law. This is what is meant by the statement that rights are protected by the constitution. The Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage of the Republic of China and the draft constitution prepared by the Legislative Yuan stipulate the basic rights of the people, which can be divided into the following categories:

1. The right to equality, which means that all citizens of the Republic of China are equal before the law, regardless of gender, race, religion, or class. The meaning of equality has already been discussed above.

2. The right to freedom, which means the right of the people to be free from interference in their person, property, speech, etc., except within the scope prescribed by law. The person of the people shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of the person. Any disposition of arrest or detention made without legal basis, or any disposition made without following the procedures prescribed by law even if there is a law, is an illegal disposition. The public officials who make such illegal dispositions shall be liable under the Disciplinary Law, the Criminal Law, and the Civil Law. The residences of the people shall not be entered, searched, or sealed except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of residence. For example, if a prosecutor or judicial police officer searches the residence of a person or seals their residence, they shall do so in accordance with the Criminal Procedure Law and other relevant laws and regulations. Any violation of this is an infringement on the freedom of the people, and they shall also be liable under the Disciplinary, Criminal, and Civil Laws. The movement of the people shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of movement. People should be allowed to move freely as necessary for their livelihood in order to achieve a satisfactory life. Restrictions may be imposed in accordance with the law only when necessary. For example, prohibiting the movement of people with infectious diseases in accordance with laws and regulations to prevent the spread of infection is one example. People's freedom of religious belief shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of religion. Freedom of religion originally includes both freedom of belief and freedom of religious practice. Pure belief is a psychological activity that cannot be externally enforced. One cannot be forced to believe or not to believe. As for religious practices, such as attending religious services and spreading religious doctrines, they are also free in principle. However, if these practices are used as a pretext to disrupt society or offend public morals, the state may naturally intervene. To say that religious belief has absolute freedom and is absolutely unrestricted by law is a misunderstanding. Therefore, the wording of the draft constitution differs slightly from the Provisional Constitution. The freedom of speech, writing, and publication of the people shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of speech, writing, and publication. Speech refers to speeches, talks, debates, etc. Writing refers to the production of documents, paintings, etc. Publication refers to the printing and distribution of documents, paintings, etc. These three are all methods by which human beings express their thoughts. Thought is an essential element for promoting civilization and social development, and the freedom of thought of each person should be recognized. However, speech, writing, and publication may be restricted if they endanger public order or harm the state. Therefore, the Criminal Law, the Emergency Penalties Law for Endangering the Republic of China, and the Publication Law contain explicit restrictions. The private communications of the people shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of private communication. Communication refers to expressing intentions by means of telegrams, telephones, letters, etc. Private refers to a situation where it is more advantageous not to be known to others or not to be known to the majority. If people express their intentions through communication and wish to keep them private, the state has no reason to interfere. However, in order to protect the interests of the state and society, restrictions may sometimes be imposed in accordance with the law. For example, inspecting mail and telecommunications in accordance with martial law, inspecting letters of criminals in accordance with the Criminal Procedure Law, and inspecting letters of bankrupts in accordance with the Bankruptcy Law are all legal. The assembly and association of the people shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of assembly and association. Assembly refers to a temporary gathering of many people, and association refers to a permanent group of many people. The thoughts of many people are exchanged, compromised, and expressed through assembly, which is indeed of great importance to communal life. Since the freedom of individuals to express their thoughts through speech has already been permitted, then assembly and association, which are merely ways to gather and express the thoughts of the people, must also be permitted. Assemblies and associations may have political purposes or non-political purposes. The laws of various countries often impose stricter restrictions on assemblies and associations with political purposes. In China, during the period of political tutelage, assemblies and associations must first obtain permission from the local party headquarters, must comply with the provisions of the Organizational Regulations for People's Organizations, and must not violate the provisions of the Criminal Law and the Emergency Penalties Law for Endangering the Republic of China. As for the police, they may supervise them for the purpose of maintaining public order, which goes without saying. The property of the people shall not be examined or confiscated except in accordance with the law. This is the freedom of property. Property is the material basis for the livelihood of the people. No illegal interference shall be made in any aspect of property rights. Even sealing or confiscation must have a legal basis. For example, requisitioning the land of the people in accordance with the Land Requisition Law and confiscating the property of the people in accordance with the Criminal Law are legal dispositions. In addition, there is freedom to choose employment and freedom to enter into contracts, which shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. The above is an analysis and explanation of the right to freedom.

3. The Right to Benefit. The right to benefit is the right of the people to enjoy special benefits from the state. Its purpose is to enjoy benefits, and it can require the state to take certain actions. It is active, not passive, and therefore different from the right to freedom. The right to freedom is passive, merely requiring the state not to interfere. If there are only passive rights without the active right to request the state to take certain actions, then the so-called right to freedom may be difficult to protect in practice. Therefore, the constitutions of various countries contain provisions regarding the right to benefit.

The scope of the right to benefit varies from country to country. Generally speaking, it can be divided into four types. One is the right to benefit in judicial matters, such as the right to civil and criminal litigation. Litigation can be brought to the judicial authorities in accordance with the provisions of the procedural law. The judicial authorities must then adjudicate the case. Another is the right to benefit in administrative matters, such as the right to bring administrative lawsuits, file petitions, or make requests. If the disposition of a public official is illegal and harms the rights of the people, the people may file a petition. If they are still not satisfied after the petition, they may bring an administrative lawsuit. As for the facilities of the state's political affairs, the people may also state their wishes to the state, which is called a request. Another is the right to benefit in education. Educational opportunities are equal for all people. Children of school age have the right to demand free education, and out-of-school people have the right to demand supplementary education. Private schools may request encouragement and subsidies, and school teachers and staff may request encouragement and protection. These are all benefits that can be enjoyed in education. Another is the right to benefit in economic matters. For example, poor people have the right to receive relief, and working people have the right to receive special protection. Special industries have the right to receive encouragement and protection. These are all rights that the people can be protected by the state in terms of livelihood.

4. The Right to Participate in Politics. The right to participate in politics is the right of the people to participate in the political affairs of the state, which is different from other rights that are exercised solely for individual benefit. On the one hand, it is called the right to participate in politics, and on the other hand, it can also be called the obligation to participate in politics. The types of political participation rights stipulated in the constitutions of most countries are limited to the right to vote and the right to hold public office. According to the Founding Program of the National Government of China, the people have four political participation rights in addition to the right to take examinations: the right to elect, the right to recall, the right to initiate legislation, and the right to referendum. These four political rights can only be fully exercised by citizens after the promulgation of the constitution. The right to elect occupies a major position in the political participation rights of the people. People can elect the members of the people's representative bodies. They can elect the administrative personnel. Even the highest administrative head must be elected by the people. Because there is the right to elect, the spirit of democratic politics can be realized. The right to recall is the right of the people to directly remove members of state organs or officials, which complements the right to elect. If the elected members or officials are deemed to have violated the law or neglected their duties, they can be recalled in accordance with legal procedures. Because the people have this right, government personnel cannot neglect their duties and must faithfully represent the will of the people in order to seek the interests of the people. The right to initiate legislation is the right of the people to initiate a certain law or to change or abolish a certain law in accordance with public opinion. If the people believe that a certain matter cannot be handled without a certain good law, they must initiate legislation in accordance with public opinion. If the people believe that a certain law is harmful to the interests of the people, they must change or abolish the law in accordance with public opinion. This right to create and abolish laws is called the right to initiate legislation. The right to referendum is the right of the people to vote on the bills of the legislative body. If the people approve the bill, the law can be established. This is different from the right to initiate legislation. It does not create laws, but approves laws. The scope of which bills of the legislative body do not require a referendum and which must be submitted to a referendum by the people is determined by law. The political affairs of governing a country cannot only have the governance of people without the governance of law. The above-mentioned rights to elect and recall are methods for seeking the "governance of people." The rights to initiate legislation and referendum are methods for seeking the "governance of law." For a detailed explanation of good laws and beautiful intentions, please refer to Mr. Sun Yat-sen's lectures on political power.

The right to take examinations is the right of the people to take examinations. The state implements examinations in order to select talent and enable them to engage in public service. All people who have certain qualifications can take the examinations. The right to take examinations is also the right to voluntarily serve as a member of the government. Although it is the same as the four political rights mentioned earlier as a right to participate in politics, it is actually different. The four political rights mentioned earlier are the rights to manage the government. The right to take examinations is only the right to voluntarily obtain the qualifications of an official to be a member of the government.

The rights of the people that are explicitly stipulated in the constitution are roughly as described above. The following will discuss the obligations that the people should fulfill.

(5) The Obligations That People Should Legally Fulfill

The people are the constituent elements of the state. In order to achieve the purpose of the state, it is natural that they cannot simply enjoy rights without assuming obligations. The scope of the people's obligations to the state varies with the times. In the past era of individual liberalism, the constitution emphasized the protection of individual rights, so the scope of the people's obligations was relatively narrow. Later, legal concepts changed, and the protection of social interests became the main focus. As a result, the constitutions of various countries also expanded the scope of the people's obligations. The Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage of the Republic of China and the draft constitution of the Republic of China also have provisions on the obligations of the people, which can be divided into the following categories for discussion:

1. The obligation to pay taxes. It is natural that the state collects taxes from the people to pay for the expenses of governance. The obligation to pay taxes is a kind of responsibility for the people to bear the expenses of the state. Those with more resources pay more taxes, and those with fewer resources pay fewer taxes, which is still in line with the principle of equality. The people only have the obligation to pay taxes within the scope stipulated by law. Taxes and levies not stipulated by law are miscellaneous taxes and oppressive taxes, and cannot be called legal.

2. The obligation to perform military service. That is, the obligation to engage in military service to defend the state. The rise and fall of the state is the responsibility of every citizen. In order to maintain the survival of the state, the people must each assume military service. It also means that all citizens are soldiers. However, this refers to countries that adopt a conscription system. If a voluntary military service system is adopted, where soldiers are recruited, the so-called obligation of citizens to serve in the military may not be realized.

3. The obligation to perform public service. Public service includes official duties, labor services, etc. Although it is a right for civil servants to perform official duties, it can also be called an obligation. If lawfully appointed, one should be selfless and not forcibly shirk responsibility. When labor services are assigned according to law, such as building roads and dredging rivers, the people also have an obligation to obey. The so-called there is only social freedom, no individual freedom, is what this means.

4. The obligation to obey the actions of government agencies. When state government agencies legally perform their duties, the people have an obligation to obey. This is because government agencies are organs that exercise the power of governance. Obeying the lawful orders and dispositions of government agencies is obeying the power of governance, which is only natural.

The above discusses the obligations of the people stipulated in the constitution. The following will discuss:

(6) What is a state ruled by law?

For thousands of years, China has practiced autocratic monarchical politics. The will of the monarch was equivalent to the law, and the monarch could change the law. Whether there was a law or whether the law was appropriate was not considered important. This was a method of relying on people rather than on law, and emphasizing the governance of people rather than the governance of law. Most officials also acted expediently and arbitrarily. The obligations of the people were not subject to definite limitations, and the rights of the people were not subject to definite guarantees. When there were virtuous monarchs and good officials, they were not without a heart for the people and did things that benefited the people. However, virtuous monarchs and good officials were rare. Because the monarch and officials were not often good, and there was no definite law to restrain them in their actions and orders, they could give or take life and property at will. There was only the authority of the monarch and officials, and no benefit to the people. It was using the world to serve one person, without regard to the original purpose of the state. It cannot even be called the governance of people. The rule of law is even less of a consideration. The so-called rule of law is using law to govern the country, using law as a tool for governing the state. Not only must the organization and powers of state organs be stipulated by law, but all matters concerning the exercise of the power of governance must be in accordance with the law. The rights and obligations of the people to the state are clearly stipulated in law, and there are also definite laws and regulations to resolve the relations of rights and obligations between people. This is a method of relying on law and not emphasizing the governance of people. If the officials governing the country are competent, it would be good for everyone. Then, using good people to use good laws would be the best phenomenon in politics. In case of incompetence, the officials may not all be good, but with laws as a standard for their actions, they would not be allowed to abuse their power and do whatever they want, so politics would not necessarily be badly affected. If the rule of law is emphasized, the obligations of the people are limited to a certain extent, and the burdens are fair. The rights of the people are guaranteed by law, so that there will be no abuses such as class oppression. From the perspective of the state, only by respecting the law can it be open and honest, gain the sympathy of the people, and promote its policies. The old saying that there is only the governance of people without the governance of law is flawed. Which modern country that can stand on the world stage with honor does not emphasize the rule of law? The rule of law is superior to the governance of people. This can be believed. The following will discuss the last point:

(7) What kind of people should a modern state have?

Modern states all emphasize the rule of law. It can be said that those who do not emphasize the rule of law are not worthy of being called modern states. Generally speaking, the strength and weakness of a country and the excellence or inferiority of its politics are related to the strength and weakness and excellence or inferiority of its people. A strong and excellent people will not constitute a strong and excellent state, and will not produce good politics. Foreign countries and China both have governments and officials. Why can they respect the law and create a state ruled by law, while we cannot? Is it that our government and officials should be responsible, and our people have no responsibility? I think not. I think our people should also bear a great responsibility. We know that the people of a state ruled by law should have the cultivation of legal knowledge. The most important of these can be mentioned in two points. The first point is to know why people have rights. If a person has no responsibility in society and no mutual obligations in the crowd, then he has no legal status. The reason why a person is a person is entirely because he is a member of society, contributes to society, and exerts his efforts to share the goals and life of society with other people. His personal status comes from society's recognition of him as a member. His rights can only exist because of the recognition of society. In other words, the reason why the law protects the life, property, and interests of individuals is because they are related to society. Protecting the interests of individuals is protecting the interests of society. If an individual is completely unrelated to social life, such a person has no legal significance. Understanding this point, then every person, every citizen, should first fulfill his obligations, not forget his relationship to society and the state, and all want to serve society and the state. If everyone has this thought and this spirit, is there still a country that is not united and not progressive? The second point is to know what constitutes a violation of the law. The distinction between violating the law and not violating the law is indeed a difficult matter, but in general, there should be a general understanding. When there is an obligation that should be fulfilled, one knows that it should be fulfilled by law, and will not delay or make excuses. When there is a right that should be enjoyed, one knows that it should be enjoyed by law, and will not give up or willingly suffer bullying. When there are orders from government agencies and dispositions from officials, one knows that they are legal and will naturally obey and comply. One knows that they are illegal and will have legitimate claims. When one is handling public affairs, one knows to adhere to the principle of handling them according to law and will not have illegal behavior. If everyone has this ability to distinguish and this ability, are there still people who are not sound and law-abiding? Are there still public officials who are unscrupulous and corrupt? From this, it can be seen that the foundation of a state ruled by law lies in the legal knowledge of the people. It goes without saying that citizens should have legal knowledge. China is to keep pace with modern states on the track of the rule of law. If our people are willing to pay more attention to legal knowledge, then there will be faster progress, and the future of the rule of law is very promising. (End)

Local News

Establishment of the Currency Reserve Management Committee Following the Ministry of Finance's Mandate of Legal Tender 55

Yesterday, regulations were stipulated for the implementation of legal tender in various regions. The British ambassador instructed his bank and nationals to cooperate with us, and the money industry was instructed to announce fixed prices for subsidiary coinage.

The Ministry of Finance announced yesterday that the banknotes of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications would be designated as legal tender, and cash would no longer be allowed to circulate. Violators would have all funds confiscated to prevent silver smuggling and leakage. Furthermore, a Currency Reserve Management Committee was established to manage the legal tender reserve. It held its first meeting yesterday at 5:00 PM, announcing the establishment of a silver and money industry association. Emergency meetings were held the previous evening and yesterday afternoon, respectively, resolving to comply. The money industry issued a public notice, instructed to announce fixed prices for subsidiary coinage. The Foreign Exchange Stabilization Committee announced yesterday morning that the stabilization tax rate would be 57.25%. The silversmiths' association resolved to request remedies. Details are provided below.

First Meeting of the Reserve Committee

The Currency Reserve Management Committee held its first meeting yesterday at 5:00 PM on the third floor of the Central Bank. The attendees included committee members Kong Xiangxi, Xu Kan, Yu Zuoyan, Wang Xiaolai, He Zhongxiao, Qin Runqing, Song Ziwen, Song Hanzhang, Hu Bijang, Tang Shoumin, Xu Xinliu, Ye Zhuotang, Du Yuesheng, Qian Xinzhi, Song Ziliang, Zhang Gongquan, Li Jue, Chen Guangfu, and Li Fusun, totaling nineteen people. Minister Kong, in his capacity as President of the Central Bank, chaired the meeting. First, Chairman Kong delivered a speech (attached later). Then, in accordance with Article 4 of the regulations, Song Ziwen, Hu Bijang, Chen Guangfu, Qian Xinzhi, and Li Jue were elected as executive committee members. Furthermore, as stipulated in Article 9 of the regulations promulgated by the Ministry, the meeting was to draft the rules of procedure for the committee. Song Hanzhang, Zhang Gongquan, Tang Shoumin, Xu Xinliu, Li Fusun, Li Jue, and Xu Kan were appointed as drafting committee members, to be convened by Committee Member Xu Kan. The meeting then adjourned.

Kong's Explanation of the Committee's Mission

Minister Kong, in his capacity as President of the Central Bank, delivered a speech, stating, "Today is the first meeting of this committee. The mission of this committee has a significant relationship with China's financial and economic history. Regarding the reform measures, the detailed announcement has already been made public, and you all are aware of it, so there is no need to elaborate. However, everything must have a good foundation to gradually develop and flourish. How to consolidate the credit of legal tender, stabilize foreign exchange, revitalize industry and commerce, and revive the economy in the future all depend on the efforts of this committee. The government's organization of this committee is for this reason. You are all domestic financial leaders, so you have been specially appointed as members of this committee, bearing this mission. I hope everyone will do their best and work together to achieve this grand plan for the benefit of the country and the people."

Ministry's Regulations on Currency Exchange Procedures in Various Regions

Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance sent a letter to the Central Bank (Shanghai Money Character No. 61), and also instructed various bank associations, money industry associations, chambers of commerce, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, all tax revenue agencies under the Ministry's direct control, financial commissioners in various provinces, and financial departments, stating, "The Ministry announced today that, starting from November 4th, the banknotes issued by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications would be designated as legal tender. All payments and receipts for taxes and all public and private funds shall be limited to legal tender, and cash shall not be used. Violators will have their funds confiscated. It is also stipulated that those holding silver coins, raw silver, and other silver types shall exchange them for legal tender." These announcements and instructions have been issued separately. However, considering that China has a vast territory and transportation is often inconvenient, the banknotes of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, and other bank notes, may not be circulating in all regions. In order to facilitate the people of various regions and to effectively implement the announcement regulations, the Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and various banks are hereby instructed to quickly transport legal tender to various regions so that there is sufficient supply. In areas where it is temporarily impossible to exchange for legal tender, the existing customs of the market may be temporarily maintained. The various associations and tax revenue agencies shall temporarily collect and exchange silver coins, raw silver, and other silver types, and transport the collected silver coins, raw silver, and other silver types to areas with legal tender for exchange, so as to avoid inconvenience to the people's daily use. The Central Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the various banks, associations, and chambers of commerce must further carefully plan convenient ways for the people and effectively implement laws and regulations based on the actual situation of the local area, and consult with the local government at any time to handle the matter. National laws are originally intended to benefit the people, and the Ministry will take into consideration any slight difficulties and address them accordingly. It is hoped that everyone will adhere to this principle, earnestly handle the matter, and report back." This is addressed to (Instruction). Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance also separately instructed the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to order local silver and money industry associations to investigate the inventory and cash reserves of various banks as of the 3rd and report them to the Ministry of Finance. The three banks have already separately instructed their respective branches in various regions to handle the matter.

State-Run Institutions to Exchange Coins

Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Railways, and the Ministry of Communications, and also sent letters to the Central Bank, various silver and money industry associations, chambers of commerce, and various banks, stating, "Currency is originally the standard for transactions. In ancient times, goods were exchanged for goods. Later, there were springs and cloths. With the increase in imports and exports and the growth of transactions, gold, silver, and copper were cast into coins. With the development of industry and commerce and the evolution of society, the number of credit currencies exceeded that of metal currencies. In modern civilized countries, there is no country that does not use banknotes instead of coins as the standard for transactions. The Ministry's decision to designate the banknotes of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications as legal tender is based on this principle. Considering that China has been using silver for a long time, and the population is large, savings are mostly in silver. At a time when new laws are being promulgated, remote areas may feel slightly inconvenienced, and the banknotes of the three banks may not have been widely circulated, or there may be cases where people holding silver coins and silver types have nowhere to exchange them for legal tender. The three banks, various banks, various money shops, various associations, various tax revenue agencies, and state-run enterprises, such as postal services, telegraph services, railways, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, and various bureaus, are hereby instructed to uniformly exchange them on behalf of the people, in order to facilitate the general public and provide a clear explanation, so as to dispel doubts and facilitate implementation. It is hoped that you will investigate and instruct your subordinates to comply." This is addressed to (You are to comply with this order immediately).

Instructing the Three Banks to Stabilize Foreign Exchange

Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance sent a letter to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications, stating, "On the 4th of this month, the Ministry announced six regulations, which have been communicated (ordered) to you. The three banks should be responsible for stabilizing foreign exchange rates. It is hoped that you will promptly observe the market situation and coordinate with the circumstances, so as not to allow any changes outside the norm. This is what is hoped for (this is of utmost importance)." This is addressed to (This order).

The Shanghai Municipal Government issued a proclamation yesterday, stating, "For the purpose of proclamation, it is found that the monetary policy announced by the Ministry of Finance on November 4th of this year is to seek the permanent stability of currency and finance, in order to achieve the goal of economic revival. All measures have been announced in detail by the Ministry of Finance. All our citizens should understand this principle and comply uniformly. Anyone who deliberately obstructs, spreads rumors, or attempts to speculate and raise prices will be severely arrested and dealt with without leniency. This proclamation."

Three Resolutions on Business Measures

Yesterday, the Banking Association issued a notice to various banks, stating, "Dear Sirs, today (the 4th) at noon, this association convened a temporary executive committee meeting to discuss banking business issues after the government stipulated the legal police. Two measures were resolved as follows: (1) From today onwards, the receipt and payment of funds will be limited to legal tender as stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, and cash shall not be used. (3) In the future, all kinds of bills issued by colleagues (such as fixed deposit certificates, promissory notes, etc.) should be uniformly marked with the words 'national currency' to show uniformity. At the same time, the Ministry of Finance's announcement was copied and distributed to various shops and announced in the market.

Foreign Banks Cooperate with Us

This time, the government, in order to stabilize the market and revive the economy, decided to avoid inflation by exploring central reserves, so that silver would not flow out, in order to consolidate the monetary system and improve finance. Since yesterday's implementation, the impression has been very good. The gold standard and the foreign exchange market have also been very stable. Now, foreign banks in this port, such as HSBC, have been ordered by the British government to work hard with our country and instruct HSBC banks and other British banks and nationals in various places to send all their inventory and holdings of silver coins to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to exchange banknotes for circulation. Regarding debt, they are also ordered to comply with our government's orders and not to pay in cash, otherwise they will be punished separately. It is heard that other foreign banks also exchanged banknotes for cash with the three banks yesterday, and the number was quite large. This policy of bank employees will undoubtedly benefit our national economy.

Announcement by British Ambassador Knatchbull-Hugessen

British Ambassador to China, Knatchbull-Hugessen, issued an announcement yesterday to prohibit the payment of silver. The translation is as follows. The original text reads, "For the purpose of notification, the following regulations are hereby formulated by this Ambassador. It is necessary to copy and issue them to your people for uniform compliance. Do not violate them. This announcement is made by British Ambassador to China, Knatchbull-Hugessen, November 4, 1935. The Prohibition of Payment of Silver Regulations of 1935, No. 2, are hereby promulgated in accordance with the granting of powers under Article 209 of the "Six An Act Concerning China" of 1925. Whereas the National Government of the Republic of China has ordered the nationwide prohibition of the use of cash silver, and the use of cash silver is an illegal act. Furthermore, in accordance with the Extraterritoriality Acts of 1890 and 1913, and the Act Concerning China of 1925, this Ambassador may formulate various regulations to manage the people of this country so that they can live and work in peace. Now, in order to promote the implementation of the aforementioned order issued by the Chinese government, the following regulations are hereby formulated. All legal persons, firms, and companies under the jurisdiction of the Supreme Court of this country shall comply without violation. (1) In these regulations, the term "legal person" refers to people, firms, and companies of British nationality residing in China, doing business in China, or within the scope of the aforementioned Act Concerning China of 1925. (2) Anyone who, alone or jointly with other British or non-British people, repays all or part of a debt with cash silver shall be deemed to have violated the law and shall be subject to imprisonment for up to three months, or with hard labor, or a fine of up to fifty pounds, or both imprisonment and a fine. (3) These regulations shall be named the Prohibition of Payment of Cash Silver Regulations of 1935. According to this decree, silver clauses in British bonds, leases, or other financial instruments are all illegal. In short, the central government has ordered the recovery of circulating silver and made it state-owned, and made the Chinese government's paper currency the legal tender for public and private obligations. Therefore, British commercial banks can have the right not to pay any silver. The effect of this move is indeed not insignificant."

Market Announcement of Subsidiary Coinage Prices

The Ningbo Road Money Market, in addition to announcing the Ministry of Finance's announcement yesterday morning, also issued an announcement on the fixed prices for subsidiary coinage. The announcement stated, "For the purpose of notification, by face-to-face instruction from the Minister of Finance, starting from October 4th, the price of subsidiary coinage shall be limited to twelve cents per standard coin, and no increase or decrease is allowed. This is specially notified to you for compliance." Therefore, the transaction of the market is different from the past, and in the future, it will be in accordance with this price, without increase or decrease.

Soaring Exchange Rates for Subsidiary Coins and Copper Coins

The money market announced yesterday that the price of Jiangnan and Guangdong subsidiary coins was 10,000 cents per 833.33 yuan, and 300,000 copper coins per 100 yuan. However, the exchange rate of 100 yuan for copper coins in the Nanshi, Zhabei, Pudong, Public Concession, and French Concession exchange shops was not uniform. The maximum was 12 cents per yuan, and the minimum was 10 cents, 240 wen, and 200 wen. The maximum for copper coins per yuan was 3,000 wen, and the minimum was 2,800 wen.

Three Banks Busy Exchanging Banknotes

After the Ministry of Finance officially announced that cash silver was state-owned, and that the banknotes issued by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications were legal tender, and that cash silver was not allowed to be used in the market to prevent outflow, various industries such as the silver and money industry, and merchants, all held silver coins to the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications to exchange for banknotes. They came and went in large numbers, and the staff of the three banks were very busy. It is expected that the number of people who will request to exchange for legal tender in the future will be even more enthusiastic.

Stabilization Tax Rate Higher Than Before

The Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee announced the equalization tax rate at 10:00 AM yesterday through the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications committee members Xi Demao, Bei Songsun, and Zhang Peishen at the Central Bank's Business Bureau meeting, which was 57.25%, which was 50.5% more than the equalization tax rate of 6.75% announced the day before.

Central Bank Announces Exchange Rates

The Central Bank announced the following telegraphic transfer buying rates this morning: (1) One British pound per national currency yuan is one shilling two and a half pence, (2) One hundred national currency yuan per New York is US$29.75, (3) One hundred national currency yuan per Paris is 450 French francs, (4) One hundred national currency yuan per Berlin is 73.5 marks, (5) One hundred national currency yuan per Japan is 103 Japanese yen, (6) One hundred national currency yuan per Hong Kong is 71 Hong Kong dollars, (7) Each customs gold unit has 2.276 national currency yuan, 33 British pence, and US$0.6775.

Silversmiths' Association Resolves to Seek Remedy

The Ministry of Finance stipulates that all silver and money shops, firms, and other public and private institutions or individuals holding silver standard coins or common silver coins, raw silver, and other such items, should be handed over to the Currency Reserve Management Committee or its designated bank to exchange for legal tender starting from November 4th. The Mint Still Operating as Usual

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency learned from the Central Mint yesterday morning that the factory is still operating normally, casting factory bars and silver coins every day. After the inspection committee inspects and approves the factory bars and silver coins cast, they will all be handed over to the Currency Reserve Management Committee as issuance reserves.

Ambassador Jiang Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 56

Took the Overnight Train to Beijing to Attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee; President Wang's Son Returned Home on the Same Ship to Visit Relatives

According to the Central News Agency, Ambassador Jiang Zuobin, our country's ambassador to Japan, returned to China on the Asia Queen, a ship of the Changxing Shipping Company, from Japan at 7:20 AM on the 4th, accompanied by Wang Xiuzhong, a staff member of the embassy, to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee. He took the train to Beijing that night. President Wang's son, Meng Jin, who went to Germany to study at the end of last month, learned about President Wang's assassination attempt in Beijing when he passed through Japan. On the morning of the 4th, he also returned to Shanghai on the same ship and took the early express train to Beijing to visit his father. The details are as follows:

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning

The Asia Queen entered the port early in the morning. At 6:30 AM, it docked at the Qichang Wharf in Pudong. The Jinghui special ship, which was welcoming Ambassador Jiang, departed from the New Customs Wharf at 6:30 AM. Those who went to welcome him included Yu Ming, the director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office, Zhao Tiezhang, the section chief, Sun Liping, the secretary, Zhou Xuan, the representative of the municipal government, Yu Hongrun, the director of the foreign affairs section of the Public Security Bureau, and Wang Zhinan, the representative of the municipal security office. Ambassador Jiang shook hands and thanked them one by one. Then, he boarded the Jinghui special ship at 7:20 AM, returned to the New Customs Wharf, disembarked, and took a car to the International Hotel to rest.

Ambassador Jiang's Speech

According to Ambassador Jiang, when he arrived in Shanghai, he said to the reporters of various newspapers in the round that his return to China this time was to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, so he would not stay in Shanghai and would go to Beijing that day to report to the central government on his mission to Japan. Before leaving Japan, he met with the Japanese authorities to bid farewell. He also talked about the Sino-Japanese issue during the meeting. The opinions of the two countries are now very close. Ambassador Jiang continued to talk about the news of President Wang's assassination attempt, which he learned about in Nagasaki. At that time, there were various rumors in Japan. He learned from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegram that President Wang's injuries were not serious, and his heart was slightly relieved. As for the date of his return to office, it has not yet been decided.

Went to Beijing Last Night

Ambassador Jiang and his party of five took the night express train to Beijing at 11:00 PM last night to attend the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Committee and pay respects to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to report. When Ambassador Jiang arrived in Shanghai, he was very concerned about President Wang's injuries, so he planned to visit him immediately after arriving in Beijing. As for President Wang's son, Meng Jin, who went abroad at the end of last month, originally planned to go to Germany via Japan to study. Unexpectedly, when he passed through Japan, he learned about President Wang's assassination attempt, so he hurriedly returned to China with Ambassador Jiang. After disembarking, he went straight to the North Railway Station to take the early express train to his hometown to visit his father.
