Niu Huilin Returns to Shanghai and Talks 59

President Wang's injuries are very good. Noel goes to Beijing to diagnose internal disorders.

According to the Central News Agency, after President Wang was shot in Beijing, he was sent to the Central Hospital for treatment. Because the bullet lodged in the intercostal space has not yet been removed, a special telegram was sent to orthopedic surgery masters Niu Huilin and Miller, requesting both doctors to take a plane from Shanghai and Guangdong to Beijing on the 3rd to diagnose and treat Wang, so as to restore his health as soon as possible. After Niu and Miller arrived in Beijing and diagnosed Wang once, they took the night express train out of Beijing that evening and arrived in Shanghai at 7:15 a.m. yesterday. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Niu at his clinic. According to him, President Wang's injuries have been progressing well since Liu Ruiheng and Shen Kefei devoted their efforts day and night to treatment. The swelling on his face has gradually subsided, and he is in good spirits, but his appetite is slightly less. The bullet lodged in the intercostal space is currently not convenient to be removed surgically. According to my experience, the bullet remaining in the body is not dangerous, so it doesn't matter whether the bullet is removed or not. President Wang suffers from diabetes, and his old illness has been newly cured, and he has suffered this injury, so more attention should be paid to treatment and recuperation. Dr. Noel, who has been treating Wang's internal disorders, has already set off from Bao Cheng and is flying to Beijing, where he will arrive on the 4th to diagnose and treat Wang, so as to improve his appetite and restore his health as soon as possible. The Central Hospital does not receive visitors to President Wang, except for those with special permission, so that he can rest peacefully. The hospital has also assigned three nurses to take turns day and night to care for him by his bedside. Wang's relatives live on both sides of the ward, and a telephone has been installed to report his injuries to the outside world at any time. All the facilities are very complete, he said. Mr. Niu also plans to go to Beijing again in the coming days.

China Merchants Liangjiang Ship Aground in Liuhe Yesterday 60

Jiangxin has been rescued and returned to Shanghai. Jianxian is currently being towed.

There was fog on the sea outside Wusongkou yesterday. The state-run China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze River ships, Jian Guo and Jiang Xin, ran aground at the mouth of Liuhe one after the other. The Shanghai General Bureau only received a special telegram from the Navy Department at noon and immediately sent a ship to rescue them. In the evening, the Jiang Xin ship had already been towed out and returned to Shanghai, while the Jian Guo ship had not yet left the shoal and was still being rescued.

Jian Guo Encountered Fog and Ran Aground

The Jian Guo has a load capacity of 2,770 tons, registered as 1,588 tons. The ship is 278 feet and 2 inches long, 42 feet and 9 inches wide, and has a draft of 12 feet. It was built in 1905. On the 3rd of this month, it was fully loaded with goods and passengers in Shanghai and set off for the Yangtze River. It left Jinliyuan Wharf at 2:00 a.m. on the 4th. By the time it left Wusongkou, it was already after 5:00 a.m. At that time, the fog outside Songkou was very heavy, making navigation extremely difficult. Captain Huang Youshi has always been careful, so when sailing to Liuhe port, near a place called Spit Buoy, about nine nautical miles from Wusong, he went off course in the heavy fog, causing the ship to run aground on a sandy beach. The captain tried to reverse the ship to try to get out on its own, but because the draft was deep and the ship was heavily loaded, the bottom of the ship was stuck in the shallow sand and could not move, losing its sailing ability.

Jiang Xin's Rescue Also Runs Aground

The China Merchants Bureau's Yangtze River ship Jiang Xin, which was returning to Shanghai from Hankou, passed by Liuhe yesterday and discovered that the Jian Guo was aground. After Jiang Xin inquired, Jian Guo asked Jiang Xin to come forward to help and tow it off the shoal. Jiang Xin stopped and sailed to where Jian Guo was aground, intending to use a wire cable to hold Jian Guo and try to tow it down. However, the draft there was very shallow, and Jiang Xin was also heavily loaded. Before it had sailed near Jian Guo, it itself ran aground. Although the situation was lighter than that of Jian Guo, it had also lost its ability to move, causing both Yangtze River ships to run aground.

Qingtian Warship Asks for Help

The Qingtian surveying ship of the Navy Department's Hydrographic Bureau sailed to the outside of Wusongkou after noon yesterday. Seeing that the Jiang Guo of Jian Guo was aground in Liuhekou, it sailed closer to inquire. The captains of the two ships asked it to send an urgent telegram to the Shanghai General Bureau on their behalf, requesting that a ship be sent to tow them. The Qingtian warship did so. This telegram was sent to the Navy Headquarters, and at 12:00 noon, the Navy Headquarters forwarded it to the China Merchants Bureau, instructing it to quickly go to the rescue. After receiving the report, the bureau immediately sent a ship to tow them.

Baohe's Rescue Fails

The British-owned Jardine Matheson's Baohe ship was returning to Shanghai from Yichang and Hankou yesterday. After passing the outside of Wusongkou, it discovered that Jiang Xin and others were aground and unable to move. When the Baohe ship approached, Jiang Xin asked it to help tow it. The Baohe ship had the intention of helping with navigation, so it went forward to tow it. However, the tide was ebbing at that time, and the water was very shallow. The Baohe ship failed to tow the Jiang Xin ship, so it sailed to Shanghai. Another ship sent by the China Merchants Bureau went to tow.

Jiang Xin Leaves Shoal and Arrives in Shanghai

After the bureau received the telegram from the Navy Headquarters, it contacted Kang Zhengji about a tugboat and rushed to rescue the two Yangtze River ships. Kang Zhengji dispatched the Beiyang tugboat with the largest horsepower, which rushed from Shanghai to Wusong at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. After arriving at the mouth of Liuhe, it first towed Jiang Xin. The Beiyang had great towing power and a shallow draft. When it went to tow Jiang Xin, it was also high tide, so Jiang Xin was towed out of the shoal. Because Jiang Xin's hull was not damaged, it sailed back to Shanghai on its own. It had already returned to Shanghai at around 5:00 p.m. and arrived at Jinliyuan Wharf to unload passengers and goods.

Jian Guo is Being Towed

The Beiyang tugboat is currently towing the Jian Guo ship. Because the place where Jian Guo ran aground is shallower than the Jiang Xin ship, the towing work is relatively more laborious. According to the bureau's spokesman, it is generally expected to be rescued. At the latest, it will be able to be towed away from the shoal this morning. If the Jian Guo's hull is not badly damaged, it will still be ordered to go upstream to Hankou and not return to Shanghai to avoid delaying the schedule.

Ministry of Finance Approves: Red Account Statements Do Not Need Stamps 64

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce notified all members yesterday: Previously, the association stated that stores issue various items of deposits and debts at the end of each year for shareholders to review, called red account statements. This is completely different from the account statements in Article 3 of the Stamp Tax Law Tax Rate Table. According to the law, it seems that there is no need to affix stamps. The Ministry of Finance was requested to verify and instruct. Now, on the 2nd of this month, the Ministry of Finance's Tax Character No. 7680 instructed that: Qing Dai Dian rest assured that the red account statements issued by stores after the end of each year to send various items of deposits and debts to shareholders for review are different in nature from the account statements given to customers as proof of payment. Naturally, there is no need to affix stamps. We should be informed, so we recorded the approval and notified, and we hope that we will check and inform, and send separate letters to the same industry to let them know.

It was decided that Chairman Shen would be sent to Lianna Foreign Firm to demand payment first. If there is no satisfactory solution, all factories will be notified to stop trading with Lianna Foreign Firm. It was decided to stop all shipments to them. The meeting adjourned at 8 o'clock.

Devouring Puffer Fish Three People Died Tragically 71

Those Who Heard It Could Not Help But Feel Sad

Zhou Agen, a native of Changshu, who lived at No. 1, Lane 5, Zhangjiabang Road, Pudong, was 56 years old. He used to run a distiller's shop, but after the shop closed, he worked on a ship. He is now unemployed. His wife, Ms. Feng, is 41 years old and from the same hometown as Zhou. His son, Rong Sheng, is 14 years old and is still studying. Zhou has a friend named Wu Zigen, nicknamed Little Wuxi, who works as a watchman at the nearby Changde Oil Factory. On the morning of the previous day, Wu bought two puffer fish in Puxi for 1,200 yuan and took them to Zhou's house to cook and eat. At lunch, Zhou and Wu drank and devoured the fish, and Ms. Feng also ate a lot of fish. Only Zhou's son, Rong Sheng, refused to eat it. Unexpectedly, at about 1:00 p.m., Wu suddenly felt severe abdominal pain and his expression changed drastically. After a while, he fell to the ground and died. Zhou then felt pain and knew that he had been poisoned by the fish. He immediately hired a car to rush to Pudong Hospital for treatment. After arriving at the hospital, his poisoning had worsened and he became unconscious. The hospital doctor determined that it was too late to save him and ordered the driver to pull him back. Before he could reach home, he died on the way. At this time, Zhou's wife, Ms. Feng, also felt severe abdominal pain. Seeing the danger of her husband and Wu, she rushed to a hospital across from the Great World on Edward Road for treatment. She died at 11:00 p.m. that night. After the tragedy occurred, Director Yang of the Yangjiadu Police Station ordered Internal Affairs Police Chief Dai Guanqing to go to investigate. He ordered the local security guard, Yang Baobao, to report to the local court, which appointed Prosecutor Zhang to come to the scene to examine the bodies of Wu and Zhou and determine that they had died from poisoning. Because Wu's body had no family members, it was ordered to be collected by the Charity Hall. Zhou's body was ordered to be collected by his brother and sister-in-law with a coffin, and another coffin was prepared to go to Puxi Hospital to collect Ms. Feng's body and carry it back to Pudong so that she could be buried with her husband. The incident caused a sensation in the neighborhood, and the spectators could not help but feel sad.

Mother and Daughter Commit Suicide by Poison 73

No Means of Livelihood, Economic Hardship, Deeply Affected by Poison, Life Difficult to Save

A Chaozhou woman, Qian Chen, 38 years old, has a daughter named Yuying, 17 years old. Since her husband's death and due to rural bankruptcy in recent years, life has been difficult. She and her daughter came to Shanghai to make a living, residing at the home of her brother, Chen Xincheng, at No. 4, Lane 551, North Shansi Road. Recently, due to her daughter's inability to find work, coupled with her brother's business failure and economic hardship, conflicts arose between the sister-in-law and the mother and daughter, and they both conceived a desire to end their lives. The other day (the 3rd), at about 1 pm, Wang Yuying went alone to the Eastern Hotel on Tibet Road, intending to book a room. The receptionist led her to the sixth floor and booked Room 606. The tea boy, Hu Qian, took out a pencil and asked the woman to write down her name, age, and place of origin. Wang Yuying took the pen and wrote "Wang Yuying, 17 years old, Suzhou." The tea boy, noticing that Wang's accent was not Wu dialect, questioned her. Wang claimed to have lived in Shanghai for a long time. The tea boy then asked her to write "local." Seeing that Yuying's hands were trembling and she looked flustered, fearing something was amiss, he politely refused and told her to book a room elsewhere. Yuying resentfully went to the fifth floor and booked Room 507 in the east wing, paying the rent. She went out and returned in the evening with an old woman (Wang Yuying's biological mother, Wang Chen), about 40 years old, to the room, where they ate dinner together. At around 9 pm, Yuying left. Her mother closed the door and went to bed. At 10 am yesterday, the tea boy called the room (Room 507 had a private phone) because the occupant had not opened the door. After a long time without an answer, he pried open the door and found the woman lying on the bed. She had new shoes on her feet. The bedding was stained with vomit after taking poison. Three empty bottles of sleeping pills were beside the pillow. When called, her limbs were cold, but her chest was still warm. The tea boy informed the cashier, who immediately reported to the Old Zhabei Police Station. An ambulance was dispatched and sent to Renji Hospital at about 11 am. When the car arrived at the hospital, Wang Yuying, who had booked the room at the Eastern Hotel yesterday, had also been sent to the hospital by a Xiang Sheng taxi due to poisoning. After emergency treatment by Western doctors, both mother and daughter were deeply affected by the poison, and their lives are feared to be unsalvageable.

Where Did the Bullets Come From in the Piano Factory? The Carpenter Severely Injured 74

Bullets Hit Head, Chest, Etc., Blood Flowing, Sent to Hospital for Treatment

In the Qin Chang Piano Factory on Peekel Road, a 29-year-old carpenter from Ningbo named Li Houfu was working. Yesterday, at around 6 pm, when Li Houfu was sawing wood in the workshop, a loud noise suddenly erupted from under the wood when he swung an axe. At the same time, Li Houfu fell to the ground. Factory staff rushed to investigate and found Li lying on the ground, bleeding profusely, with wounds all over his head and chest. Not knowing how he was injured, they quickly reported to the police station and sent him to the hospital for treatment. An investigation revealed that he had been injured by bullets. However, the origin of the bullets is unknown. The police have summoned the factory owner for questioning.

Murder Case in Caojiadu 75

Suspects Apprehended Within Two Hours

Yesterday morning at about 8 am, a male corpse, chopped with an axe, was discovered in an open space at No. 22, west of Fushi Garden, Lysina Road, Caojiadu. The Caojiadu Police Station of Yidingpan Road received the report and immediately dispatched police to investigate. The deceased was about 30 years old, resembling a coolie, with seven or eight axe wounds on the back of his head and face. Beside the corpse was a blood-stained wooden stick and a rickshaw driver's license, number 3630, with a photo attached. Detective Team Leader Zhuang Dexiu, Deputy Leader Liu Shaoqing, and Detective Song Ziming carefully examined the scene and conducted an investigation based on the photo on the license. Within an hour, the main suspect, Zhang Xuebin, was apprehended. According to his confession, the deceased was named Xiao Ma San, from Funing, and earned a living by pulling a rickshaw. He had a feud with Cao Zigan and Xiao Haoliu for jointly stealing rickshaws. This morning, he was lured to the open space, where Zhang, Cao, and Xiao attacked him and killed him. The mistresses of Xiao and Cao, Wu Li, Cao Zhou, and Xiao Cao, were also arrested and taken to the station for interrogation. A local bailiff was dispatched to the court for an inquest.

Antique Broker Defrauds a Large Sum of Antiques 76

Sells Some, Pawns Others, Avoids Meeting, Finally Arrested

Gao Yunlong, from Nanjing, who works as an antique broker, went to the home of antique dealer Wang Zhongcai at No. 3, Lane 33, Houjiabang, Nanshi, on the 15th of last month. Claiming to sell on consignment, he obtained twelve ivory carvings of the Three Flower Gods and four beauties, valued at 525 yuan. On the 19th and 21st of the same month, he went to the Qiugu Antique Shop at No. 69, Jiangxi Road, and obtained eighteen ivory Arhats, eight ivory horses, and ivory statues of beauties, totaling 1,290 yuan, using the same words. After obtaining the above items, Gao sold some to Westerners and pawned others, using all the proceeds for himself. He avoided meeting with Wang Zhongcai and others. The day before yesterday afternoon, Wang Congren ran into Gao at the intersection of Rue Edouard VII and Luzon Road. He called the police, who arrested him and took him to the Central Police Station. Detective Wu Yaozu investigated him. According to Gao's confession, in addition to the items pawned and sold, several items were given to a Mr. Jiang, residing at No. 11, Anqingfang, Bansongyuan Road, and to Da Yingshan, a fellow villager at No. 14, Pingkangli, Rue Lanwei. Detectives went to arrest the two men. Jiang had fled, but Da was arrested and taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu explained the situation and requested a postponement for further investigation, stating that Gao's wife had handed over a pawn ticket for the stolen goods. The police are preparing to file a case. Judge Huang Risheng, after questioning the defendant, ordered a postponement for further interrogation. Gao Yunlong was detained, and Da was released on 200 yuan bail.

Aviation Association Recruitment Team's 32nd Administrative Meeting 77

Discuss Fundraising and Promotional Strategies; Exhibition Set for 10th in Southern Shanghai

The office of the general team leader of the Shanghai Municipal Recruitment Team of the Chinese Aviation Association held its 32nd administrative meeting the day before yesterday (the 2nd) at 4 pm to discuss fundraising and promotional strategies. Attendees included General Secretary Li Dachao, Secretaries Zhang Yuliang, Zhou Songhe, Wei Jianxin, Liu Songtao, Chen Shuo, Li Jimin, Song Zheng, Lu Zhangyan, Zhang Xiamin, Zhu Shengyang, Bao Lengxue, Gu Shangrui, Yang Peiwen, etc. General Secretary Li chaired the meeting, and Chen Shuo took the minutes. The chairman reported that the administrative meetings had been suspended four times in the past month due to the opening of the 6th National Games and the urgency of disaster relief work. He briefly reported on the work done during these four weeks. The Chinese Flying Club was formally established on Double Tenth Day and started operations at No. 146, Lane 1, Rue Lupan. Part of the fundraising proceeds was allocated to cover expenses. Secretary-General Yao and the chairman jointly oversaw the related matters. Currently, they are recruiting members, with a target of 5,000 people. Young people with potential, enthusiastic about saving the country, and deeply interested in aviation will be given training in flying skills to create grassroots civilian pilots. The location is the Longhua Flying School, which will start soon. During the National Games, the office organized the Chinese Aviation Association's Aviation and National Salvation Simple Exhibition in the city center sports field. Many secretaries and staff were assigned to take care of it. Although it only lasted ten days, it was visited by 200,000 to 300,000 people. The venue was almost impassable, which shows the city's compatriots' deep interest in aviation and national salvation. Shanghai has a population of over 3 million. During this time of national crisis, people should be made more aware of aviation and air defense. In order to popularize this, a simple mobile aviation and national salvation exhibition is being prepared. The city is divided into five areas: Southern Shanghai, Northern Shanghai, Eastern Shanghai, Western Shanghai, and the Special District. Each area's exhibition will last about 20 days, including preparation time. It has been decided that Southern Shanghai will be held first at the People's Education Center on Wenmiao Road, opening on the 10th of this month. The work of each recruitment team depends on the efforts of the team leaders, deputy team leaders, and team members. Reports of progress are encouraging. A circular has been issued for phased completion, and the teams are actively recruiting. The outside secretaries should assist in the process to increase progress and complete it as soon as possible. Also, all industries are working hard to collect aviation and national salvation donations based on business income. The results of the fundraising have been announced repeatedly. It is planned to launch the collection of aviation and national salvation donations from the shipping industry, and contacts have been made and are ready. It will start soon. In addition, the aviation variety show and antique auction will be held this month to raise funds for aviation and national salvation. After the reports from each outside secretary on the progress of contact and inspection, a number of fundraising and promotional plans were discussed. The meeting adjourned at 6 pm.

Artist Zhang Chongren Returns Home After Completing His Studies 86

Mr. Zhang Chongren, a native of Shanghai, studied painting at the St. Luke's Art Gallery in Xujiahui from a young age and possessed a remarkable artistic talent. He once served as an editor for the Illustrated Times and studied at the Shanghai Academy of Fine Arts for a long time. Four years ago, with the introduction of his uncle, Mr. Ma Xiangbo, and Mr. Chu Minyi and Mr. Wang Jingqi, he was recommended by the Sino-Belgian Geng款 Committee to study abroad and was admitted to the painting department of the Royal Academy of Fine Arts in Brussels. He also studied at the Fine Arts Department of the National University of Brussels. The following year, in the Royal Academy of Fine Arts painting competition, Mr. Zhang's works all ranked first or second, adding glory to the Chinese art world. Major newspapers in Brussels reported on the matter, and art magazines published his works, earning him widespread praise in the art world. The Chinese Embassy in Belgium specially awarded him an honorary certificate to encourage him. Mr. Zhang continued to study in the oil painting department, studied in the sculpture department, and was admitted to the National Chemical College to study industrial chemistry, hoping to contribute to production upon his return to China. During the summer vacation last summer, he went to Paris and admired the masterpieces of past generations in the National Museum. Five of his paintings of famous sights in Paris and two portraits were appreciated by the Sino-Belgian Geng款 Committee and selected for preservation by the Nanjing Central University Art Museum, which shows the excellence of his achievements. In June this summer, he obtained a diploma as a sculptor from the Belgian government and received a bonus of 3,000 francs. Mr. Zhang had been in Belgium for four years and made plans to return. Before returning east, he traveled to the capitals and famous cities of countries such as England, the Netherlands, Germany, and Italy, especially Florence and Rome in Italy, where he enjoyed the masterpieces of art from past generations, greatly broadened his horizons, and advanced his art. He boarded the Italian ship Count Rosso on October 11 in Venice and returned home. He arrived in Shanghai last night (the 4th). Friends and relatives who went to the Jianggan wharf to welcome him all requested to hold a solo art exhibition. Mr. Zhang said that since his luggage had just been unloaded, he would have to wait until it was organized before a date could be chosen.

Robbery Case: Robbers Sentenced to Five Years Each 87

Robbers Wu Junshou and Tang Naikun, both from Jiangbei, along with accomplices, committed armed robbery at Shan Nong Bamboo Shop, No. 80, Lane 20, Hejian Road, stealing goods worth over 300 yuan. They were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. French Police Arrest 13 Male and Female Armed Robbers; Seize Handguns, Bullets, Handcuffs, Iron Chains, etc. These Criminals Are Involved in Numerous Major Cases of Robbery and Kidnapping.

French Police Detective Jiang Futian received a tip on the 20th of last month and led detectives Wang Rusong, Zhang Daorong, Liu Jinrong, Guo Shaorong, and others to arrest Han Jinshu (21 years old, from Pudong) and Huang Caigen (23 years old, apprentice at a woolen suit shop at No. 101 Guba Road) near the intersection of Pingji Road and Lafayette Road. After questioning at the police station, based on Han’s confession, they went to No. 4 Shenyu Lane, Huacheng Road, north of Fangban Bridge, and arrested Jiang Zhian (also known as Jiang Wu, 25 years old), Jiang Anguo (20 years old, Jiang Wu’s younger brother), Wang Fuyan (20 years old), Li Jianzhi (25 years old), and others. In Jiang Zhian's room, they seized a handgun (No. 129100), 25 bullets, a pair of handcuffs, an iron chain, a handgun holster, a diamond ring, 235 yuan in cash, a gold-backed pearl ring, a Chinese Bank deposit slip for 1032 yuan, 14 pawn tickets, and 3 seals. They then proceeded to No. 5 Tongyi Lane, Beile Road, and arrested Ma Bosheng (45 years old, a detective in the First District of the Jiangsu Water Police Team in Minhang), seizing a handgun and 4 bullets, and brought them back to the police station for detention. Accompanied by detectives dispatched by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, they went to the Rixin Inn on Diandang Street in the Nanshi district, and escorted Lu Wangshi (43 years old), Lu Xiuying (20 years old), Wang Jingfang (25 years old), Wang A'er (48 years old), and Wang Kangzhang (49 years old) back to the police station. In total, 12 male and female robbery suspects, all from Nanhui and Fengxian, were arrested. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the First Criminal Court for interrogation. The police lawyer Chen stated that the defendants were arrested for robbery and kidnapping, and because the case was complex and involved many criminals, he requested a two-week extension for investigation before prosecution. Detective Liu Jinrong reported the arrest of the defendants and submitted the seized items as evidence. Jiang Zhian confessed that the handgun was sent to his house by Ma Bosheng, and the handcuffs and iron chain were found by his cousin when digging soil and kept at his house. The cash was entrusted to him by his maternal uncle to buy gold jewelry for his daughter's wedding, the deposit book belonged to his adopted grandfather Wang Yongxiang who sold cotton in the countryside and asked him to deposit the money in the bank, and the diamond ring and pearl ring belonged to his concubine. He denied committing robbery, but admitted to lending the handgun twice in the past. The first time, Yang Chunsheng, Jin Fusheng, Li Baorong, and Zhu Fuxiang went to rob No. 5 Xidou Lane, Ximen Road, and later gave him 150 yuan, of which he used 50 yuan and gave 100 yuan to Ma Bosheng. The second time he lent the gun, it was in a teahouse, and he did not know where they were going to rob. Ma Bosheng claimed that he was a former water police detective who was dismissed in May of this year. He was planning to surrender the handgun when the detective came to arrest him. He claimed he had never committed robbery and had never lent the handgun to anyone. He accused Jiang Zhian of falsely accusing him because he had once handled Jiang Zhian's smuggling of soil when he was a police officer. Han Jinshu confessed that he had not committed robbery, but Jiang Zhian had asked him to deliver the handgun twice. The first time, Yang, Jin, Li, Zhu, and Jiang Zhian went to rob No. 5 Ximen Lane, Ximen Road. The second time they robbed No. 101 Guba Road but failed. Huang Caigen confessed that he was an apprentice at No. 101 Guba Road. He drew the plans, and they (referring to Jiang et al.) went to rob, but failed. The other defendants all denied knowing about the robbery. The court adjourned the hearing to the 4th of this month (yesterday). The defendants were remanded in custody. At the time, because key figures were at large, the details could not be disclosed. The case is still under investigation by the police. However, two robbery cases in the French Concession have been uncovered: one attempted kidnapping, at No. 101 Guba Road, where the shop owner was grabbed, but he grabbed the kidnapper's leg and shouted for help, causing the robbers to flee. There were also two cases in Fengxian and the Caizhaoqiao village in western Shanghai. One victim has been ransomed. Because the case is complex and accomplices need to be arrested, the investigation will take time. In the interim, accomplice Chen Arong (39 years old, from Nanhui), Ma Bosheng’s partner, was arrested upon returning to Shanghai from his hometown and visiting Ma Bosheng’s house. Yesterday, the hearing resumed. The police brought the 13 male and female defendants to the Second Special Court at noon, where Judge Zhang presided over the Second Criminal Court for interrogation. The lawyers hired by the defendants, Wang Shizong, Xu Wufang, and Zhu Dianliao (represented by Lu Kaisheng), were also present. The police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated that the case involved robbery and kidnapping, and was very complex, so he requested another eight-day extension for investigation. Although several defendants were not related to the case, because key figures involved in negotiating ransoms in the kidnapping case were still at large, he requested that the innocent defendants be temporarily detained in the police station for a few days until the key figures were arrested and the case was thoroughly investigated. He requested that the innocent defendants be released. The court approved the request and only questioned Chen Arong about his age and origin before adjourning the hearing to 9 a.m. on the 13th. The defendants were remanded in custody.

Shi Weiyong Returns Home After Completing His Studies 89

Arrived in Shanghai from France aboard the Comte de Rousseau Ship, Having Achieved Profound Academic Success in His Studies of Sociology

Mr. Shi Weiyong, a native of Jiaxing, Zhejiang Province, engaged in rural movements in his early years, which swept through western Zhejiang. He then handled party affairs, focusing especially on reforming and developing local enterprises. With his practical personality and love of experimentation, Mr. Shi realized the need to solve problems through academic theory during his years of social service. Ya Pu Er Light Bulbs Can Still Be Sold Freely in the Dutch Territories 90

Four-Year-Old Case Resolved Satisfactorily

China's Ya Pu Er electric light bulbs have always enjoyed good sales in the Nanyang region. In 1931, because their quality and design were similar to Philips bulbs, the Dutch East Indies government used the pretext of patent issues to restrict their import, which attracted the attention of the Chinese people at the time. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs directly negotiated with the Dutch government, while instructing Song Faxiang, the Consul General in Batavia, to argue the case with the local government. After four years, the case has not been resolved. Now, it is learned that Mr. Hu Xiyuan, General Manager of Ya Pu Er Factory, has received formal notice from Consul General Song that the case has been resolved satisfactorily. Ya Pu Er electric light bulbs can still be sold freely in the Dutch territories without obstruction.

Li Quewei Runs Over and Kills Li Chuanbin; Taxpayer Association Sends Letter Requesting Swift Justice 93

The Shanghai Chinese Taxpayer Association sent a letter to Mr. Philip, Acting General Manager of the Public Concession's Public Works Department, yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you regarding a letter received from the Suzhou Native Association in Shanghai, concerning the case of Mr. Li Chuanbin, a telegraph operator at the Central News Agency, who was walking on the south sidewalk of Hankou Road on his way to work from his residence at No. 8, Tong'an Lane, on October 8th of this year at 1:55 p.m., when he was run over by Mr. Li Quewei, an employee of the Public Works Department's Taxation Office, who was driving car No. 8497 in the same direction, violating traffic regulations by driving onto the south sidewalk. Our fellow native association member Mr. Li Chuanbin was struck from behind, his leg was crushed, and he suffered internal injuries, resulting in his death. Our association has protested to the Public Works Department regarding this matter. We now find that prosecution is the standard procedure in traffic accidents, and the police authorities should handle it accordingly. However, the Public Works Department handles cases of traffic accidents involving Chinese people with extraordinary diligence, but claims insufficient evidence or lack of witnesses in cases involving foreigners, especially accidents involving public buses. Now, in the case of an accident involving an employee of the Public Works Department, they are doing everything possible to exonerate the perpetrator, disregarding the life and body of the victim. If cars can drive on the sidewalk and kill pedestrians, where is safety to be found? Are the traffic regulations of the Public Works Department not binding on Public Works Department employees? We do not know under what law this is based. In light of the above, we request your assistance in upholding justice and enforcing the law."

Pudong Middle School Debt Dispute 94

Zuozhe Bookstore Files Lawsuit

Pudong Middle School in this city was founded by Mr. Yang Sicheng with his own funds and is one of the leading middle schools, known for its mathematics, physics, and chemistry departments. Over the years, it has focused on improving the academic atmosphere. In 1932, a new board of directors was established, including Wu Xingya, Du Yuesheng (Chairman of the Board of Directors), Wu Kaixian, Wang Yansong, Yu Zuoting, Xu Jiqing, Zhang Shouchong, Zhu Baozhang, Zhang Xiaoliang, and other celebrities. The school quickly attracted a large number of students, reaching over 800. It is reported that the school lacks funds, so its finances are often strained. At the end of each semester, it must borrow money to maintain operations. In February of this year, the old principal of the school resigned, and the school's external borrowing was not clarified. Zuozhe Bookstore in this city has a close relationship with the school due to the sale of books. In November 1933 and January of this year, the school repeatedly and earnestly requested interest-free loans of 3,200 yuan, promising to repay them after receiving tuition fees at the beginning of the spring semester of this year. In addition to the promissory note, the school also issued four Shanghai Bank checks that expired in February. Now, the bookstore is filing a lawsuit in the local court for legal relief because the checks have expired and cannot be cashed. The bookstore has repeatedly sent letters to the school principal and directors, such as Mr. Du Yuesheng, requesting repayment. The directors, such as Mr. Du Yuesheng, sympathized with the bookstore's sincerity in supporting the school and promised that the new principal would be responsible for repayment. However, after a delay of more than half a year, the school has not repaid the debt. The bookstore has limited capital and is approaching the end of the year, so it has filed a lawsuit in the local court for legal relief. It is reported that the court will hold a hearing soon.

Unemployed Russian Steals Cemetery Vases 95

Wreaths, vases, potted plants, flowers, and other items placed by relatives of the deceased in the cemeteries of the Public Works Department are provided by the placers themselves, and the cemetery keepers are not responsible for their safekeeping. However, in reality, the cemetery keepers monitor the cemeteries day and night. The cemetery keepers discovered that vases had been stolen and caught a Russian immigrant red-handed with two stolen vases. It is reported that the Russian immigrant has been sentenced to 50 days of detention by the First Special District Court as a warning to others.

Fire at Route Béteille 96

A fire broke out in the kitchen of Wang Shengtin's house at No. 48, Lane 964, Route Béteille, in the French Concession at about 7:15 a.m. yesterday. Continued Hearing in the Yan Shengquan Case of Killing Tang Akun 97

Tang Akun (also known as Tang Yongshan), who resided at No. 491, Kang Nao Tuo Road, in western Shanghai, once served as the captain of the Changzhou Opium Suppression Bureau. After his dismissal, he had been unemployed. On the morning of November 16th of last year, at about 8 a.m., Tang Akun was walking on the coal cinder road near Yan's house when he was axed to death. His wife, Tang Zhu, sued the local court prosecutor, alleging that her husband was murdered by Yan Shengquan, who lived nearby, along with Zhao A'er and two others. The court arrested Yan based on the complaint. Prosecutor Xie Lian interrogated Yan and charged him with joint murder, stating that Yan Shengquan had a long-standing grudge against the deceased Tang Akun. On the morning of the incident, at about 8 a.m., Tang Akun went to Yan Shengquan's house by rickshaw. Yan had arranged for Zhao A'er and an unknown person to hide an axe and wait by the coal cinder road near Yan's house. Yan Shengquan then accompanied Tang Akun to the destination and together they axed Tang Akun in the head, causing serious injuries. Yan and the others fled without a trace. Tang Akun was rescued by the police and sent to the Red Cross Hospital, but he died of his injuries. Moreover, Yan Shengquan fled with his family immediately after Tang Akun was killed, which is strong evidence that the murder was premeditated. The crime constitutes a violation of Article 284, Paragraph 1, Item 1 of the Criminal Law. A trial was held once but not concluded. Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., Judge Wu Detang specially opened the Third Court for trial. First, the plaintiff, the deceased's wife Tang Zhu, 40 years old, from Shanghai, testified that her husband, Tang Akun, was invited by Yan Shengquan to his house on the morning of the tenth day of the tenth month of the lunar calendar last year, at around 8 a.m., claiming there was something to discuss. He left but never returned. Shortly after, the rickshaw puller Xiao Houcai returned home to report that her husband had been axed to death. Her husband had said that if anything happened to him in the future, Yan Shengquan would be the one to ask. She pleaded for justice and requested private compensation of 7,600 yuan. Next, Xiao Houcai, 32 years old, from Yancheng, testified that he was a rickshaw puller for Yan's family. On the morning of the incident, his employer took the rickshaw to Yan's house. About ten minutes later, his employer left with Yan Shengquan and three other people, heading east. His employer told him to wait there. A moment later, he suddenly heard that his employer had been axed to death. He immediately went home and told the mistress. Then, Shao Jingfan, the current Chinese Detective Chief of the Jiading Road Police Station in the Public Concession, testified that after the incident, he immediately transported the injured party to the hospital. The injured party said that he was axed by Yan Shengquan. Finally, the defendant Yan Shengquan, 36 years old, from Shanghai, testified that he was a chauffeur. He was seeking employment elsewhere but returned to Shanghai after losing his job and was suddenly falsely accused. The judge adjourned the hearing for further investigation and ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody.

Barrister Peng Wangdong from the prominent Peng family of Wumen, and Miss Pan Zhiquan, daughter of Shanghai notable Mr. Pan Yangyao, held their wedding ceremony at the New Asia Hotel yesterday. Correction

The temporary meeting of managers convened by the Money Industry Association the other night was due to the announcement by the Ministry of Finance of six measures to reform the currency system, which were scheduled to take effect on the fourth. Therefore, managers from all banks were summoned to report on the spot for compliance. There was no public shortage of 17 million yuan due to discrepancies in offsetting single-ended linings, nor was there a request to deposit cash from the money industry in the Central Bank in exchange for banknotes for relief. The report in yesterday's newspaper was completely inaccurate. This is hereby formally corrected.

A Visit to the Freedom Farm (Continued) 104

— Jinhua Ting

Three Departments of Work

Generally, a dairy farm is divided into four main departments: milk production, dairy processing, business, and accounting. The Freedom Farm is naturally no exception. Now, I will roughly describe the work situation of the farm's four departments.

(1) Milk Production Department (A) Matters concerning the feeding and mating of cows; (B) Research on breeding and selection; (C) Management and protection. All the above departments require expert management, but there is a real shortage of this type of talent. Even veterinary talent is scarce. Shanghai's dairy cows are also prone to many infectious diseases: (1) Pleuropneumonia, (2) Foot-and-mouth disease, (3) Rinderpest. It is worth mentioning the sources of these three diseases. Pleuropneumonia was transmitted from Russia three years ago, and dairy cows are most susceptible to this disease. Foot-and-mouth disease was transmitted from the United States last year. Rinderpest is most prevalent in Shanghai and Qingdao. Currently, there are various serums to prevent and control the above infectious diseases, but the cost is several thousand yuan per year.

(2) Dairy Processing Department (A) The bottle washing procedure is divided into four parts: (1) Degreasing, (2) Washing inside and out, (3) Rinsing, (4) Steaming. The same applies to milk cans. (B) Capping: The capping procedure is also divided into four parts: (1) Dust removal machine, (2) Sterilization machine, (3) Automatic temperature recording device (the milk is cooked at 145 degrees Fahrenheit for 30 minutes), (4) Cooling machine (the hot milk must be cooled to 45 degrees). (C) Bottling machine: As long as the fingers do not touch the bottle during bottling, it is fine.

(3) Business Department The farm has more than a thousand subscribers. In addition to the original work, there are also the following three movements, hoping to reduce prices on the one hand and popularize milk on the other.

(A) Children's Milk Drinking Movement Mr. You believes that milk is the best food for children, so the children's milk drinking movement has been implemented since October 1st. His method is roughly: (1) Temporarily set a quota of one thousand people. Milk bottles are divided into two types: small bottles, half a pound, priced at 12 cents; medium bottles, one pound, priced at 20 cents. The farm has also recently shipped nineteen cows from the United States, all of which are very healthy, and plans to use the milk from these nineteen cows specifically to supply this children's milk drinking movement. In addition, a female nurse has been hired to visit the children drinking milk in various families every day on a rotating basis.

(B) School Milk Drinking Movement This movement aims to make milk popular in schools. It is done in two stages. The first time was last year, starting with universities. Fudan, Shanghai, St. John's, Jiaotong, Tongji, Daxia, Guanghua, and Shanghai Medical College, among other eight universities, have already succeeded. The second time is this year, proceeding from the perspective of middle school students and faculty. Many middle school students and faculty are already drinking milk.

(C) Institutional Milk Drinking Movement This movement has also been implemented. A quarter of a pound of milk is mixed with a quarter of a pound of black tea, then sweetened with white sugar and packaged in cans for distribution. In addition, two biscuits are provided, so that public servants in the agency can enjoy tea and snacks without leaving their office, priced at 10 cents. To avoid trouble, a voucher will be issued for easy exchange with the milk delivery person at any time.

(4) Accounting Department The accounting department has five staff members. In addition to managing various accounts in Shanghai, Suzhou, and Hangzhou, they are also responsible for compiling various statistical tables: daily reports, monthly summaries, and annual reports. This is the most important work from a management perspective.

Finally, Mr. You also talked about the establishment process of his farm, its current situation, and future plans. The Freedom Farm was established around 1920, with a start-up cost of only ten thousand several thousand yuan. Initially, it could only do a few dollars of business a month. Now, it can do ten thousand several thousand yuan. At the same time, our capital has also increased to sixty thousand yuan. In 1926, with a capital of twenty thousand yuan, a branch farm was established in Suzhou, and the business was very good. In 1931, another branch farm was established in Hangzhou with thirty thousand yuan, and the business was only enough to maintain itself, a bit worse than Suzhou. Recently, preparations are being made to set up another branch farm in Nanjing, which is still in preparation. At the same time, twenty-four acres of land have been leased long-term in Longhua, preparing to build the main farm next year. In addition, there are two attached projects: one is the "Family Service Society," headed by Mr. Shen, whose main purpose is to handle household affairs for subscribers, such as paying water, electricity, and housing donations. The other is the "Rural Research Office," headed by Mr. Li. Currently, there are over a hundred types of Chinese and foreign newspapers, dozens of rural magazines, and hundreds of agricultural books, collecting various materials in preparation for improving the countryside. A trial run has started in Xuejiawan, Suzhou, and some progress has been made.

This Mr. You has a great interest in agricultural affairs, so once he started talking, he was eloquent and tireless. He graduated from the agricultural department of Cornell University in the United States, which is the most prestigious university in the world, and is particularly familiar with the situation of agricultural affairs in the United States. He made a few statistical comparisons between New York milk and Shanghai milk. He said that there are a total of 24 million dairy cows in the United States, with an annual output of about 90 million pounds. If a cow's annual output is less than 6,000 pounds, it will be slaughtered. New York receives about 5 million pounds of milk daily from all directions. There are 55 million milk transport vehicles and 32 trains with 259 carriages. The farthest distance is 450 miles, and the nearest is 44 miles. There are a total of 3,000 dairy cows in Shanghai, selling 30,000 pounds per day. If we talk about the freshness of milk, Shanghai milk is much better than New York milk, but the sales volume is far different.

Corrigendum In yesterday's published "Visit to the Freedom Farm," the twelve lines from "Starting with expert talks" to the sentence "Allowing the superior to survive" should be placed in the "Full Farm Tour" section, after the twenty-fourth line of the "Three Disinfection Departments," after the sentence "Not allowing development and survival." This is hereby corrected.

The Malaysian Chinese Football Team's Two Matches in the Philippines The First Match Victorious Against the Ateneo Team 105

Xie Qingfu scored three goals, Yao Shenghua scored four goals. The next day, they lost to the Rizal Team with a score of 1-3.

(Manila News) The Malaysian Chinese football team, runner-up in this year's National Games football competition, arrived in Manila yesterday morning (26th). Five hours after unloading their luggage, they made a stunning debut at the Rizal Memorial Sports Field, defeating the famous Ateneo de Manila University team by a score of 7-0.

A Great Victory Over Ateneo

At half-past four, the Western referee blew the whistle to start the match. The Ateneo team kicked off the attack. Both sides wore the same blue shirts and white pants, making it difficult for the players to distinguish each other. After three minutes of melee, Yin Jinzhen dribbled in from the right wing. The opponent's left back rushed out to intercept, and Yin immediately passed to the center. Xie Qingfu rushed forward to meet it with his head, and the ball flew into the net, scoring the first goal amidst cheers. After losing this goal, the runner-up immediately counterattacked, but our defense was tight, and they retreated without success many times. Afterwards, the Malaysian Chinese also attacked several times, but they were too impatient, so many long shots either bounced off the crossbar or went over the goal. While the overseas Chinese community was sighing, Xie Qingfu suddenly received a pass from Yao Shenghua and again used his old trick to head the ball, and the ball flew into the net again, making the score 2-0. Because they were eager to win, the opponent's movements inevitably became irritable. Our Xu Houkun was even scratched on his left eyebrow, and blood flowed profusely. Fortunately, it was not a vital part, and Ji Youling replaced him. In the continuing battle, although the Malaysian Chinese took the upper hand, the Ateneo team's central defense line was quite tight, and the Malaysian Chinese failed to score many times. Two minutes before the end of the first half, Yao Shenghua suddenly shot fiercely with his left foot in front of the enemy's goal, 15 yards out, but it was caught. Xie Qingfu intercepted it and passed it back to Yao Shenghua. Yao did not fail his mission, using his left foot to pass the enemy defender, and then shooting fiercely with his right foot. The ball brushed in from the right corner of the goal, with a beautiful momentum. The Ateneo goalkeeper could only shake his head and sigh. At the end of the first half, the Malaysian Chinese led 3-0.

After the lemon break, the opponent changed sides to continue the fight. With the victory in the first half in hand, the Malaysian Chinese's attack became more fierce, and the other side also knew that they could not counterattack, so they switched to defense. This field gave the Malaysian Chinese quite a tenacious resistance. However, the Malaysian Chinese were an experienced team, and they became more courageous as they fought. Li Yiyao shot from ten yards in front of the enemy's goal, but the ball was slightly high and went over the goal. Before long, the Malaysian Chinese got a forty-yard free kick, which Xie Qingfu took. Xie lifted his foot and shot a low, fast ball. Although the goalkeeper dived, it was too late. The ball was strong and fast, winning applause from the whole field, making the score 4-0. After the center kick-off, Qingfu's ambition was not dead, and he rushed in again for a goal, but the referee ruled this goal offside, so it was not counted. At that time, the Malaysian Chinese's arrogance was at its peak, and the other side could only parry but could not counterattack, so Qingfu turned around and kicked in another goal. Yao Shenghua did not let Qingfu monopolize the glory. With the help of Xie Qingfu and Yin Jinzhen, he scored two consecutive goals, creating a half-dozen number. In order to break this goose egg record, everyone held the ambition of burning the boats. Sure enough, the war situation changed. At that time, the five forwards were invading the Philippine hinterland. Although Huang Jinbo had twice caught dangerous balls, afterwards, with the strong defense of Xie Fayu, Jian Dehui, Lin Zhiquan, and Chen Qiwan, the goal was extremely leisurely. On the contrary, Yin Jinzhen, Xie Qingfu, and Yao Shenghua successively attacked the goal, but they were all caught. In the melee, Xie Qingfu and Yao Shenghua advanced side by side into the enemy area. Yao aimed and shot fiercely from ten yards in front of the enemy's goal. The ball was like an arrow from a bow. The goalkeeper knelt to catch it, but the ball leaked out and rolled in, causing the whole field to exclaim. Until the end of the game, neither side gained anything. The Malaysian Chinese returned triumphantly with a score of 7-0.

Defeated by the Rizal Team

Another quick report on the 28th: The Malaysian Chinese football team made its first appearance at half-past four yesterday afternoon, fighting the Rizal team, the champion of all Philippine universities. As a result, they suffered a disastrous defeat with a score of 1-3. Now the competition schedule has been temporarily changed. There are about four reasons for yesterday's failure: (1) Lack of strength, (2) Only the right forward attacked, (3) Xie Qingfu was monitored by three fierce enemy players, (4) The enemy team had better contact, and the central defender had strong skills. The battle situation was tense from beginning to end. Twenty minutes after the start of the first half, the Malaysian Chinese team's Sheng Hua took the lead in creating a record. Five minutes later, the Philippine team's Austria kicked in a goal. The first half was evenly divided, with a score of 1-1. In the second half, the Rizal team bravely attacked, and their momentum was fierce. The Malaysian Chinese team's strength had declined, and they gradually became depressed. After Austria scored another goal, they were even more panicked, causing them to lose many excellent opportunities. About fifteen minutes before the end of the game, they were shot fiercely by the enemy's center forward Austria, and the ball flew into the net, making the score 3-1. At that time, the general situation had passed, so although the Malaysian Chinese made a desperate struggle, they ultimately failed.

List of Research Questions for the Secondary School Teachers' Education Research Association This Semester 115

A total of sixty questions have been compiled by the Education Bureau.

Divided into six major categories, including curriculum, teaching, etc.

The research questions for the first semester of the 24th academic year of the Municipal Secondary School Teachers' Education Research Association were submitted separately by each school and have been compiled by the Education Bureau, with a total of sixty questions, divided into sixty categories including curriculum and teaching, which have been announced for each school to read in preparation for the meeting and research. The date of the meeting will be notified after it has been selected. The research questions are recorded as follows.

Curriculum Teaching

secondary schools regulate exercises and notes for each subject, (5) How should the correction method of secondary school arithmetic exercise books be regulated, (6) Students feel that extracurricular assignments are too heavy for academic subjects, how should methods be devised to remedy this, (7) How to compile extracurricular reading lists, (8) How to increase students' efficiency in automatic learning, (9) How to standardize the progress of junior high school English teaching, (10) Although the current secondary school curriculum has been vigorously promoted by the government for science education, the scientific achievements of secondary schools cannot be improved, what are the reasons and what methods should be used to remedy this, (11) How should the internship methods of teachers' college students be promoted, (12) How to link students' school life with practical social life, (13) Should secondary schools increase students' time to visit various social lives, (14) The secondary school curriculum is too complicated, repetitive, and stagnant, and should be thoroughly revised to give students individuality and enable each to achieve something, (15) High school essays, vernacular and classical Chinese, should not be restricted, (16) How should the teaching hour table for teachers' college subjects be revised, (17) Should the teachers' college curriculum be revised, (18) Should ordinary secondary schools implement productive education, (19) How to promote secondary school students' interest in teaching and learning and academic achievements, (20) Do schools have adaptive methods for individual differences, (21) How to improve the quantity of mathematics teaching materials, (22) Should middle school students be separated by gender, (23) How should charts for junior high school biology, hygiene, history, geography, and other subjects be designed, printed, and distributed according to the new curriculum standards to facilitate teaching, (24) Simplification of Chinese characters in schools, (25) Should the application of Chinese and foreign language reading grammar be taught together, (26) Must the texts that should be read carefully in Chinese class all be improved?

Teacher Training

Ministry of Education Issues Order for Short-Term Primary School System Experiment 117

(Nanjing, 4th) The Ministry of Education issued an order to various departments and bureaus, stating that in order to implement compulsory education, one-year short-term primary schools should be established in various regions during the first phase, and two-year short-term primary schools should be established during the second phase. To improve various methods for these short-term primary schools and facilitate implementation, the Ministry has formulated experimental measures for the short-term primary school system. According to the provisions of these measures, affiliated elementary schools or experimental elementary schools of domestic normal universities, colleges of education, independent colleges of education, provincial and municipal normal schools, and other elementary schools with experimental capabilities should follow the specified experimental items and conduct experiments accordingly. The Ministry hereby issues these measures and orders that they be circulated to the affiliated institutions for compliance and reporting.

Chapter 6: The Weary Birds Return to Their Nests

July had arrived, and the work of cutting hay had begun. The crops in the small gardens were flourishing, and the long summer days were filled with interesting embellishments. The doors of the house were open from morning till night, and the children lived outdoors except when attending classes. The homework was not long, and there were many holidays because the Pei family believed that a lot of exercise was needed to cultivate a strong body, and summer was not long, so it was best to use it for outdoor work. The children had become tanned, rosy-cheeked, and strong team; they had good appetites; very developed arms and legs, and the sleeves and trouser legs of their previous clothes were all too short. They jumped and laughed in Mei Village; they did very interesting things in the house; they went everywhere in the mountains and fields. How happy the wise Pei family was to see their group of children developing both physically and mentally!—All these, I cannot describe in detail one by one. In fact, two things were enough to make them infinitely happy, and the discovery of this matter was entirely unexpected and also most accidental.

Securities Except for '96, Bonds All Hit the Upper Limit 129

Yesterday at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange, due to the government's sudden announcement of currency control reform, both bullish and bearish sides frantically scurried about, and the atmosphere on the trading floor was extremely tense. Whether this measure is beneficial to public bonds is a matter of opinion, with each person having a different perspective. All sorts of extreme views were expressed. Since this is a pioneering initiative in China, the soaring of commodity prices is naturally to be expected. Public bonds, being government debt contracts, are similar in nature to paper money. Whether they will also follow the path of soaring prices is a matter of general consensus. This type of measure by the government has in fact been implemented for some time, the only difference being cash nationalization. Observing the informal market, the bulls of "78" were most active. Yarn and Cotton Drastic Changes in Yarn and Cotton 130

Benchmark Yarn Rises and Falls by 9 Yuan, Spot Cotton Jumps by 3 Yuan

The yarn market is experiencing wild surges and plunges, with tumultuous waves. The Ministry of Finance's announcement that banknotes from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications are legal tender and that cash cannot be used has caused extreme market chaos, with various rumors spreading and widespread panic. Short sellers are in a state of disarray. Chang Feng and Da Feng are aggressively buying, further strengthening the upward momentum. Second-round prices for all months have simultaneously broken through the 200-yuan mark, reaching a new high since the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan. Subsequently, as the trend in spot gold eased, Tong Ji began to release their holdings, and Yu Da reversed course and sold short, causing prices to fluctuate sharply. The price difference reached as high as 9 yuan, indicating the anxiety of both bullish and bearish sides.

Near Months Weak, Distant Months Firm in Benchmark Yarn

The benchmark yarn market opened with a surge in all months. The market situation was extremely serious, and the atmosphere was heated to a boiling point. Buying orders were deafening, and bid prices were chaotic. Later, Tong Ji suddenly appeared and sold into the market, maintaining the situation. All months rose by more than 2 yuan. The April contract soared by 4 yuan. By the second round, the market situation became even more volatile. The intensity of both bullish and bearish sides was extremely fierce, especially the panic of the short sellers. As spot cotton soared by 2 yuan, the cotton-yarn ratio should have risen by 10 yuan, triggering a surge in buying interest. The November contract jumped by 6 yuan compared to the second round, and all months simultaneously broke through the 200-yuan mark. However, Tong Ji, Yu Da, Da Ji, and securities firms suddenly started selling in large quantities, slightly easing the pressure on the trading floor. The spot gold price remained stable, and a sudden reversal occurred. Prices in the third round fell back by 1 yuan. By the closing bell, selling pressure suddenly intensified, and prices plummeted. The February contract fell by 4 yuan compared to the third-round price. As a result, near months closed with gains of 2.40 to 2 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price, while distant months fell by 1.50 yuan. The afternoon session opened with near months still falling by 1 yuan, but distant months rebounded. After the second round, the market turned more moderate, and trading volume decreased.

As a result, near months fell by 3.80 to 1.40 yuan compared to the morning closing price, while distant months rose by 0.10 to 1.30 yuan. Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 141

— (Zhongshe)

A person often picks roses far away, but tramples on the chrysanthemums at his feet. You need to know that great careers start from small things.

The most valuable spirit of a person is the determination not to turn back when you encounter any obstacles or blows.

A person's strong determination will scare away many demons who can confuse the minds of the weak; it will eliminate many difficulties and obstacles.

The tributary will never be higher than the source. The success of your career will never be higher than your self-confidence.

What can develop our strength and talents is not external help, but self-help; not dependence, but self-reliance. People sitting on the "cushion of convenience and happiness" will fall asleep.

A Record of Burying a Cow 142

— Shaou

The Agricultural Experiment Field of Jiangsu Provincial Educational College, in order to test and improve livestock breeds, once spent a lot of money to purchase multiple superior breeds of cattle, sheep, chickens, and pigs from abroad. I don't know if it's because they couldn't adapt to the water and soil, or because the breeding was not good. These foreign cattle and foreign pigs are not as prosperous as the foreigners who live in China.

On Double Tenth Day, the National Rural Work Discussion Conference, with 169 representatives from 99 groups in 19 provinces and cities, was held in the college. A large bull raised on the college's farm happened to die at 1:00 p.m. that afternoon. Fearing to disturb the guests, the farm's administrators secretly kept the news quiet. They dug a hole in the highlands outside the college, directly facing Mount Hui, to serve as the "resting place for the cow." After the lights were turned off at night, they quietly asked the farmers to carry it away. But they didn't know that fifteen strong farmers couldn't move it. (This "bull" weighed about 1,600 pounds.) They had to temporarily call a group of short-term workers to help. After tying it up, they were about to put it on their shoulders when the single pole (thick wood) couldn't bear the weight and suddenly broke in the middle. They had to replace it with another wooden bar, but it broke again. So they knocked on the wood shop in the middle of the night to buy wood to make a bar. It was already about 2:00 a.m. After midnight. With the strength of twenty-two people, they wanted to carry the foreign cow's body away. By the time it was buried, the sky was already turning white, and the morning rooster was crowing. It was truly "rushing to the funeral at night and crawling to the road."

This cow was a pure Holstein breed, worth 800 yuan. It was specially used for mating. Mating female cows outside the college requires a fee of two yuan per time. It is no different from a "male prostitute."

Waiting for Crabs 143

— Chen Liang

The seasonal winds have painted the maple leaves crimson and whitened the reeds' beards. Under the eaves of the ancient temple, decaying leaves cling to cobwebs, while the ocher hues of the autumn mountains rise distantly. Across the lonely stream lies a solitary log bridge, gazing leisurely at the thin clouds drifting by—it is once again the season for fat crabs.

On the slippery mudflats, scoured by the stream, crab claw marks resembling sunflower seeds are left, disorderly and crisscrossing, indicating the crab swarm's bustling activities of the previous night. However, precisely because of these visible traces, the villagers are stirred with the intention of waiting for crabs. This is something crabs themselves would never anticipate—that humans would use light to lure their lives, satisfying their appetites or imprisoning them to be sold in towns for profit, thereby enriching themselves with the lives of these aquatic beetles.

As the second watch's gong sound sinks into the distant village dwellings, here, a mast lamp has quietly been lit. By the creek, reeds rustle, seemingly sighing for the crabs' impending fate. Perhaps a lone wild goose slices through the long loneliness of the autumn night, but the crab-waiter pays no attention. He even holds his breath, waiting, waiting...

The crabs, finally, are lured onto the mudflats again, just like the previous night. However, they do not know that what lured them last night was the bright moonlight, while tonight it is the fire of the crab-waiter's mast lamp. Sadly, though the crabs possess two eyes, they still crawl toward the crab-waiter's hand. One enters the bamboo cage, while another continues to approach, one after another... The crab-waiter's face reveals a triumphant joy, and in his mind, he calculates the next day's rice wine, dry tobacco, oil, and salt—all the necessities of life. Thus, crabs are sold in the market, pickled, boiled, and pan-fried with batter.

All this is thanks to the crab-catchers' efforts, right? But the lives of the crabs go unnoticed. A four-year-old son picks up two crabs from somewhere, pins them to the wall, and claps his hands. Is it that humans are cruel from a young age? If so, then I must not blame the crab-waiters.

King Yu's Sleeve 144

— Jiang Mi

Autumn Park 145

— Wu Yafei

For the sake of my job, I sit in a guiltless prison all day long. Normally, I am not easily allowed to step beyond the bounds. Therefore, regardless of spring, summer, autumn, or winter, besides changing my clothes like everyone else, I live so mechanically throughout the year, never having the opportunity to stroll through the spring countryside or enjoy the autumn scenery.

Now, I have finally obtained a more leisurely occupation, which often allows me to go to the park for a walk or a quiet sit. Thus, I have seen the bare branches on the old trees, and I have stepped on the yellow leaves in the grassy paths. However, although all these scenes inevitably carry a heavy sentimental tone, and every corner seems to be piled up with infinite feelings of desolation, the people visiting the park are still so active. I believe that the hearts of most young people must be filled with excitement and joy. Whenever I sit on that chair by the pond, musing or daydreaming, I always hear the laughter of young men and women and the singing of children, drifting gently in my ears, drifting. But loneliness in my heart cannot be driven away.

"Can I also return to childhood and forget the traumas of life?" I ask myself, but besides a bitter smile, there is no comforting answer. I still stare at the white clouds in the sky.

"Autumn!" A yellow leaf floats down from above and falls on my lap. I carefully push it to the ground, where it happens to be crushed by the high heels of a modern girl. At this moment, a wave suddenly stirs in my heart, as if her step was stepping on my heart. My heart is also crushed: "Life is short, life is limited. How am I going to pursue my life? But, but my youth has already been driven away by life!" I silently stood up, walked through the woods, and stared at a group of children by the pond in a daze.

Miscellaneous Remarks

A Brief Record of Shooting Riddles 146

— Ai Mei

There is a poetry society at sea, initially named Seeking Sound, later called Singing Society. Recently, on the occasion of its twentieth anniversary, it specially sent letters to summon society members from far and near for a gathering to reminisce about the past. After the drinking and singing, Sun Shushi and Yao Jinqiu prepared riddles as rewards, hanging lanterns for subtle shooting. It reached a peak of popularity for a time.

Among the society members who are good at shooting riddles, Ye Youqin and Yao Zhuxuan should be mentioned. Yao even has the nickname of "Tiger-Fighting General." Others such as Jia Shuxiang, Zhu Dake, and Zheng Zhian are all skillful as well. Guests from outside the society who are adept at this skill, such as Shi Jiqun, Lu Dan'an, and Xu Xingsu, also came to attend. They rubbed shoulders and stood around the riddles, focusing their minds and pointing at their palms, their elegant interests, how wonderful!

The wife of society member Wu Qinmu is quite skilled in calligraphy and painting, and is particularly clever at solving riddles. She correctly answered five of Jinqiu's riddles in a row. I noted their solutions: "One son Shu serves in government" was a riddle from Strange Tales from a Chinese Studio. "Shang Sanguan" was the answer. "One by one east" was a riddle for a character name from Water Margin: Dong Ping. "Young couple" was a riddle for a character: Sha. "Evil guest" was a riddle for a character: Fan. "A blind man riding a blind horse" was a riddle for a dialect: "Scolding the monk for being bald." From this, readers can imagine her hand waving and eyes following, with wonderful thoughts arising continuously. At that time, I was on the side and suddenly had a flash of inspiration and got a riddle, intending to tease Qinmu, it read: "Mrs. Wu guessing riddles, riddle from the Four Books:" The answer was: "A wife does not speak, but when she does, she is always right." But my friendship with Qinmu was still shallow, and I was afraid he would be angry, so I did not dare to reveal it! I also saw a riddle: "Fond of ancient prose, riddle from Peking Opera:" Kaitian Pidi (The Creation of the World), because "good" in ancient times was written with the characters Zi and Chou. According to tradition, the sky opened at Zi time and the earth split at Chou time, hence the saying. It was correctly answered by his daughter, Wen. It can be said that the whole family is elegant, which is enviable!

My brain has been injured for a long time and cannot withstand thinking, so I only solved one riddle, fortunately successfully. It was: "A dream, a phantom, a bubble, a shadow, dew, lightning, pull up the blindfold, riddle from the Thousand Character Classic:" "Like the Six Classics." The gift I received was a standing scroll of reed geese by Jinqiu, which is extremely valuable, and my heart was extremely happy.

In two days, no fewer than a hundred riddles were solved. I have copied some of them to share with everyone. However, for the sake of length, I will not list the names of those who solved them. For example: "Society, riddle from the Three Character Classic:" "The Xiahou clan used pine, the Yin people used cypress, and the Zhou people used chestnut." "Thousands of wrongs, ten thousands of wrongs, all are the fault of the young student, collection of Kunqu opera titles:" "Till Dawn, Carrying Thorns. Little Western Heaven 147

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-One: Gently Relying on Others, Appreciating the Moon's Beauty in the Courtyard; Angrily Scolding the Son-in-Law, Listening to the Lion's Roar from the Next Room

After a wave of distress in her heart, Yueying had paused for some time, and naturally collected the tears that were about to flow out. She continued to him: "My father, seeing that situation, naturally dared to stop them. But he couldn't help but feel sad when they insisted on cutting all the wheat in the field, so he shouted loudly and fell to the ground. The officer was also in the wheat field, watching the soldiers cut the wheat. Seeing my father fall to the ground, he felt compassionate and said to my father: 'Don't be sad, when our pay arrives, we'll reward you with some money.' My father lay on the ground unconscious for a while, then woke up, and said: 'If you're waiting for future pay to reward me with money, it's better to reward me with some grain now. I worked so hard to grow so much wheat, but I haven't tasted a single grain. Don't you think I'm wronged?' The officer laughed and said: 'Since that's the case, why don't you join my camp as a soldier? We have plenty to eat, and you'll naturally have plenty to eat too.' My father said, 'My family has several mouths to feed, all relying on me alone. If you take me to be a soldier, who will take care of my family?' The officer said it well, 'Which soldier doesn't have a family? Do you think you're the only one with a family?' When the officer said this, the soldiers under his command thought he was going to enlist my father, so without allowing any explanation, they dragged my father away. At that time, we were all at home and didn't know about this. We only found it strange when we didn't see my father return in the afternoon. These soldiers lived in our fort, constantly going in and out. One of the quick-tongued ones sent us a message, and we learned that the grain was gone and the person was gone too." (355)

Imperial Fragrance Drifting Record 148

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

"Hurry up! Don't delay any longer!" Finally, she urged us on, in a reversed manner. No matter how unfavorable this omen is, we must go out immediately! I think something must happen in this morning's court, at least a piece of bad news. Perhaps at this moment, that old man Qing Shun (i.e., Grand Councilor Prince Qing) already has an memorial in his sleeves that is greatly unfavorable to us.

Her extremely arbitrary prediction was originally not permitted by reason, and I didn't dare to believe it at the time, but what happened later was exactly as expected, truly a coincidence! Now let me slowly describe it, and readers can believe it or not as they please.

The Empress Dowager always took a group of us out with her to court every day, as usual. She was doing the same this day. I carefully watched her from behind, only to see that she was walking much faster than usual today, but although fast, her steps were very hurried and sometimes crooked, unlike her usual stability. Instead, she fully displayed the walking posture of an ordinary old woman. From this point of view, that magnolia flower that suddenly bloomed in the garden had indeed threatened the Empress Dowager, revealing her old age!

When we entered the main hall, the Empress Dowager's ministers were already waiting below the hall. As soon as they saw the Empress Dowager arrive, they knelt down together without hesitation, respectfully kowtowing and reporting their names to pay their respects. This was an old routine that I was tired of watching, so there is no need to describe it in detail. After everyone had paid their respects, Prince Qing remained kneeling, waiting for the Old Buddha to grant him the special permission to speak. (451)
