Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao Local News

Brief Remarks

The Issue of Salaries for Elementary School Teachers in Our Country 149

— Xing An

Everyone acknowledges that elementary school teachers in our country live in great poverty. Their meager salaries are barely enough to sustain their personal lives.

Salaries of elementary school teachers in all countries are superior to those in any part of our country. The lowest salary in our country, such as in Shaanxi, is twenty-four yuan per year. The highest salary, such as in Hubei, is one thousand eight hundred yuan per year. But these refer to the lowest and highest salaries in the entire country. In general, an elementary school teacher can earn an annual salary of two hundred to four hundred yuan.

Education is the fundamental plan for establishing a nation. Whether a country's education is developed or not is of great importance to the rise and fall of the country. Nowadays, countries around the world, such as England, America, and France, are becoming increasingly powerful. In addition to strengthening their military forces, the development of education is undoubtedly the greatest reason. Investigating the underdevelopment of education in our country, although there are many reasons, the meager salaries of teachers should be a fatal problem. Therefore, if our country does not talk about reforming education, then so be it. If we want to reform education, we must first start with improving the salaries of elementary school teachers. Because if the salaries of elementary school teachers are not improved, our country's education will not be improved for a single day. I hope the education authorities will pay close attention to this point.

It is said that Italy requires elementary school teachers to pass a national examination before they can be employed. Once employed, it is a lifelong position, and the state cannot change their position without reason. The situation in Japan is the same as in Italy. Thus, teachers' salaries are superior, and they are dedicated to their work. Having such a solid and superior guarantee in life allows them to fully develop their talents and devote themselves to the education cause they are engaged in.

The Government Inspector 150

— Tian

—Amateur Actors Performing in Jin City—

"The Government Inspector" appeared before my eyes for the first time, but I have been yearning for "The Government Inspector" to appear for several years. I had this thought when I read the play.

There are many difficulties in staging this play: the characters' personalities are not easy to grasp, one; the tone is not easy to unify, two; the costumes, props, and sets must match the Russian court of the early nineteenth century. Although it is not difficult to find reference materials, it is difficult to make them realistic. When this play was first staged in Russia, its poor performance provoked the original author, Gogol, to protest angrily.

Although Gogol's plays are not many, since "The Government Inspector" was published, it was as if a bomb had been dropped on the Russian theater scene, sweeping away the clownish jokes and the boring nonsense, and turning into serious laughter and scolding, the scourging of life, and the punishment of ugliness. He used his unrestrained and sharp pen to fully display the corruption and foolishness of the feudal officials of Russia at that time, as well as the ugliness of the group affiliated with that class, in a short five-act play. Gogol put a lot of effort into this, fulfilling the responsibility of a midwife transitioning from feudal society to capitalist society. He is a great "critical realist." The postures of the characters, such as the county magistrate, principal, hospital director, judge, postmaster, shrew, merchant, and the fake government inspector, are the entire foundation of the Russian superstructure at that time. This outline of a hater of the world is typically and dialectically imaged, is it not? Even the "smell of alcohol" on the juror's body is because "his mother harmed him when he was a child." He has a particularly sensitive "nose" and has smelled all the stench on the bodies of officials all over Russia after only being a low-level official for a month or so, and from here he issued a critique that even Emperor Nicholas felt stank. If you remember the judge repeatedly mentioning selling dogs, you will smile knowingly! This is no different from his method of writing novels. In terms of structure, apart from the monologue in the first act, which is now considered inappropriate, the entire play is tight, and each act is tighter than the last, so that the audience's heart is constantly disturbed by the progress of the tense plot. If you compare Molière's many comedies with "The Government Inspector," not only are the styles different, but the structures are also very different. I dare not say

Page 18

that Molière's works are inferior to Gogol, but Molière's works are sometimes too relaxed due to looseness, and the depth of portrayal is not as venomous as Gogol's, which is obvious to all.

Speaking of this performance, the overall achievement is above "Nora." The allocation of roles, the composition of the stage, the design of the costumes, and the coordination of the sound effects were carefully crafted, especially the personalities of the characters and the tone between the acts, which were done to more than eighty percent. Of course, there are also shortcomings, such as sometimes being too exaggerated and close to civilized drama. For example, that character Yin Xiucen is a vulgar clown, and it is unlikely that he would be among the gentry of the county. In terms of sound effects, when Ye Luxi looked at the "Government Inspector" and danced and sang, there was a lack of musical accompaniment and footsteps. Using drums to accompany the slapping was not realistic enough.

In terms of the actors, Gu Eryi was good in everything except for occasional inaccurate pronunciation. He seemed to have more than enough energy for such a heavy play. Jin Shan was too weak in the first act, playing the character of a playboy into a coy woman. Hunger will never change a person's character in an instant, but after that, each act was more vivid than the last. Wang Ying and Ye Luxi played the mother and daughter's jealousy, and every word and movement struck people's hearts. The facial expressions were particularly flexible—but Miss Wang's makeup was a little too beautiful. Compared with her daughter Ye Luxi, it was impossible to tell that they were mother and daughter, but rather a pair of sisters. Zheng Junli looked very much like a capable Russian official, but his words and actions were so weak. A judge in the feudal era should still have a considerable amount of majesty. He was a competent one, without any characteristics. Zuo Ming's old servant, he performed with skillful techniques, from which we can see that he probably did not rehearse much, because sometimes his movements were very flustered, but when I went to see it again on the second night, he was much calmer than the first time. Gu Menghu does not have many plays, but apart from a slight lack of posture in walking, both times he read the letter were quite funny, and that kind of seemingly true but not true attitude is precisely Gogol's style. Yin Xiucen and Liu Mang had already announced in the instructions that they were a pair of Laurel and Hardy, but unexpectedly they really acted as Laurel and Hardy. Gogol arranged this pair of characters to complete the epitome of feudal politics with laughter and tears, but they completely acted as laughing characters, which was wrong. Shi Chao almost turned into an idiot when he saw the government inspector, and the scene of eating a cigar, forcibly spitting the smoke on the ground, seemed too exaggerated, but this is the director's responsibility. In addition, Lan Pin, Zhu Mingxian, Jin Yi, and He Kangli were all competent, but I could not even hear what Ms. Wu Ling was saying.

All in all, the result was not ordinary.

Dream of Hope 151

— Shi Ying

Robbery 152

— Wang Youhou

As soon as the sky began to brighten, Little Sanzi's mother called him up. She was an abandoned middle-aged woman who had been struggling to make a living with her only asset—Little Sanzi—since her husband fled. Now Little Sanzi could also pick up some trash to help her. But when she saw the fatigue on her son's face every day when she called him awake, she always felt a hidden pain in her heart.

"Have you washed your face? Hurry up! It's already late!" she said, looking at Little Sanzi's face, then raising her head to look at the sky, and continuing to mend the unfinished torn clothes in her hand.

Little Sanzi didn't say a word from beginning to end, carrying the trash basket on his back with an empty stomach, and left!

She rushed out, calling,——calling him back to eat, but he left without turning his head.

Little Sanzi had a good companion, Ah Hu next door. They went to pick up trash together every day and played together.

"Hey! Look! There's something over there!" Ah Hu discovered something new, it seemed.

"Ah! A doll!" Little Sanzi ran over and picked it up, thinking it was his good luck.

"I saw this doll! Why did you take it? Give it back to me quickly!" Ah Hu argued with Little Sanzi, with a threatening tone.

"Hmph! Give it back to you! You wish! I picked it up." Little Sanzi said stubbornly.

"Hmph! You won't give it to me? Look! Look at the bomb that your ancestors brought from overseas! Can you handle it?" Ah Hu took out a foreign bottle from the broken basket, making a fighting posture.

"I won't give it to you, I definitely won't give it to you, I've never been afraid of fighting!" Little Sanzi stubbornly said.

"Okay!"

The sound of crying resonated next to the trash can in the alley. Little Sanzi's head was broken by Ah Hu; he lay in a pool of blood with his eyes tightly closed. The trash basket was also crushed by others. Many people surrounded him. Finally, an ambulance took him to the hospital, but his mouth was mumbling——"My doll! My doll!"

At lunchtime, his mother waited for him at the door, but she never saw her son's shadow until evening.

On Wheels 153

— Le Jian

The ocean liner rested in Xiamen harbor for a while, re-filled its belly with rouge powder fragrance, suits, and English, then slowly cranked up its iron anchor again, heading straight for Shanghai.

In the steerage, clusters of young men and women gathered, mixed together, exhaling powder fragrance, permeated by a peculiar stuffy air unique to the ship's cabin, suffocating people's lungs like a worn-out cloth. Precisely because of this, and out of curiosity towards the singing and laughter of a group of men and women at the stern, my aimless legs invariably led me to the stern, where I leaned against the railing, breathing in the refreshing sea breeze, and silently counting the waves bursting from each swell; or I would feign a weary expression, turn my body, lean sideways on the railing, and observe the entertainment of that group of young men and women.

There was a solitary White Russian, a healthy and sturdy tall man, with a face the color of bread crust, his clear gold and brown pupils fixed in the middle of light blue eyeballs, wooden and expressionless. His luggage consisted of a small trunk, covered with baggage tags from many ports, which was enough to prove his drifting and unsettled life. Moreover, from his coarse clothing, one could infer that he was a worker.

In his wooden gaze, there seemed to be a deep-seated stern and cold light, fixed and sharp, making me afraid to look him directly in the eye.

Several times, I stared blankly at the white gulls on the sea, fluttering and soaring, shattering wavelets one after another, and catching drops of water. Lost in thought, my gaze was drawn back by the delightful laughter behind me, and I watched that group of innocent children of the South Seas perform kissing gestures. But the corner of my eye felt an inexplicable threat, piercingly approaching, and I timidly glanced sideways, only to discover it was her two wooden yet sharp eyes, as if they were watching me.

Finally, I couldn't suppress my anger, and I angrily shouted at him:

"What are you looking at..." I looked him in the face, but at a glance, I found his eyes were kind, with a simple and wooden luster.

This embarrassed him, he went from astonishment to unease, looking around, but there was no one else. His embarrassment aroused my regret. I fled awkwardly from the stern, returning to the nauseating cabin.

After that, I never strolled over there, I didn't want to see him, until—

The next afternoon, the ship was filled with clamorous noise, and I finally ran there, squeezing in and craning my neck to look. I heard an old ticket inspector expounding his theory.

"No ticket, no ride. We can't be careless!"

"I have a ticket," he said haltingly in broken Cantonese.

"I have a ticket, I'm going to Xiamen to find my wife and son." Everyone else spoke a hundred sentences, but he only had this one sentence; until several heavy slaps landed on his cheeks, he still only had this one awkward sentence.

"Haha, Xiamen is long gone, left behind!" Everyone burst into laughter.

He was clearly a little confused, and let the ticket inspector search his pocket for the only four foreign coins he had to pay for the fare.

"I do have a ticket, I'm going to Xiamen to find my wife and son!"

At this moment, I vaguely saw several clumps of small birds in the horizon, predicting that the ship would dock at the Shanghai pier early tomorrow morning.

Beihai Park 154

— Li Ni

"In the eighth month, the barbarian sky flies snow," beyond the pass, it should be a season of wind and snow, covered roads, and ice everywhere. In the old capital, protected by the Western Hills like a screen, although it hasn't reached the severe cold of breathing and turning into ice, the chilling north wind and the sight of falling leaves flying all over the sky cannot help but evoke a bit of desolate and lonely power.

Wrapped in that old camel-hair robe, dragging my heavy steps, surrounded by dust, I entered the gate of Beihai Park alone.

Strolling, strolling, I climbed the White Pagoda. Looking up, the golden glazed tiles of the Forbidden City emitted a brilliant light in the setting sun, the towering ramparts of the Forbidden City were so somber and magnificent. Coal Hill, which once left a tragic page in Chinese history, was especially gray in the midst of swirling smoke. Then, expanding my vision; the towering greatness of Zhengyang Gate may make your emotions tense, and the blue roof of the Peking Library may evoke a bit of poetic and artistic feeling.

Facing the wind, letting the falling leaves hit my face, I forgot my homeland thousands of miles away. Sorrow, depression, and boredom were all blown away by the north wind.

After gazing for a while, seeing that the sun was about to hide behind the Western Hills, I hastily descended the pagoda and quietly slipped into Yilan Hall. The lotus flowers of Beihai had withered long ago, and the lake water couldn't withstand the blowing of the north wind last night, it was frozen.

Thinking back to the height of summer, how lively it must have been here! Women in cicada-wing-like clothes, arm in arm with gentlemen, strolling back and forth, how vibrant! At this time, you might find a few short-bearded Japanese people sitting under the green willows, fishing. Yilan Hall was even more indispensable for those petty bourgeoisie to put on a show of talent. Gathering in small groups, sitting around, sipping tea, and letting the cool breeze drive away the heat from their bodies, what a leisurely scene. But how long ago was it that the north wind drove away the gentlemen and ladies? Leaving this cold and desolate hall to be occupied by those sparrows, jumping freely and without restraint.

With a desolate heart, I strolled out of the long corridor, and my hand would involuntarily caress the jade stone railing again. This feeling was truly like reluctantly parting with a departing lover.

Leaving Yilan Hall, treading along the avenue lined with ancient cypress trees, even though it was winter, the needle-like cypress leaves were still so green and lovely. No wonder tourists from afar, upon reaching this place, couldn't help but praise them.

The darkness of night made my steps quicken. Walking to the Nine Dragon Wall, I stopped, panting, and carefully observed this ingenious creation. The lifelike dragons seemed about to soar into the clouds. Knowing that I was not an artist, I dared not arbitrarily criticize this precious wall, but it certainly made me never tire of looking at it.

The Five Dragon Pavilions became even more exquisite and lovely in the dim night. The golden yellow of the glazed tiles and the green of the cypress leaves, intricately mixed, with clear lines, were the best picture.

Night was gradually falling, and the chattering of the birds in the treetops and the mournful cries of the crows drove me out of the gate of Beihai Park like an eviction notice. Looking back, the Five Dragon Pavilions, leaning quietly by the water's edge, looked like a few fireflies lying there.

Aftersounds 160

Mr. Zhou Jiaoqing was hired by Zhonghua Book Company two years ago to broadcast basic English on the Yongsheng Radio Station, which was probably the earliest to teach English over the air in Shanghai. Recently, Yongsheng Radio Station has stopped broadcasting for many days due to license issues. The original educational programs of Mr. Zhou Jiaoqing's Shuangshi Culture Society, professional English, and correct pronunciation, etc., will be broadcast on the Li Shutang Radio Station starting this month, from 6:30 AM to 7:30 AM every day. Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, teaching professional English, "Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday, teaching English E sound, and every Sunday from 7:00 to 8:00 at the Zhongxi Radio Station teaching E sound. The textbook is 30 cents per volume, available at the Li Shutang Radio Station on Baike Road, the Zhongxi Radio Station on Fourth Avenue, and major bookstores. Mr. Ma Xingtao, greetings: Your manuscript is too long, and there is no space to publish it at the moment. However, the editor feels that it is necessary to say a few words about those untrue messages. Although Mr. Shen stated the "Recent Events in the Singing Stage" in the New Night News on the 28th. Adding "Aftersounds" is for the readers' request to publish a little more news and interesting things, but often for a trivial piece of news, (the editor thought it was irrelevant when sending the manuscript) it caused great disputes, so I declare again, I hope that the contributors, when "spreading rumors and creating trouble", first ask their own "conscience"; although there are indeed "facts", I want to "shirk responsibility" and cause trouble. Regarding Mr. Ma's statement this time, it is for the "buying a suit on Wusong Road" issue. If it is true, it is not a very indecent thing, otherwise it seems that the "rumormonger" has ulterior motives. I think they are waiting for your correction letter to laugh for a while. It is not necessary to waste precious time to answer those rumors that are obvious at a glance. What do you think, sir? Finally, I hope the contributors to Yuyin will forgive me for often not knowing what to do with the correction letter. "Yuyin" needs accurate news and harmless interesting things. (Editor)

Movie News

Thrilling Scenes in the Emerald Horse 161

Old Woman Gong Jianong plays a villain selling poison pills in "The Emerald Horse". When his poison mechanism was discovered by Wang Zhengxin and checked, he became very flustered, which seemed to be a warning to him, so if he wanted things to go smoothly, he had to punish Wang Tiemin.

One night, the moonlight was so dim, making it feel particularly quiet and terrifying. The old woman, carrying a pistol, secretly sneaked into Wang Weixin's residence. At this time, Old Wang was sitting under the lamp, studying the methods of solving the case. The old woman took advantage of his solitary meditation and shot a bullet at him from outside the window. But Wang Zhengxin's shrewdness was truly like a divine being, unpredictable. He tilted his head and dodged it. At the same time, he very shrewdly slammed the table lamp to the ground with a "bang", and the whole room was immediately dark. Although the old woman outside the window was shooting bullets like a string of pearls, because she lost her target, none of the shots were effective. Of course, at this time, the old woman panicked, and the situation was no small matter. While continuing to fire a few shots, she hurried away. By the time the great detective's men arrived fully armed, the old woman had escaped without a trace.

When "The Emerald Horse" was being screened at the central location, several Misses and little angels almost screamed when the scene was shown on the screen. Of course, the thrilling scenes in "The Emerald Horse" are not limited to just this one scene. This is just one example.

Honeymoon Blood Case 162

— Nanjing Ying

A Scene from "Night of the Wedding Candles" 163

Qin Tong Humiliates Wang Yin, Yuan Meiyun Cries

Yihua Company's new sound film, directed by Yue Feng, "Night of the Wedding Candles," filmed the following scene yesterday.

A rural house surrounded by green mountains and clear waters is where the famous writer Wang Xitao's writing career is located. On this day, Xitao was buried at his desk, engaged in writing a lengthy romance novel with marriage issues as the main theme, when suddenly his lover, Ye Caiyun, ran over to see him. Caiyun is a beautiful girl with an unspoiled innocence, and she lives not far from Xitao's house. Xitao quickly pushed the manuscript aside and stepped forward to greet Caiyun and sat her down on a chair. But at this time, Xitao suddenly found her eyes filled with tears, so he asked her in surprise what it was for? At first, Caiyun refused to tell the reason, but later, unable to resist Xitao's gentle persistence, she slowly complained, "Our affair has already been known to the Li family (Caiyun's fiancé's family). Just now, my father was called to scold them, and when he came back, my father vented his anger on me, even severely beating me and scolding me for being cheap and calling you a con artist and a bad guy. Later, he also said that if he found me with you again in the future, he would kill me." As Caiyun said this, she began to cry sadly. Looking at Wang Xitao, his teeth were clenched tightly, and he glared in one direction in grief and indignation.

Caiyun continued, "Now that my father has gone out, my mother, feeling sorry for me, secretly let me out and told me to ask if you have a solution?"

"In a few days, after I finish writing this novel, I'll take it to a bookstore in Shanghai to exchange it for money, and wouldn't that be enough to return the money to the Li family?" Xitao comforted her in this way.

But just when the two were talking very happily, Caiyun's father had tracked them down. Seeing the intimate situation of the two, he couldn't help but be furious, scolding Xitao for being a bad guy, a con artist, a vulgar thing, and a lecher, and angrily dragged Caiyun away. What about Xitao? He could only stand there blankly, watching her go.

Because of the director's efforts, the atmosphere was very tense. And Yuan Meiyun, who played Ye Caiyun, Wang Yin, who played Wang Xitao, and Qin Tong, who played Ye's father, were all skilled performers, so there was a special success in the performance, which goes without saying.

Shen Bao Architecture Weekly

Architecture and Garden Design for Suburban Middle-Class Families (Part 1) 165

— Written by Takuo Hoto, Translated by Guangzheng Zhang

The Suburban Life Urgently Needed by City Dwellers

The complexity of the city increases daily. People in noisy and bustling places rush about to pursue their goals, constantly striving with various tools of civilization. Vehicles stir up dust, and the smell of kerosene fills the streets; the smoke emitted by various factories covers the sky and the earth. Modern urban life is in such a state. In this kind of noisy sound, foul odor, and intense red glow, it is impossible to rest from the day's fatigue. From a health perspective, urban life is extremely bad. Conversely, the air is fresh, the lush green is captivating, the trees sprout tender yellow buds in spring and wear beautiful red leaves in autumn, and the scenery changes with the seasons; at the same time, one can listen to the delicate and melodious songs of birds in a gentle environment. Such suburban life is abundant.

If we do not only think about profit and desire but broaden our horizons to see the interesting natural beauty, then suburban life is a very meaningful thing. In short, for people who want to develop interests and improve their health, the suburbs are the best place to go. So, what are the characteristics of houses built in the suburbs, especially for middle-class families? Of course, just as ten people together have different appearances, everyone has different perspectives on houses. And people are accustomed to having dissatisfaction with their own things. Therefore, objectively examining the superior characteristics of suburban houses is a very interesting and painstaking task. Now, briefly speaking from the facts, there are approximately the following points.

Harmony Between the House and its Surroundings

1. Light: What distinguishes the suburbs from the city is the ability to fully capture light. Modern European architectural structures pay close attention to this point. Glass can be used that allows ultraviolet rays to pass through, so you can bathe in the grace of the sun. That is to say, the currently popular sunbathing can already be done indoors. In short, good lighting must be considered when building.

2. Scenery: The suburbs have suitable conditions for enjoying the scenery to your heart's content. In the city, except for special environments, it is almost impossible to see far. This characteristic can be said to be enjoyed only by those who have lived in the suburbs. Accordingly, skillfully considering the arrangement of the house's position can receive extremely beautiful scenery. The joy of seeing the graceful posture of high mountains through a small window is difficult to describe. Closer views, such as forests and fields, are also very nostalgic scenes. As such, the body and mind fatigued from urban life can get full rest.

3. Ventilation: Open on all sides, with plenty of space. In summer, if planned properly, cool breezes will often come leisurely, which can eliminate a lot of heat. In countries where south winds often blow in summer, ventilation from south to north can better enjoy the benefits of suburban life.

4. House Form: Living in the city, there are few opportunities to look around. But in the suburbs, because the fields are open, it is good to look near and far. In this kind of situation, the form of the house must be paid considerable attention. Especially for the distant view, the surrounding forests must be considered. At the same time, research must also be done on the harmony of color and the environment. Among the interlaced old trees, the shadow reflects a corner of the red wall; in the dense trees, the white wall appears faintly, which will give people a very beautiful feeling.

However, how can the kind of environment described above be created? What is the appropriate way to handle the surrounding garden? Indeed, the environment is not easy to create. First of all, when selecting land before starting construction, you should draw your ideal house in your mind, so that you can choose the appropriate place.

In the suburbs, there are many gentle slopes, winding streams, rocks, forests, and other natural gifts. If they can be used appropriately and cleverly, a house that people praise incessantly can be created. Generally, it is slightly higher, convenient for water, with good drainage, and sufficient sunlight. There must be lush forests above, and the view will naturally be suitable.

Using these naturally given materials to arrange the garden according to the terrain is the most appropriate thing to do. Accordingly, not only will daily life get great comfort, but visiting friends will also be very happy. This kind of facility cannot be done by human power alone.

Matters to Pay Attention to in the Design of People's Theaters 166

— Zhongchao Liu

Drama and film inherently have the mission of imparting knowledge and assisting education. Therefore, in culturally developed countries, there are countless theaters. In our country, except for a few major cities, the cities with theater facilities are as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. If there are any, they are just simple straw mats and wooden frames with simple equipment. The theaters in big cities are mostly magnificent and beautiful, and the huge construction costs and expensive ticket prices cannot be popularized among the public. Therefore, all parts of our country need the establishment of people's theaters.

The construction of people's theaters must pay attention to both drama and film. So that the invested funds will not be stagnant. The structure of the building must be strong, because inland theaters often collapse due to carelessness, resulting in tragedies. Therefore, it is best to use steel-reinforced concrete or T-shaped steel to make it durable and fire-resistant. Although the cost is high, it is also a safe solution for once and for all. The support of the theater's floor should not be done with large beams or very long cantilevers that cross the theater, as is often the case in Shanghai's grand theaters. This method is particularly dangerous. It should still be supported by pillars. Although the audience may have the regret of "eating the pillars," it only takes up a dozen seats. As for equipment and decoration, there is no need for air conditioning, hot water radiators, in-wall electric lights, spring chairs, patterned doorposts, carved ceilings, silk velvet curtains, carpets, etc. Just keep it simple and clean.

Too many seats will inevitably waste capital, and too few will hinder future development. It is best to have between 1,000 and 1,300, distributed on two levels, with the ratio of about three above and seven below. The distribution of one floor or three floors is not correct in terms of sight lines, so it cannot be used. The volume of the theater must be such that each seat has a space of one or two cubic feet. Ventilation equipment must use exhaust fans and indirect air vents. The number of windows must be reduced to avoid disturbing the sight lines. The number of doors must be one for every 120 people, with a minimum width of four feet. The position of the doors must be scattered on all sides and not concentrated in one place.

The seats downstairs must be arranged in an oval shape. The widest point should not exceed 35 seats, and each seat should be 15 inches wide. The number of rows should not exceed 30. The distance between each row should be at least two and a half feet. If the seats in the Rongguang Cinema are about 60 or 70 rows, the viewers at the very back seem to be too straining their eyes, which is not appropriate. It is best to have four aisles, each wide enough for two people to walk side by side. This road must be a few inches lower than the ground, so that the guests coming and going will not obstruct the sight of the audience. (This method has not been seen in Shanghai theaters.)

The structure of the floor must allow the sight lines of the rear rows downstairs to reach the top of the screen, and the rows upstairs to reach the edge of the stage, without being blocked by the heads of the people in the front rows. If the floor is too close to the stage, the slope will be steep, and the feet of the audience in the rear rows will often bump into the heads of the audience in the front rows, which is very annoying. If it is far from the stage, the rear rows of the floor seats will be too far from the stage, otherwise the floor seats must also be reduced. Therefore, the position of the floor and the two corridors must have an appropriate distance, height, and slope. This is closely related to the area and height of the theater. The projection room should not be too far or too high from the screen. It is best to protrude into the middle of the floor seats, so that the light is clearer and the angle with the screen is more accurate. The above are just superficial points, but they are also what should be paid attention to when designing a people's theater.

On the Crisis of Highly Developed Architecture 167

— Ouyang Gu

Chinese culture is one of the earliest in the world. Even in terms of architectural art alone, it has influenced foreigners. However, if someone talks about the history of Chinese architecture, it is pitiful to shake their head and say: nothing. Until recently, not only have I not seen a single special book, but even the term "Chinese architectural history" seems impossible to establish. Countries like Japan and Korea have directly or indirectly received Chinese architecture in the past, so their temples and houses have an oriental color. After the Middle Ages, foreign forces and influences transformed all the inherent art in architecture, overturning all the original old buildings. At the same time, the capitals also felt the increase in population and the development of commerce. In the fixed and limited land, there was a shortage of application. Therefore, the potential for upward development has become a necessity.

Although high-rise development is indeed the best way to solve the problem of densely populated cities, the so-called "occupying the sky but not the land" does not hinder anything. But the facts are not so. We can understand by looking at the survey below:

Last year, the New York Health Bureau investigated 1,062 offices in commercial areas, with a total of 5,833 office workers. Among them, 79% of the offices were located in extremely high buildings. The indoor air and light were poor, and lights had to be turned on even during the day, resulting in reduced physiological functions, pale complexion, weak eyesight, and weight loss. It can be seen that the impact on health is extremely great.

For this reason, the United Kingdom and the United States have clear regulations to divide regions and absolutely restrict the upward development of houses. Some use the width of the road as the standard. Japan has geological reasons, so tall buildings are rare, fearing that earthquakes would cause even greater harm. The tall buildings of apartments and banks in the Shanghai Public Concession and the French Concession must occupy at least a quarter of the land, and the light shining on the opposite roof must also form an angle of 56 degrees to avoid affecting the neighboring houses. In addition, Chicago, the city with the highest building restrictions in the world, is above 260 feet, but it must not exceed two and a half times the width of the road in front. Ordinary residential buildings, especially the Shikumen alleys in the Public Concession of this city, are not even allowed to build three floors. It can be seen that the defense is precise, so the reduction of all kinds of dangers is naturally expected. If high-rise buildings are used instead, elevators must be used up and down. If there is a fire, the danger will be even more unspeakable.
